<body epub:type="bodymatter z3998:fiction">
<section id="book-1" epub:type="part">
<section id="hymn-1-1." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">1.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Adam.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Gen. iii.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-1-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>On man, in his own image made,</span>
      <span class="i1">How much did God bestow!</span>
    <span>The whole creation homage paid,</span>
      <span class="i1">And own'd him lord below.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-1-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>He dwelt in Eden's garden, stored</span>
      <span class="i1">With sweets for every sense;</span>
    <span>And there, with his descending Lord,</span>
      <span class="i1">He walk'd in confidence.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-1-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But, oh by sin how quickly changed—</span>
      <span class="i1">His honour forfeited—</span>
    <span>His heart from God and truth estranged—</span>
      <span class="i1">His conscience fill'd with dread!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-1-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Now from his Maker's voice he flees,</span>
      <span class="i1">Which was before his joy,</span>
    <span>And thinks to hide amidst the trees</span>
      <span class="i1">From an all-seeing eye.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-1-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Compell'd to answer to his name,</span>
      <span class="i1">With stubbornness and pride,</span>
    <span>He cast on God himself the blame,</span>
      <span class="i1">Nor once for mercy cried.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-1-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But grace, unask'd, his heart subdued,</span>
      <span class="i1">And all his guilt forgave;</span>
    <span>By faith the promised Seed he view'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">And felt His power to save.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-1-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus we ourselves would justify,</span>
      <span class="i1">Though we the law transgress,—</span>
    <span>Like him, unable to deny,</span>
      <span class="i1">Unwilling to confess.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-1-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But when by faith the sinner sees</span>
      <span class="i1">A pardon bought with blood,</span>
    <span>Then he forsakes his foolish pleas</span>
      <span class="i1">And gladly turns to God.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-2." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">2.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Cain and Abel.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Gen. iv, 3-8.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-2-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When Adam fell he quickly lost</span>
    <span>God's image, which he once possess'd:</span>
    <span>See all our nature since could boast,</span>
    <span>In Cain, his first-born son, express'd!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-2-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The sacrifice the Lord ordain'd</span>
    <span>In type of the Redeemer's blood</span>
    <span>Self-righteous reasoning Cain disdain'd,</span>
    <span>And thought his own first-fruits as good.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-2-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Yet rage and envy fill'd his mind</span>
    <span>When, with a sullen downcast look,</span>
    <span>He saw his brother favour find,</span>
    <span>Who God's appointed method took.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-2-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>By Cain's own hand good Abel died,</span>
    <span>Because the Lord approved his faith;</span>
    <span>And, when his blood for vengeance cried,</span>
    <span>He vainly thought to hide his death.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-2-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Such was the wicked murderer Cain,</span>
    <span>And such by nature still are we—</span>
    <span>Untill by grace we're born again,</span>
    <span>Malicious, blind, and proud as he.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-2-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Like him the way of grace we slight,</span>
    <span>And in our own devices trust;</span>
    <span>Call evil good, and darkness light,</span>
    <span>And hate and persecute the just.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-2-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The saints in every age and place</span>
    <span>Have found his history fulfill'd:</span>
    <span>The numbers all our thoughts surpass</span>
    <span>Of Abels whom the Cains have kill'd!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-2-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus Jesus fell; but, oh! his blood</span>
    <span>Far better things than Abel's cries,—</span>
    <span>Obtains his murderers' peace with God,</span>
    <span>And gains them mansions in the skies.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-3" epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">3</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Walking with God.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Gen. v, 24.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-3-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Oh for a closer walk with God,</span>
      <span class="i1">A calm and heavenly frame,</span>
    <span>A light to shine upon the road</span>
      <span class="i1">That leads me to the Lamb!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-3-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Where is the blessedness I knew</span>
      <span class="i1">When first I saw the Lord?</span>
    <span>Where is the soul-refreshing view</span>
      <span class="i1">Of Jesus and his word?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-3-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>What peaceful hours I once enjoy'd!</span>
      <span class="i1">How sweet their mem'ry still!</span>
    <span>But they have left an aching void</span>
      <span class="i1">The world can never fill.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-3-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Return, O holy Dove! return,</span>
      <span class="i1">Sweet messenger of rest;</span>
    <span>I hate the sins that made thee mourn,</span>
      <span class="i1">And drove thee from my breast.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-3-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The dearest idol I have known,</span>
      <span class="i1">Whate'er that idol be,</span>
    <span>Help me to tear it from thy throne,</span>
      <span class="i1">And worship only thee.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-3-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>So shall my walk be close with God,</span>
      <span class="i1">Calm and serene my frame;</span>
    <span>So purer light shall mark the road</span>
      <span class="i1">That leads me to the Lamb.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-4" epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">4</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Another.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead"></p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-4-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>By faith in Christ I walk with God,</span>
    <span>With heaven, my journey's end, in view;</span>
    <span>Supported by his staff and rod,</span>
    <span>My road is safe and pleasant too.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-4-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>I travel through a desert wide,</span>
    <span>Where many round me blindly stray:</span>
    <span>But he vouchsafes to be my guide,</span>
    <span>And will not let me miss my way.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-4-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Though snares and dangers throng my path.</span>
    <span>And earth and hell my course withstand,</span>
    <span>I triumph over all by faith,</span>
    <span>Guarded by his almighty hand.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-4-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The wilderness affords no food,</span>
    <span>But God for my support prepares,—</span>
    <span>Provides me every needful good,</span>
    <span>And frees my soul from wants and cares.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-4-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>With him sweet converse I maintain;</span>
    <span>Great as he is, I dare be free;</span>
    <span>I tell him all my grief and pain,</span>
    <span>And he reveals his love to me.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-4-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Some cordial from his word he brings</span>
    <span>Whene'er my feeble spirit faints,—</span>
    <span>At once my soul revives and sings,</span>
    <span>And yields no more to sad complaints.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-4-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>I pity all that worldlings talk</span>
    <span>Of pleasures that will quickly end:</span>
    <span>Be this my choice, O Lord, to walk</span>
    <span>With thee, my Guide, my Guard, my Friend.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-5" epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">5</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Lot in Sodom.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Gen. xiii, 10.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-5-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>How hurtful was the choice of Lot,</span>
      <span class="i1">Who took up his abode</span>
    <span>(Because it was a fruitful spot)</span>
      <span class="i1">With them who fear'd not God!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-5-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>A pris'ner he was quickly made,</span>
      <span class="i1">Bereaved of all his store;</span>
    <span>And but for Abra'm's timely aid</span>
      <span class="i1">He had return'd no more.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-5-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Yet still he seem'd resolved to stay,</span>
      <span class="i1">As if it were his rest,</span>
    <span>Although their sins from day to day</span>
      <span class="i1">His righteous soul distress'd.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-5-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Awhile he stay'd, with anxious mind,</span>
      <span class="i1">Exposed to scorn and strife;</span>
    <span>At last he left his all behind,</span>
      <span class="i1">And fled to save his life.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-5-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>In vain his sons-in-law he warn'd;</span>
      <span class="i1">They thought he told his dreams;</span>
    <span>His daughters too of them had learn'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">And perish'd in the flames.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-5-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>His wife escaped a little way,</span>
      <span class="i1">But died for looking back:</span>
    <span>Does not her case to pilgrims say,</span>
      <span class="i1">"Beware of growing slack"?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-5-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Yea, Lot himself could ling'ring stand</span>
      <span class="i1">Though vengeance was in view;</span>
    <span>'Twas Mercy pluck'd him by the hand</span>
      <span class="i1">Or he had perish'd too.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-5-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The doom of Sodom will be ours</span>
      <span class="i1">If to the earth we cleave:</span>
    <span>Lord, quicken all our drowsy powers</span>
      <span class="i1">To flee to thee and live.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-6." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">6.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Jehovah-Jireh—The Lord will Provide.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Gen. xxii, 14.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-6-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The saints should never be dismay'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">Nor sink in hopeless fear;</span>
    <span>For, when they least expect his aid,</span>
      <span class="i1">The Saviour will appear.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-6-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>This Abra'm found: he raised the knife,</span>
      <span class="i1">God saw, and said, "Forbear!</span>
    <span>Yon ram shall yield his meaner life—</span>
      <span class="i1">Behold the victim there."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-6-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Once David seem'd Saul's certain prey;</span>
      <span class="i1">But hark! the foe's at hand;</span>
    <span>Saul turns his arms another way,</span>
      <span class="i1">To save th' invaded land.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-6-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When Jonah sunk beneath the wave</span>
      <span class="i1">He thought to rise no more;</span>
    <span>But God prepared a fish to save</span>
      <span class="i1">And bear him to the shore.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-6-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Bless'd proofs of power and grace divine</span>
      <span class="i1">That meet us in his word!</span>
    <span>May every deep-felt care of mine</span>
      <span class="i1">Be trusted with the Lord!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-6-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Wait for his seasonable aid,</span>
      <span class="i1">And though it tarry, wait:</span>
    <span>The promise may be long delay'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">But cannot come too late.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-7." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">7.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Lord will Provide.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead"></p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-7-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Though troubles assail,</span>
    <span>And dangers affright,</span>
    <span>Though friends should all fail,</span>
    <span>And foes all unite;</span>
    <span>Yet one thing secures us,</span>
    <span>Whatever betide,</span>
    <span>The Scripture assures us</span>
    <span>The Lord will provide.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-7-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The birds without barn</span>
    <span>Or storehouse are fed;</span>
    <span>From them let us learn</span>
    <span>To trust for our bread:</span>
    <span>His saints what is fitting</span>
    <span>Shall ne'er be denied,</span>
    <span>So long as 'tis written,</span>
    <span>The Lord Will provide.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-7-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>We may, like the ships,</span>
    <span>By tempests be tost</span>
    <span>On perilous deeps,</span>
    <span>But cannot be lost:</span>
    <span>Though Satan enrages</span>
    <span>The wind and the tide,</span>
    <span>The promise engages</span>
    <span>The Lord will provide.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-7-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>His call we obey,</span>
    <span>Like Abr'am of old,</span>
    <span>Not knowing our way,</span>
    <span>But faith makes us bold:</span>
    <span>For though we are strangers,</span>
    <span>We have a good guide,</span>
    <span>And trust, in all dangers,</span>
    <span>The Lord will provide.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-7-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When Satan appears,</span>
    <span>To stop up our path</span>
    <span>And fill us with fears,</span>
    <span>We triumph by faith;</span>
    <span>He cannot take from us,</span>
    <span>Though oft he has tried,</span>
    <span>This heart-cheering promise,</span>
    <span>The Lord will provide.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-7-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>He tells us we're weak,</span>
    <span>Our hope is in vain,</span>
    <span>The good that we seek</span>
    <span>We ne'er shall obtain;</span>
    <span>But when such suggestions</span>
    <span>Our spirits have plied,</span>
    <span>This answers all questions,</span>
    <span>The Lord will provide.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-7-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>No strength of our own</span>
    <span>Or goodness we claim;</span>
    <span>Yet since we have known</span>
    <span>The Saviour's great name,</span>
    <span>In this our strong tower</span>
    <span>For safety we hide,</span>
    <span>The Lord is our power,</span>
    <span>The Lord will provide.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-7-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When life sinks apace,</span>
    <span>And death is in view,</span>
    <span>This word of his grace</span>
    <span>Shall comfort us through:</span>
    <span>No fearing or doubting</span>
    <span>With Christ on our side,—</span>
    <span>We hope to die shouting,</span>
    <span>The Lord will provide.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-8." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">8.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Esau.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Gen. xxv; Heb. xii, 16.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-8-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Poor Esau repented too late</span>
    <span>That once he his birthright despised,</span>
    <span>And sold, for a morsel of meat,</span>
    <span>What could not too highly be prized:</span>
    <span>How great was his anguish when told,</span>
    <span>The blessing he sought to obtain</span>
    <span>Was gone with the birthright he sold,</span>
    <span>And none could recall it again!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-8-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>He stands as a warning to all</span>
    <span>Wherever the gospel shall come;</span>
    <span>O hasten and yield to the call</span>
    <span>While yet for repentance there's room!</span>
    <span>Your season will quickly be past;</span>
    <span>Then hear and obey it to-day,</span>
    <span>Lest, when you seek mercy at last,</span>
    <span>The Saviour should frown you away.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-8-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>What is it the world can propose?</span>
    <span>A morsel of meat at the best!</span>
    <span>For this are you willing to lose</span>
    <span>A share in the joys of the bless'd?</span>
    <span>Its pleasures will speedily end,</span>
    <span>Its favour and praise are but breath;</span>
    <span>And what can its profits befriend</span>
    <span>Your soul in the moments of death?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-8-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>If Jesus for these you despise,</span>
    <span>And sin to the Saviour prefer,</span>
    <span>In vain your entreaties and cries</span>
    <span>When summon'd to stand at his bar:</span>
    <span>How will you his presence abide?</span>
    <span>What anguish will torture your heart!</span>
    <span>The saints all enthroned by his side,</span>
    <span>And you be compell'd to depart.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-8-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Too often, dear Saviour, have I</span>
    <span>Preferr'd some poor trifle to thee;</span>
    <span>How is it thou dost not deny</span>
    <span>The blessing and birthright to me?</span>
    <span>No better than Esau I am,</span>
    <span>Though pardon and heaven be mine;</span>
    <span>To me belongs nothing but shame—</span>
    <span>The praise and the glory be thine.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-9." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">9.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Jacob’s Ladder.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Gen. xxviii, 12.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-9-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>If the Lord our leader be,</span>
    <span>We may follow without fear;</span>
    <span>East or west, by land or sea,</span>
    <span>Home with him is every where.</span>
    <span>When from Esau Jacob fled,</span>
    <span>Though his pillow was a stone,</span>
    <span>And the ground his humble bed,</span>
    <span>Yet he was not left alone.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-9-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Kings are often waking kept,</span>
    <span>Rack'd with cares on beds of state:</span>
    <span>Never king like Jacob slept,</span>
    <span>For he lay at heaven's gate.</span>
    <span>Lo! he saw a ladder rear'd,</span>
    <span>Reaching to the heavenly throne;</span>
    <span>At the top the Lord appeared,</span>
    <span>Spake, and claim'd him for his own:—</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-9-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Fear not, Jacob, thou art mine,</span>
    <span>And my presence with thee goes;</span>
    <span>On thy heart my love shall shine,</span>
    <span>And my arm subdue thy foes:</span>
    <span>From my promise comfort take,</span>
    <span>For my help in trouble call;</span>
    <span>Never will I thee forsake</span>
    <span>Till I have accomplish'd all."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-9-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Well does Jacob's ladder suit</span>
    <span>To the gospel throne of grace;</span>
    <span>We are at the ladder's foot,</span>
    <span>Every hour, in every place.</span>
    <span>By assuming flesh and blood,</span>
    <span>Jesus heaven and earth unites;</span>
    <span>We by faith ascend to God,</span>
    <span>God to dwell with us delights.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-9-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>They who know the Saviour's name</span>
    <span>Are for all events prepared;</span>
    <span>What can changes do to them,</span>
    <span>Who have such a guide and guard?</span>
    <span>Should they traverse earth around,</span>
    <span>To the ladder still they come:</span>
    <span>Every spot is holy ground,—</span>
    <span>God is there, and he's their home.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-10." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">10.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">My Name is Jacob.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Gen. xxxii, 27.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-10-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Nay, I cannot let thee go</span>
    <span>Till a blessing thou bestow:</span>
    <span>Do not turn away thy face,</span>
    <span>Mine's an urgent, pressing case.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-10-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Dost thou ask me who I am?</span>
    <span>Ah, my Lord, thou know'st my name!</span>
    <span>Yet the question gives a plea</span>
    <span>To support my suit with thee.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-10-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thou didst once a wretch behold,</span>
    <span>In rebellion blindly bold,</span>
    <span>Scorn thy grace, thy power defy,</span>
    <span>That poor rebel, Lord, was I.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-10-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Once a sinner near despair</span>
    <span>Sought thy mercy-seat by prayer;</span>
    <span>Mercy heard and set him free—</span>
    <span>Lord, that mercy came to me.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-10-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Many years have pass'd since then,</span>
    <span>Many changes I have seen,</span>
    <span>Yet have been upheld till now;</span>
    <span>Who could hold me up but thou?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-10-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thou hast help'd in every need,</span>
    <span>This emboldens me to plead;</span>
    <span>After so much mercy past,</span>
    <span>Canst thou let me sink at last?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-10-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>No—I must maintain my hold;</span>
    <span>'Tis thy goodness makes me bold;</span>
    <span>I can no denial take,</span>
    <span>When I plead for Jesu's sake.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-11." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">11.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Plenty in the Time of Dearth.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Gen. xli, 56.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-11-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>My soul once had its plenteous years,</span>
    <span>And throve, with peace and comfort fill'd,</span>
    <span>Like the fat kine and ripen'd ears</span>
    <span>Which Pharaoh in his dream beheld.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-11-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>With pleasing frames and grace received,</span>
    <span>With means and ordinances fed,</span>
    <span>How happy for a while I lived,</span>
    <span>And little fear'd the want of bread!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-11-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But famine came, and left no sign</span>
    <span>Of all the plenty I had seen;</span>
    <span>Like the dry ears and half-starved kine,</span>
    <span>I then look'd wither'd, faint, and lean.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-11-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>To Joseph the Egyptians went;</span>
    <span>To Jesus I made known my case:</span>
    <span>He, when my little stock was spent,</span>
    <span>Open'd his magazine of grace.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-11-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>For he the time of dearth foresaw,</span>
    <span>And made provision long before;</span>
    <span>That famish'd souls, like me, might draw</span>
    <span>Supplies from his unbounded store.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-11-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Now on his bounty I depend,</span>
    <span>And live from fear of dearth secure:</span>
    <span>Maintain'd by such a mighty friend,</span>
    <span>I cannot want till he is poor.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-11-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>O sinners, hear his gracious call!</span>
    <span>His mercy's door stands open wide;</span>
    <span>He has enough to feed you all,</span>
    <span>And none who come shall be denied.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-12." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">12.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Joseph made known to his Brethren.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Gen. xlv, 3, 4.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-12-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When Joseph his brethren beheld</span>
    <span>Afflicted and trembling with fear,</span>
    <span>His heart with compassion was fill'd;</span>
    <span>From weeping he could not forbear.</span>
    <span>Awhile his behaviour was rough,</span>
    <span>To bring their past sins to their mind;</span>
    <span>But when they were humbled enough,</span>
    <span>He hasted to show himself kind.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-12-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>How little they thought it was he</span>
    <span>Whom they had ill-treated and sold!</span>
    <span>How great their confusion must be,</span>
    <span>As soon as his name he had told!</span>
    <span>"I am Joseph, your brother," he said,</span>
    <span>"And still to my heart you are dear;</span>
    <span>You sold me, and thought I was dead,</span>
    <span>But God for your sakes sent me here."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-12-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Though greatly distressed before,</span>
    <span>When charged with purloining the cup,</span>
    <span>They now were confounded much more,—</span>
    <span>Not one of them dared to look up.</span>
    <span>"Can Joseph, whom we would have slain.</span>
    <span>Forgive us the evil we did?</span>
    <span>And will he our households maintain?</span>
    <span>O this is a brother indeed!"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-12-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus dragg'd by my conscience I came,</span>
    <span>And laden with guilt, to the Lord,</span>
    <span>Surrounded with terror and shame,</span>
    <span>Unable to utter a word.</span>
    <span>At first he look'd stern and severe,</span>
    <span>What anguish then pierced my heart!</span>
    <span>Expecting each moment to hear</span>
    <span>The sentence, "Thou cursed, depart!"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-12-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But, O what surprise when he spoke,</span>
    <span>While tenderness beam'd in his face!</span>
    <span>My heart then to pieces was broke,</span>
    <span>O'erwhelm'd and confounded by grace:</span>
    <span>"Poor sinner, I know thee full well,</span>
    <span>By thee I was sold and was slain;</span>
    <span>But I died to redeem thee from hell,</span>
    <span>And raise thee in glory to reign.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-12-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"I am Jesus, whom thou hast blasphemed,</span>
    <span>And crucified often afresh;</span>
    <span>But let me henceforth be esteemed</span>
    <span>Thy brother, thy bone, and thy flesh:</span>
    <span>My pardon I freely bestow,</span>
    <span>Thy wants I will fully supply;</span>
    <span>I'll guide thee and guard thee below,</span>
    <span>And soon will remove thee on high.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-12-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Go, publish to sinners around,</span>
    <span>That they may be willing to come,</span>
    <span>The mercy which now you have found,</span>
    <span>And tell them that yet there is room."</span>
    <span>O sinners, the message obey!</span>
    <span>No more vain excuses pretend;</span>
    <span>But come without further delay,</span>
    <span>To Jesus, our brother and friend.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-13." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">13.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Bitter Waters.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Exod. xv, 23-25.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-13-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Bitter indeed the waters are</span>
      <span class="i1">Which in this desert flow;</span>
    <span>Though to the eye they promise fair,</span>
      <span class="i1">They taste of sin and woe.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-13-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Of pleasing draughts I once could dream;</span>
      <span class="i1">But now, awake, I find</span>
    <span>That sin has poison'd every stream,</span>
      <span class="i1">And left a curse behind.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-13-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But there's a wonder-working wood,</span>
      <span class="i1">I've heard believers say,</span>
    <span>Can make these bitter waters good,</span>
      <span class="i1">And take the curse away.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-13-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The virtues of this healing tree</span>
      <span class="i1">Are known and prized by few:</span>
    <span>Reveal the secret, Lord, to me,</span>
      <span class="i1">That I may prize it too.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-13-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The cross on which the Saviour died</span>
      <span class="i1">And conquer'd for his saints,</span>
    <span>This is the tree by faith applied,</span>
      <span class="i1">Which sweetens all complaints.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-13-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thousands have found the bless'd effect,</span>
      <span class="i1">Nor longer mourn their lot;</span>
    <span>While on his sorrows they reflect,</span>
      <span class="i1">Their own are all forgot.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-13-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When they, by faith, behold the cross,</span>
      <span class="i1">Though many griefs they meet,</span>
    <span>They draw a gain from every loss,</span>
      <span class="i1">And find the bitter sweet.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-14." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">14.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Jehovah-Rophi—I am the Lord that healeth thee.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Exod. xv.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-14-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Heal us, Emmanuel; here we are,</span>
      <span class="i1">Waiting to feel thy touch:</span>
    <span>Deep-wounded souls to thee repair,</span>
      <span class="i1">And, Saviour, we are such.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-14-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Our faith is feeble, we confess,—</span>
      <span class="i1">We faintly trust thy word;</span>
    <span>But wilt thou pity us the less?</span>
      <span class="i1">Be that far from thee, Lord!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-14-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Remember him who once applied</span>
      <span class="i1">With trembling for relief;</span>
    <span>"Lord, I believe," with tears he cried,</span>
      <span class="i1">"0 help my unbelief!"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-14-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>She too who touch d thee in the press,</span>
      <span class="i1">And healing virtue stole,</span>
    <span>Was answer'd, "Daughter, go in peace:</span>
      <span class="i1">Thy faith hath made thee whole."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-14-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Conceal'd amid the gathering throng,</span>
      <span class="i1">She would have shunn'd thy view,</span>
    <span>And if her faith was firm and strong—</span>
      <span class="i1">Had strong misgivings too.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-14-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Like her, with hopes and fears we come,</span>
      <span class="i1">To touch thee if we may;</span>
    <span>Oh! send us not despairing home,</span>
      <span class="i1">Send none unheal'd away.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-15." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">15.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Manna.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Exod. xvi, 18.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-15-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Manna to Israel well supplied</span>
      <span class="i1">The want of other bread;</span>
    <span>While God is able to provide,</span>
      <span class="i1">His people shall be fed.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-15-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>(Thus though the corn and wine should fail,</span>
      <span class="i1">And creature-streams be dry,</span>
    <span>The prayer of faith will still prevail</span>
      <span class="i1">For blessings from on high.)</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-15-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Of his kind care how sweet a proof;</span>
      <span class="i1">It suited every taste:</span>
    <span>Who gather'd most had just enough—</span>
      <span class="i1">Enough who gather'd least.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-15-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>'Tis thus our gracious Lord provides</span>
      <span class="i1">Our comforts and our cares;</span>
    <span>His own unerring hand divides,</span>
      <span class="i1">And gives us each our shares.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-15-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>He knows how much the weak can bear,</span>
      <span class="i1">And helps them when they cry;</span>
    <span>The strongest have no strength to spare,</span>
      <span class="i1">For such he'll strongly try.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-15-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Daily they saw the manna come</span>
      <span class="i1">And cover all the ground;</span>
    <span>But what they tried to keep at home</span>
      <span class="i1">Corrupted soon was found.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-15-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Vain their attempt to store it up,</span>
      <span class="i1">This was to tempt the Lord:</span>
    <span>Israel must live by faith and hope,</span>
      <span class="i1">And not upon a hoard.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-16." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">16.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Manna hoarded.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Exod. xvi, 20.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-16-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The manna, favour'd Israel's meat,</span>
      <span class="i1">Was gather'd day by day;</span>
    <span>When all the host was served, the heat</span>
      <span class="i1">Melted the rest away.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-16-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>In vain to hoard it up they tried</span>
      <span class="i1">Against to-morrow came;</span>
    <span>It then bred worms and putrified,</span>
      <span class="i1">And proved their sin and shame.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-16-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>'Twas daily bread, and would not keep,</span>
      <span class="i1">But must be still renewed;</span>
    <span>Faith should not want a hoard or heap,</span>
      <span class="i1">But trust the Lord for food.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-16-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The truths by which the soul is fed</span>
      <span class="i1">Must thus be had afresh;</span>
    <span>For notions resting in the head</span>
      <span class="i1">Will only feed the flesh:</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-16-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>However true, they have no life</span>
      <span class="i1">Or unction to impart;</span>
    <span>They breed the worms of pride and strife,</span>
      <span class="i1">But cannot cheer the heart.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-16-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Nor can the best experience past</span>
      <span class="i1">The life of faith maintain;</span>
    <span>The brightest hope will faint at last</span>
      <span class="i1">Unless supplied again.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-16-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Dear Lord, while we in prayer are found,</span>
      <span class="i1">Do thou the manna give;</span>
    <span>Oh let it fall on all around,</span>
      <span class="i1">That we may eat and live!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-17." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">17.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Jehovah-Nissi—The Lord my Banner.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Exod. xvii, 15.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-17-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">By whom was David taught</span>
      <span class="i1">To aim the dreadful blow,</span>
      <span class="i1">When he Goliath fought,</span>
      <span class="i1">And laid the Gittite low?</span>
    <span>No sword nor spear the stripling took,</span>
    <span>But chose a peeble from the brook.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-17-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">'Twas Israel's God and King</span>
      <span class="i1">Who sent him to the fight,—</span>
      <span class="i1">Who gave him strength to sling,</span>
      <span class="i1">And skill to aim aright.</span>
    <span>Ye feeble saints, your strength endures,</span>
    <span>Because young David's God is yours.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-17-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Who order'd Gideon forth</span>
      <span class="i1">To storm th' invader's camp,</span>
      <span class="i1">With arms of little worth—</span>
      <span class="i1">A pitcher and a lamp?</span>
    <span>The trumpets made his coming known,</span>
    <span>And all the host was overthrown.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-17-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Oh! I have seen the day</span>
      <span class="i1">When, with a single word,</span>
      <span class="i1">God helping me to say,</span>
      <span class="i1">My trust is in the Lord,</span>
    <span>My soul has quell'd a thousand foes,</span>
    <span>Fearless of all that could oppose.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-17-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">But unbelief, self-will,</span>
      <span class="i1">Self-righteousness, and pride,</span>
      <span class="i1">How often do they steal</span>
      <span class="i1">My weapon from my side!</span>
    <span>Yet David's Lord and Gideon's friend</span>
    <span>Will help his servant to the end.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-18." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">18.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Golden Calf.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Exod. xxxii, 4, 31.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-18-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When Israel heard the fiery law</span>
      <span class="i1">From Sinai's top proclaim'd,</span>
    <span>Their hearts seem'd full of holy awe,</span>
      <span class="i1">Their stubborn spirits tamed:</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-18-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Yet, as forgetting all they knew,</span>
      <span class="i1">Ere forty days were past,</span>
    <span>With blazing Sinai still in view,</span>
      <span class="i1">A molten calf they cast.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-18-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Yea, Aaron, God's anointed priest.</span>
      <span class="i1">Who on the mount had been,</span>
    <span>He durst prepare the idol-beast,</span>
      <span class="i1">And lead them on to sin!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-18-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Lord, what is man, and what are we,</span>
      <span class="i1">To recompense thee thus?</span>
    <span>In their offence our own we see—</span>
      <span class="i1">Their story points at us.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-18-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>From Mount Sinai we heard thee speak.</span>
      <span class="i1">And from Mount Calv'ry too;</span>
    <span>And yet to idols oft we seek,</span>
      <span class="i1">While thou art in our view.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-18-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Some golden calf, or golden dream,</span>
      <span class="i1">Some fancied creature-good,</span>
    <span>Presumes to share the heart with Him</span>
      <span class="i1">Who bought the whole with blood.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-18-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Lord, save us from our golden calves,</span>
      <span class="i1">Our sin with grief we own;</span>
    <span>We would no more be thine by halves,</span>
      <span class="i1">But live to thee alone.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-19." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">19.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The True Aaron.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Levit. viii, 7-9.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-19-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>See Aaron, God's anointed priest,</span>
      <span class="i1">Within the veil appear,</span>
    <span>In robes of mystic meaning dress'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">Presenting Isr'el's pray'r.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-19-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The plate of gold which crowns his brows</span>
      <span class="i1">His holiness describes;</span>
    <span>His breast displays, in shining rows,</span>
      <span class="i1">The names of all the tribes.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-19-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>With the atoning blood he stands</span>
      <span class="i1">Before the mercy-seat;</span>
    <span>And clouds of incense from his hands</span>
      <span class="i1">Arise with odour sweet.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-19-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Urim and Thummim near his heart,</span>
      <span class="i1">In rich engravings worn,</span>
    <span>The sacred light of truth impart,</span>
      <span class="i1">To teach and to adorn.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-19-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Through him the eye of faith descries</span>
      <span class="i1">A greater Priest than he:—</span>
    <span>Thus Jesus pleads above the skies</span>
      <span class="i1">For you, my friends, and me.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-19-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>He bears the names of all his saints</span>
      <span class="i1">Deep on his heart engraved,</span>
    <span>Attentive to the state and wants</span>
      <span class="i1">Of all his love has saved.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-19-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>In him a holiness complete—</span>
      <span class="i1">Light and perfections shine,</span>
    <span>And wisdom, grace, and glory meet;—</span>
      <span class="i1">A Saviour all divine.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-19-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The blood which as a Priest he bears</span>
      <span class="i1">For sinners is his own;</span>
    <span>The incense of his prayers and tears</span>
      <span class="i1">Perfumes the holy throne.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-19-9>
 	<header>
 		<p>IX</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>In him my weary soul has rest,</span>
      <span class="i1">Though I am weak and vile;</span>
    <span>I read my name upon his breast,</span>
      <span class="i1">And see the Father smile.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-20." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">20.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Balaam’s Wish.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Numb. xxiii, 10.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-20-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">How bless'd the righteous are</span>
      <span class="i1">When they resign their breath!</span>
    <span>No wonder Balaam wish'd to share</span>
      <span class="i1">In such a happy death.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-20-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">"Oh! let me die," said he,</span>
      <span class="i1">"The death the righteous do,—</span>
    <span>When life is ended, let me be</span>
      <span class="i1">Found with the faithful few."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-20-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">The force of truth, how great!</span>
      <span class="i1">When enemies confess,</span>
    <span>None but the righteous, whom they hate,</span>
      <span class="i1">A solid hope possess.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-20-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">But Balaam's wish was vain,</span>
      <span class="i1">His heart was insincere;</span>
    <span>He thirsted for unrighteous gain.</span>
      <span class="i1">And sought a portion here.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-20-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">He seem'd the Lord to know,</span>
      <span class="i1">And to offend him loath;</span>
    <span>But Mammon proved his overthrow,</span>
      <span class="i1">For none can serve them both.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-20-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">May you, my friends, and I,</span>
      <span class="i1">Warning from hence receive,</span>
    <span>If like the righteous we would die,</span>
      <span class="i1">To choose the life they live.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-21." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">21.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Gibeon.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Joshua, x, 6.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-21-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When Joshua, by God's command,</span>
    <span>Invaded Canaan's guilty land,</span>
    <span>Gibeon, unlike the nations round,</span>
    <span>Submission made, and mercy found.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-21-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Their stubborn neighbours who, enraged,</span>
    <span>United war against them waged,</span>
    <span>By Joshua soon were overthrown,</span>
    <span>For Gibeon's cause was now his own.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-21-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>He from whose arm they ruin fear'd</span>
    <span>Their leader and ally appear'd;</span>
    <span>An emblem of the Saviour's grace</span>
    <span>To those who humbly seek his face.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-21-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The men of Gibeon wore disguise,</span>
    <span>And gain'd their peace by framing lies;</span>
    <span>For Joshua had no power to spare,</span>
    <span>If he had known from whence they were.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-21-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But Jesus invitations sends,</span>
    <span>Treating with rebels as his friends;</span>
    <span>And holds the promise forth in view</span>
    <span>To all who for his mercy sue.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-21-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Too long his goodness I disdain'd,</span>
    <span>Yet went at last and peace obtain'd;</span>
    <span>But soon the noise of war I heard,</span>
    <span>And former friends in arms appear'd.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-21-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Weak in myself, for help I cried,</span>
    <span>Lord, I am press'd on every side;</span>
    <span>The cause is thine, they fight with me,</span>
    <span>But every blow is aim'd at thee.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-21-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>With speed to my relief he came,</span>
    <span>And put my enemies to shame:</span>
    <span>Thus saved by grace, I live to sing</span>
    <span>The love and triumphs of my King.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-22." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">22.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Jehovah-Shalem—The Lord send Peace.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Judges, vi, 24.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-22-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Jesus, whose blood so freely stream'd</span>
    <span>To satisfy the law's demand,</span>
    <span>By thee from guilt and wrath redeem'd,</span>
    <span>Before the Father's face I stand.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-22-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>To reconcile offending man,</span>
    <span>Made Justice drop her angry rod;</span>
    <span>What creature could have form'd the plan,</span>
    <span>Or who fulfill it but a God?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-22-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>No drop remains of all the curse</span>
    <span>For wretches who deserved the whole;</span>
    <span>No arrows dipp'd in wrath to pierce</span>
    <span>The guilty but returning soul.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-22-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Peace by such means, so dearly bought,</span>
    <span>What rebel could have hoped to see?</span>
    <span>Peace, by his injured Sovereign wrought,</span>
    <span>His Sovereign fasten'd to the tree!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-22-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Now, Lord, thy feeble worm prepare;</span>
    <span>For strife with earth and hell begins;</span>
    <span>Confirm and gird me for the war;</span>
    <span>They hate the soul that hates his sins.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-22-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Let them in horrid league agree!</span>
    <span>They may assault, they may distress,</span>
    <span>But cannot quench thy love to me,</span>
    <span>Nor rob me of the Lord my peace.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-23." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">23.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Gideon’s Fleece.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Judges, vi, 37-40.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-23-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The signs which God to Gideon gave</span>
    <span>His holy sovereignty made known,</span>
    <span>That he alone has power to save,</span>
    <span>And claims the glory as his own.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-23-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The dew which first the fleece had fill'd,</span>
    <span>When all the earth was dry around,</span>
    <span>Was from it afterwards withheld,</span>
    <span>And only fell upon the ground.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-23-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>To Isr'el thus the heav'nly dew</span>
    <span>Of saving truth was long restrain'd;</span>
    <span>Of which the Gentiles nothing knew,</span>
    <span>But dry and desolate remained.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-23-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But now the Gentiles have received</span>
    <span>The balmy dew of gospel peace;</span>
    <span>And Isr'el, who his Spirit grieved,</span>
    <span>Is left a dry and empty fleece.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-23-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>This dew still falls at his command,</span>
    <span>To keep his chosen plants alive;</span>
    <span>They shall, though in a thirsty land,</span>
    <span>Like willows by the waters thrive.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-23-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But chiefly when his people meet,</span>
    <span>To hear his word and seek his face,</span>
    <span>The gentle dew, with influence sweet,</span>
    <span>Descends and nourishes their grace.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-23-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But ah! what numbers still are dead,</span>
    <span>Though under means of grace they lie,—</span>
    <span>The dew still falling round their head,</span>
    <span>And yet their heart untouch'd and dry.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-23-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Dear Saviour, hear us when we call;</span>
    <span>To wrestling prayer an answer give;</span>
    <span>Pour down thy dew upon us all,</span>
    <span>That all may feel and all may live.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-24." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">24.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Samson’s Lion.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Judges, xiv, 8.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-24-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The lion that on Samson roar'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">And thirsted for his blood,</span>
    <span>With honey afterwards was stored,</span>
      <span class="i1">And furnish'd him with food.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-24-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Believers as they pass along</span>
      <span class="i1">With many lions meet,</span>
    <span>But gather sweetness from the strong,</span>
      <span class="i1">And from the eater meat.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-24-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The lions rage and roar in vain,</span>
      <span class="i1">For Jesus is their shield:</span>
    <span>Their losses prove a certain gain,</span>
      <span class="i1">Their troubles comfort yield.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-24-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The world and Satan join their strength,</span>
      <span class="i1">To fill their souls with fears;</span>
    <span>But crops of joy they reap at length</span>
      <span class="i1">From what they sow in tears.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-24-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Afflictions make them love the word,</span>
      <span class="i1">Stir up their hearts to prayer,</span>
    <span>And many precious proofs afford</span>
      <span class="i1">Of their Redeemer's care.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-24-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The lions roar but cannot kill;</span>
      <span class="i1">Then fear them not, my friends;</span>
    <span>They bring us, though against their will,</span>
      <span class="i1">The honey Jesus sends.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-25." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">25.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Hannah; or the Throne of Grace.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">1 Sam. i, 18.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-25-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">When Hannah, press'd with grief,</span>
      <span class="i1">Pour'd forth her soul in pray'r;</span>
      <span class="i1">She quickly found relief,</span>
      <span class="i1">And left her burden there:</span>
    <span>Like her, in every trying case</span>
    <span>Let us approach the throne of grace.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-25-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">When she began to pray,</span>
      <span class="i1">Her heart was pain'd and sad;</span>
      <span class="i1">But ere she went away</span>
      <span class="i1">Was comforted and glad.</span>
    <span>In trouble what a resting-place</span>
    <span>Have they who know the throne of grace!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-25-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Though men and devils rage,</span>
      <span class="i1">And threaten to devour,</span>
      <span class="i1">The saints from age to age</span>
      <span class="i1">Are safe from all their power;</span>
    <span>Fresh strength they gain to run their race</span>
    <span>By waiting at the throne of grace.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-25-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Eli her case mistook;</span>
      <span class="i1">How was her spirit moved</span>
      <span class="i1">By his unkind rebuke!</span>
      <span class="i1">But God her cause approved.</span>
    <span>We need not fear a creature's face</span>
    <span>While welcome at the throne of grace.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-25-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">She was not fill'd with wine,</span>
      <span class="i1">As Eli rashly thought,</span>
      <span class="i1">But with a faith divine,</span>
      <span class="i1">And found the help she sought.</span>
    <span>Though men despise and call us base,</span>
    <span>Still let us ply the throne of grace.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-25-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Men have not power or skill</span>
      <span class="i1">With troubled souls to bear;</span>
      <span class="i1">Though they express good-will.</span>
      <span class="i1">Poor comforters they are:</span>
    <span>But swelling sorrows sink apace</span>
    <span>When we approach the throne of grace.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-25-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Numbers before have tried,</span>
      <span class="i1">And found the promise true;</span>
      <span class="i1">Nor yet one been denied,</span>
      <span class="i1">Then why should I or you?</span>
    <span>Let us by faith their footsteps trace,</span>
    <span>And hasten to the throne of grace.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-25-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">As fogs obscure the light,</span>
      <span class="i1">And taint the morning air,</span>
      <span class="i1">But soon are put to flight</span>
      <span class="i1">If the bright sun appear,</span>
    <span>Thus Jesus will our troubles chase,</span>
    <span>By shining from the throne of grace.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-26." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">26.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Dagon before the Ark.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">1 Sam. v, 4, 5.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-26-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When first, to make my heart his own,</span>
    <span>The Lord reveal'd his mighty grace,</span>
    <span>Self reign'd, like Dagon, on the throne,</span>
    <span>But could not long maintain its place.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-26-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>It fell, and own'd the power divine,</span>
    <span>(Grace can with ease the victory gain,)</span>
    <span>But soon this wretched heart of mine</span>
    <span>Contrived to set it up again.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-26-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Again the Lord his name proclaim'd,</span>
    <span>And brought the hateful idol low;</span>
    <span>Then self, like Dagon, broken, maim'd,</span>
    <span>Seem'd to receive a mortal blow:</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-26-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Yet self is not of life bereft,</span>
    <span>Nor ceases to oppose his will;</span>
    <span>Though but a maimed stump be left,</span>
    <span>'Tis Dagon—'tis an idol still.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-26-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Lord! must I always guilty prove,</span>
    <span>And idols in my heart have room?</span>
    <span>Oh! let the fire of heavenly love</span>
    <span>The very stump of self consume.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-27." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">27.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Milch Kine drawing the Ark: Faith’s Surrender of all.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">1 Sam. vi, 12.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-27-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">The kine unguided went</span>
      <span class="i1">By the directest road,</span>
    <span>When the Philistines homeward sent</span>
      <span class="i1">The ark of Israel's God.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-27-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Lowing they pass'd along</span>
      <span class="i1">And left their calves shut up;</span>
    <span>They felt an instinct for their young,</span>
      <span class="i1">But would not turn or stop.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-27-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Shall brutes, devoid of thought,</span>
      <span class="i1">Their Maker's will obey;</span>
    <span>And we, who by his grace are taught.</span>
      <span class="i1">More stubborn prove than they?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-27-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">He shed his precious blood,</span>
      <span class="i1">To make us his alone;</span>
    <span>If wash'd in that atoning flood,</span>
      <span class="i1">We are no more our own.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-27-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">If he his will reveal,</span>
      <span class="i1">Let us obey his call;</span>
    <span>And think, whate'er the flesh may feel,</span>
      <span class="i1">His love deserves our all.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-27-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">We should maintain in view</span>
      <span class="i1">His glory as our end;</span>
    <span>Too much we cannot bear or do</span>
      <span class="i1">For such a matchless Friend.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-27-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">His saints should stand prepared</span>
      <span class="i1">In duty's path to run;</span>
    <span>Nor count their greatest trials hard</span>
      <span class="i1">So that his will be done.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-27-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">With Jesus for our guide,</span>
      <span class="i1">The path is safe, though rough,</span>
    <span>The promise says, "I will provide;"</span>
      <span class="i1">And faith replies, "Enough!"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-28." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">28.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Saul’s Armour.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">1 Sam. xvii, 38–40.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-28-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When first my soul enlisted</span>
      <span class="i1">My Saviour's foes to fight,</span>
    <span>Mistaken friends insisted</span>
      <span class="i1">I was not arm'd aright:</span>
    <span>So Saul advised David</span>
      <span class="i1">He certainly would fail,</span>
    <span>Nor could his life be saved</span>
      <span class="i1">Without a coat of mail.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-28-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But David, though he yielded</span>
      <span class="i1">To put the armour on,</span>
    <span>Soon found he could not wield it,</span>
      <span class="i1">And ventured forth with none.</span>
    <span>With only sling and pebble</span>
      <span class="i1">He fought the fight of faith:</span>
    <span>The weapons seem'd but feeble,</span>
      <span class="i1">Yet proved Goliath's death.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-28-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Had I by him been guided,</span>
      <span class="i1">And quickly thrown away</span>
    <span>The armour men provided,</span>
      <span class="i1">I might have gain'd the day:</span>
    <span>But arm'd as they advised me,</span>
      <span class="i1">My expectations fail'd;</span>
    <span>My enemy surprised me,</span>
      <span class="i1">And had almost prevail'd.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-28-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Furnish'd with books and notions,</span>
      <span class="i1">And arguments and pride,</span>
    <span>I practised all my motions,</span>
      <span class="i1">And Satan's power defied:</span>
    <span>But soon perceived with trouble</span>
      <span class="i1">That these would do no good;</span>
    <span>Iron to him is stubble,</span>
      <span class="i1">And brass like rotton wood.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-28-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>I triumph'd at a distance,</span>
      <span class="i1">While he was out of sight;</span>
    <span>But faint was my resistance</span>
      <span class="i1">When forced to join in fight:</span>
    <span>He broke my sword in shivers,</span>
      <span class="i1">And pierced my boasted shield;</span>
    <span>Laugh'd at my vain endeavours,</span>
      <span class="i1">And drove me from the field.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-28-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Satan will not be braved</span>
      <span class="i1">By such a worm as I;</span>
    <span>Then let me learn with David</span>
      <span class="i1">To trust in the Most High,—</span>
    <span>To plead the name of Jesus,</span>
      <span class="i1">And use the sling of prayer:</span>
    <span>Thus arm'd, when Satan sees us</span>
      <span class="i1">He'll tremble and despair.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-29." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">29.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">David’s Fall.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">2 Sam. xi, 27.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-29-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>How David, when by sin deceived,</span>
      <span class="i1">From bad to worse went on!</span>
    <span>For when the Holy Spirit's grieved,</span>
      <span class="i1">Our strength and guard are gone.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-29-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>His eyes, on Bathsheba once fix'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">With poison fill'd his soul;</span>
    <span>He ventured on adult'ry next,</span>
      <span class="i1">And murder crown'd the whole.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-29-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>So from a spark of fire at first,</span>
      <span class="i1">That has not been descried,</span>
    <span>A dreadful flame has often burst,</span>
      <span class="i1">And ravaged far and wide.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-29-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When sin deceives it hardens too;</span>
      <span class="i1">For though he vainly sought</span>
    <span>To hide his crimes from public view,</span>
      <span class="i1">Of God he little thought.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-29-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>He neither would nor could repent,</span>
      <span class="i1">No true compunction felt,</span>
    <span>Till God in mercy Nathan sent,</span>
      <span class="i1">His stubborn heart to melt.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-29-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The parable held forth a fact,</span>
      <span class="i1">Design'd his case to show;</span>
    <span>But though the picture was exact,</span>
      <span class="i1">Himself he did not know.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-29-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Thou art the man," the prophet said:</span>
      <span class="i1">That word his slumber broke;</span>
    <span>And when he own'd his sin and pray'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">The Lord forgiveness spoke.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-29-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Let those who think they stand, beware,</span>
      <span class="i1">For David stood before:</span>
    <span>Nor let the fallen soul despair,</span>
      <span class="i1">For Mercy can restore.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-30." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">30.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Is this thy kindness to thy Friend?.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">2 Sam. xvi, 17.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-30-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Poor, weak, and worthless, though I am,</span>
    <span>I have a rich, almighty Friend;</span>
    <span>Jesus, the Saviour, is his name,</span>
    <span>He freely loves, and without end.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-30-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>He ransom'd me from hell with blood,</span>
    <span>And by his power my foes control'd;</span>
    <span>He found me wand'ring far from God,</span>
    <span>And brought me to his chosen fold.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-30-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>He cheers my heart, my want supplies,</span>
    <span>And says that I shall shortly be</span>
    <span>Enthroned with him above the skies:</span>
    <span>what a Friend is Christ to me!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-30-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But ah! my inmost spirit mourns,</span>
    <span>And well my eyes with tears may swim,</span>
    <span>To think of my perverse returns;</span>
    <span>I've been a faithless friend to him.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-30-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Often my gracious Friend I grieve,</span>
    <span>Neglect, distrust, and disobey;</span>
    <span>And often Satan's lies believe</span>
    <span>Sooner than all my Friend can say.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-30-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>He bids me always freely come,</span>
    <span>And promises whate'er I ask;</span>
    <span>But I am straiten'd, cold, and dumb,</span>
    <span>And count my privilege a task.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-30-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Before the world, that hates his cause,</span>
    <span>My treach'rous heart has throbb'd with shame;</span>
    <span>Loath to forego the world's applause,</span>
    <span>I hardly dare avow his name.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-30-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Sure, were not I most vile and base,</span>
    <span>I could not thus my Friend requite!</span>
    <span>And were not he the God of grace</span>
    <span>He'd frown, and spurn me from his sight.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-31." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">31.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Ask what I shall give Thee.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">1 Kings, iii, 5.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-31-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Come, my soul, thy suit prepare,—</span>
    <span>Jesus loves to answer prayer;</span>
    <span>He himself has bid thee pray,</span>
    <span>Therefore will not say thee nay.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-31-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thou art coming to a King,</span>
    <span>Large petitions with thee bring;</span>
    <span>For his grace and power are such</span>
    <span>None can ever ask too much.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-31-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>With my burden I begin,—</span>
    <span>Lord, remove this load of sin!</span>
    <span>Let thy blood, for sinners spilt,</span>
    <span>Set my conscience free from guilt.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-31-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Lord! I come to thee for rest,—</span>
    <span>Take possession of my breast;</span>
    <span>There thy blood-bought right maintain,</span>
    <span>And without a rival reign.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-31-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>As the image in the glass</span>
    <span>Answers the beholder's face,</span>
    <span>Thus unto my heart appear,</span>
    <span>Print thine own resemblance there.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-31-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>While I am a pilgrim here</span>
    <span>Let thy love my spirit cheer;</span>
    <span>As my Guide, my Guard, my Friend,</span>
    <span>Lead me to my journey's end:</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
