<section id="stanza-1-31-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Show me what I have to do;</span>
    <span>Every hour my strength renew;</span>
    <span>Let me live a life of faith,</span>
    <span>Let me die thy people's death.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-32." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">32.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Another.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead"></p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-32-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>If Solomon for wisdom pray'd,</span>
    <span>The Lord before had made him wise;</span>
    <span>Else he another choice had made,</span>
    <span>And ask'd for what the worldings prize.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-32-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus he invites his people still,—</span>
    <span>He first instructs them how to choose,</span>
    <span>Then bids them ask whate'er they will,</span>
    <span>Assured that he will not refuse.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-32-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Our wishes would our ruin prove,</span>
    <span>Could we our wretched choice obtain,—</span>
    <span>Before we feel the Saviour's love</span>
    <span>Kindle our love to him again:</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-32-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But when our hearts perceive his worth,</span>
    <span>Desires, till then unknown, take place;</span>
    <span>Our spirits cleave no more to earth,</span>
    <span>But pant for holiness and grace.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-32-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>And dost thou say, "Ask what thou wilt"?</span>
    <span>Lord, I would seize the golden hour,—</span>
    <span>I pray to be released from guilt,</span>
    <span>And freed from sin and Satan's power.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-32-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>More of thy presence, Lord, impart;</span>
    <span>More of thy image let me bear;</span>
    <span>Erect thy throne within my heart,</span>
    <span>And reign without a rival there.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-32-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Give me to read my pardon seal'd,</span>
    <span>And from thy joy to draw my strength,—</span>
    <span>To have thy boundless love reveal'd</span>
    <span>In all its height and breadth and length.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-32-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Grant these requests,—I ask no more,</span>
    <span>But to thy care the rest resign;</span>
    <span>Sick or in health, or rich or poor,</span>
    <span>All shall be well if thou art mine.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-33." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">33.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Another.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead"></p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-33-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Behold the throne of grace!</span>
      <span class="i1">The promise calls me near;</span>
    <span>There Jesus shows a smiling face,</span>
      <span class="i1">And waits to answer pray'r.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-33-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">That rich atoning blood</span>
      <span class="i1">Which sprinkled round I see</span>
    <span>Provides for those who come to God</span>
      <span class="i1">An all-prevailing plea.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-33-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">My soul, ask what thou wilt,—</span>
      <span class="i1">Thou canst not be too bold;</span>
    <span>Since his own blood for thee he spilt,</span>
      <span class="i1">What else can he withhold?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-33-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Beyond thy utmost wants</span>
      <span class="i1">His love and power can bless;</span>
    <span>To praying souls he always grants</span>
      <span class="i1">More than they can express.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-33-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Since 'tis the Lord's command,</span>
      <span class="i1">My mouth I open wide;</span>
    <span>Lord, open thou thy bounteous hand,</span>
      <span class="i1">That I may be supplied.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-33-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Thine image, Lord, bestow,</span>
      <span class="i1">Thy presence and thy love;</span>
    <span>I ask to serve thee here below,</span>
      <span class="i1">And reign with thee above.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-33-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Teach me to live by faith,</span>
      <span class="i1">Conform my will to thine;</span>
    <span>Let me victorious be in death,</span>
      <span class="i1">And then in glory shine.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-33-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">If thou these blessings give,</span>
      <span class="i1">And wilt my portion be,</span>
    <span>Cheerful the world's poor toys I leave</span>
      <span class="i1">To them who know not thee.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-34." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">34.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Queen of Sheba.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">1 Kings, x, 1-9.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-34-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>From Sheba a distant report</span>
    <span>Of Solomon's glory and fame</span>
    <span>Invited the queen to his court,</span>
    <span>But all was outdone when she came:</span>
    <span>She cried with a pleasing surprise,</span>
    <span>When first she before him appear'd,</span>
    <span>"How much what I see with my eyes</span>
    <span>Surpasses the rumour I heard!"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-34-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When once to Jerusalem come</span>
    <span>The treasure and train she had brought,</span>
    <span>The wealth she possessed at home</span>
    <span>No longer had place in her thought:</span>
    <span>His house, his attendants, his throne,</span>
    <span>All struck her with wonder and awe;</span>
    <span>The glory of Solomon shone</span>
    <span>In every object she saw.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-34-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But Solomon most she admired,</span>
    <span>Whose spirit conducted the whole,—</span>
    <span>His wisdom, which God had inspired,</span>
    <span>His bounty, and greatness of soul.</span>
    <span>Of all the hard questions she put</span>
    <span>A ready solution he show'd,—</span>
    <span>Exceeded her wish and her suit,</span>
    <span>And more than she ask'd him bestow'd.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-34-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus I, when the gospel proclaim'd</span>
    <span>The Saviour's great name in my ears,</span>
    <span>The wisdom for which he is famed,</span>
    <span>The love which to sinners he bears,</span>
    <span>I long'd, and I was not denied,</span>
    <span>That I in his presence might bow;</span>
    <span>I saw, and transported I cried,</span>
    <span>"A greater than Solomon thou!"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-34-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>My conscience no comfort could find,</span>
    <span>By doubt and hard questions opposed;</span>
    <span>But he restored peace to my mind,</span>
    <span>And answer'd each doubt I proposed.</span>
    <span>Beholding me poor and distress'd,</span>
    <span>His bounty supplied all my wants;</span>
    <span>My pray'r could have never express'd</span>
    <span>So much as this Solomon grants.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-34-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>I heard and was slow to believe,</span>
    <span>But now with my eyes I behold</span>
    <span>Much more than my heart could conceive,</span>
    <span>Or language could ever have told.</span>
    <span>How happy thy servants must be</span>
    <span>Who always before thee appear!</span>
    <span>Vouchsafe, Lord, this blessing to me,</span>
    <span>I find it is good to be here.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-35." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">35.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Elijah fed by Ravens.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">1 Kings, xvii, 6.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-35-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Elijah's example declares,</span>
    <span>Whatever distress may betide,</span>
    <span>The saints may commit all their cares</span>
    <span>To Him who will surely provide:</span>
    <span>When rain long withheld from the earth</span>
    <span>Occasion'd a famine of bread,</span>
    <span>The prophet, secured from the dearth,</span>
    <span>By ravens was constantly fed.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-35-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>More likely to rob than to feed</span>
    <span>Were ravens, who live upon prey;</span>
    <span>But when the Lord's people have need,</span>
    <span>His goodness will find out a way.</span>
    <span>This instance to those may be strange</span>
    <span>Who know not how faith can prevail;</span>
    <span>But sooner all nature shall change</span>
    <span>Than one of God's promises fail.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-35-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Nor is it a singular case</span>
    <span>The wonder is often renew'd;</span>
    <span>And many can say to his praise,</span>
    <span>He sends them by ravens their food.</span>
    <span>Thus worldlings, though ravens indeed,</span>
    <span>Though greedy and selfish their mind,</span>
    <span>If God has a servant to feed,</span>
    <span>Against their own wills can be kind.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-35-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus Satan, that raven unclean,</span>
    <span>Who croaks in the ears of the saints,</span>
    <span>Compell'd by a Power unseen,</span>
    <span>Administers oft to their wants:</span>
    <span>God teaches them how to find food</span>
    <span>From all the temptations they feel;</span>
    <span>This raven, who thirsts for my blood,</span>
    <span>Has help'd me to many a meal.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-35-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>How safe and how happy are they</span>
    <span>Who on the good Shepherd rely!</span>
    <span>He gives them out strength for their day,</span>
    <span>Their wants he will surely supply:</span>
    <span>He ravens and lions can tame,—</span>
    <span>All creatures obey his command;</span>
    <span>Then let me rejoice in his name,</span>
    <span>And leave all my cares in his hand.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-36." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">36.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Meal and Cruse of Oil.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">1 Kings, xvii, 16.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-36-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>By the poor widow's oil and meal</span>
      <span class="i1">Elijah was sustain'd;</span>
    <span>Though small the stock, it lasted well,</span>
      <span class="i1">For God the store maintain'd.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-36-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>It seem'd as if from day to day</span>
      <span class="i1">They were to eat and die;</span>
    <span>But still, though in a secret way,</span>
      <span class="i1">He sent a fresh supply.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-36-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus to his poor He still will give</span>
      <span class="i1">Just for the present hour;</span>
    <span>But for to-morrow they must live</span>
      <span class="i1">Upon his word and power.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-36-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>No barn or storehouse they possess</span>
      <span class="i1">On which they can depend;</span>
    <span>Yet have no cause to fear distress,</span>
      <span class="i1">For Jesus is their Friend,</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-36-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Then let not doubts your mind assail;</span>
      <span class="i1">Remember God has said,</span>
    <span>"The cruse and barrel shall not fail,—</span>
      <span class="i1">My people shall be fed."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-36-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>And thus, though faint it often seems,</span>
      <span class="i1">He keeps their grace alive;</span>
    <span>Supplied by his refreshing streams,</span>
      <span class="i1">Their dying hopes revive.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-36-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Though in ourselves we have no stock,</span>
      <span class="i1">The Lord is nigh to save;</span>
    <span>His door flies open when we knock,</span>
      <span class="i1">And 'tis but ask and have.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-37." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">37.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Jericho; or, The Waters healed.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">2 Kings, ii, 19-22.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-37-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Though Jericho pleasantly stood,</span>
    <span>And look'd like a promising soil,</span>
    <span>The harvest produced little food,</span>
    <span>To answer the husbandman's toil.</span>
    <span>The water some property had</span>
    <span>Which poisonous proved to the ground,</span>
    <span>The springs were corrupted and bad,</span>
    <span>The streams spread a barrenness round.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-37-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But soon by the cruse and the salt</span>
    <span>Prepared by Elisha's command</span>
    <span>The water was cured of its fault,</span>
    <span>And plenty enriched the land.</span>
    <span>An emblem sure this of the grace</span>
    <span>On fruitless dead sinners bestow'd;</span>
    <span>For man is in Jericho's case</span>
    <span>Till cured by the mercy of God.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-37-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>How noble a creature he seems!</span>
    <span>What knowledge, invention, and skill!</span>
    <span>How large and extensive his schemes!</span>
    <span>How much can he do if he will!</span>
    <span>His zeal to be learned and wise</span>
    <span>Will yield to no limits or bars;</span>
    <span>He measures the earth and the skies,</span>
    <span>And numbers and marshals the stars.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-37-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Yet still he is barren of good;</span>
    <span>In vain are his talents and art;</span>
    <span>For sin has infected his blood,</span>
    <span>And poison'd the streams of his heart.</span>
    <span>Though cockatrice eggs he can hatch,</span>
    <span>Or, spider-like, cobwebs can weave,</span>
    <span>'Tis madness to labour and watch</span>
    <span>For what will destroy and deceive.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-37-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But grace, like the salt in the cruse,</span>
    <span>When cast in the spring of the soul,</span>
    <span>A wonderful change will produce,</span>
    <span>Diffusing new life through the whole:</span>
    <span>The wilderness blooms like a rose,</span>
    <span>The heart which was vile and abhorr'd</span>
    <span>Now fruitful and beautiful grows—</span>
    <span>The garden and joy of the Lord.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-38." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">38.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Naaman.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">2 Kings, v, 14.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-38-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Before Elisha's gate</span>
      <span class="i1">The Syrian leper stood;</span>
      <span class="i1">But could not brook to wait,—</span>
      <span class="i1">He deem'd himself too good:</span>
    <span>He thought the prophet would attend,</span>
    <span>And not to him a message send.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-38-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">"Have I this journey come,</span>
      <span class="i1">And will he not be seen?</span>
      <span class="i1">I were as well at home</span>
      <span class="i1">Would washing make me clean;</span>
    <span>Why must I wash in Jordan's flood?</span>
    <span>Damascus' rivers are as good."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-38-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Thus, by his foolish pride,</span>
      <span class="i1">He almost miss'd a cure;</span>
      <span class="i1">Howe'er at length he tried,</span>
      <span class="i1">And found the method sure:</span>
    <span>Soon as the pride was brought to yield</span>
    <span>The leprosy was quickly heal'd.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-38-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Leprous and proud as he,</span>
      <span class="i1">To Jesus thus I came,</span>
      <span class="i1">From sin to set me free,</span>
      <span class="i1">When first I heard his fame:</span>
    <span>Surely, thought I, my pompous train</span>
    <span>Of vows and tears will notice gain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-38-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">My heart devised the way</span>
      <span class="i1">Which I supposed he'd take;</span>
      <span class="i1">And when I found delay,</span>
      <span class="i1">Was ready to go back:</span>
    <span>Had he some painful task enjoin'd,</span>
    <span>I to performance seem'd inclined.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-38-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">When by his word he spake,</span>
      <span class="i1">"That fountain open'd see;</span>
      <span class="i1">'Twas open'd for thy sake,—</span>
      <span class="i1">"Go wash, and thou art free;"</span>
    <span>Oh! how did my proud heart gainsay,—</span>
    <span>I fear'd to trust his simple way.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-38-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">At length I trial made,</span>
      <span class="i1">When I had much endured;</span>
      <span class="i1">The message I obey'd,—</span>
      <span class="i1">I wash'd, and I was cured.</span>
    <span>Sinners, this healing fountain try,</span>
    <span>Which cleansed a wretch so vile as I.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-39." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">39.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The borrowed Axe.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">2 Kings, vi, 5, 6.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-39-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>1 The prophets' sons in times of old,</span>
      <span class="i1">Though to appearance poor,</span>
    <span>Were rich without possessing gold,</span>
      <span class="i1">And honour'd though obscure.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-39-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>In peace their daily bread they eat,</span>
      <span class="i1">By honest labour earn'd;</span>
    <span>While daily at Elisha's feet</span>
      <span class="i1">They grace and wisdom learn'd.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-39-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The prophet's presence cheer'd their toil,</span>
      <span class="i1">They watch'd the words he spoke,</span>
    <span>Whether they turn'd the furrow'd soil,</span>
      <span class="i1">Or fell'd the spreading oak.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-39-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Once as they listen'd to his theme</span>
      <span class="i1">Their conference was stopp'd;</span>
    <span>For one beneath the yielding stream</span>
      <span class="i1">A borrow'd axe had dropp'd.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-39-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Alas! it was not mine," he said;</span>
      <span class="i1">"How shall I make it good?"</span>
    <span>Elisha heard, and when he pray'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">The iron swam like wood.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-39-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>If God in such a small affair</span>
      <span class="i1">A miracle performs,</span>
    <span>It shows his condescending care</span>
      <span class="i1">Of poor unworthy worms.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-39-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Though kings and nations in his view</span>
      <span class="i1">Are but as motes and dust,</span>
    <span>His eyes and ear are fix'd on you</span>
      <span class="i1">Who in his mercy trust.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-39-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Not one concern of ours is small</span>
      <span class="i1">If we belong to him.</span>
    <span>To teach us this, the Lord of all</span>
      <span class="i1">Once made the iron swim.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-40." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">40.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">More with us than with them.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">2 Kings, vi, 16.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-40-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Alas! Elisha's servant cried,</span>
    <span>When he the Syrian army spied;</span>
    <span>But he was soon released from care,</span>
    <span>In answer to the prophet's prayer.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-40-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Straightway he saw, with other eyes,</span>
    <span>A greater army from the skies,—</span>
    <span>A fiery guard around the hill;</span>
    <span>Thus are the saints preserved still.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-40-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When Satan and his host appear,</span>
    <span>Like him of old, I faint and fear;</span>
    <span>Like him, by faith, with joy I see</span>
    <span>A greater host engaged for me.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-40-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The saints espouse my cause by pray'r,</span>
    <span>The angels make my soul their care;</span>
    <span>Mine is the promise seal'd with blood,</span>
    <span>And Jesus lives to make it good.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-41." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">41.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Faith’s Review and Expectation.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">1 Chron. xvii, 16, 17.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-41-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Amazing grace! (how sweet the sound!)</span>
      <span class="i1">That saved a wretch like me!</span>
    <span>I once was lost, but now am found,—</span>
      <span class="i1">Was blind, but now I see.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-41-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>'Twas grace that taught my heart to fear,</span>
      <span class="i1">And grace my fears relieved;</span>
    <span>How precious did that grace appear</span>
      <span class="i1">The hour I first believed!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-41-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Through many dangers, toils, and snares.</span>
      <span class="i1">I have already come;</span>
    <span>'Tis grace has brought me safe thus far,</span>
      <span class="i1">And grace will lead me home.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-41-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The Lord has promised good to me,—</span>
      <span class="i1">His word my hope secures;</span>
    <span>He will my shield and portion be</span>
      <span class="i1">As long as life endures.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-41-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Yes, when this flesh and heart shall fail,</span>
      <span class="i1">And mortal life shall cease,</span>
    <span>I shall possess, within the veil,</span>
      <span class="i1">A life of joy and peace.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-41-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The earth shall soon dissolve like snow,</span>
      <span class="i1">The sun forbear to shine;</span>
    <span>But God, who call'd me here below,</span>
      <span class="i1">Will be for ever mine.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-42." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">42.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Joy of the Lord is your Strength.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Neh. viii, 10.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-42-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Joy is a fruit that will not grow</span>
      <span class="i1">In Nature's barren soil;</span>
    <span>All we can boast till Christ we know</span>
      <span class="i1">Is vanity and toil.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-42-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But where the Lord has planted grace,</span>
      <span class="i1">And made his glories known,</span>
    <span>There fruits of heavenly joy and peace</span>
      <span class="i1">Are found, and there alone.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-42-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>A bleeding Saviour seen by faith,</span>
      <span class="i1">A sense of pard'ning love,</span>
    <span>A hope that triumphs over death,</span>
      <span class="i1">Give joys like those above.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-42-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>To take a glimpse within the veil,</span>
      <span class="i1">To know that God is mine,</span>
    <span>Are springs of joy that never fail,</span>
      <span class="i1">Unspeakable! divine!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-42-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>These are the joys which satisfy</span>
      <span class="i1">And sanctify the mind;</span>
    <span>Which make the spirit mount on high,</span>
      <span class="i1">And leave the world behind.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-42-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>No more, believers, mourn jour lot,</span>
      <span class="i1">But if you are the Lord's,</span>
    <span>Resign to them that know him not</span>
      <span class="i1">Such joys as earth affords.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-43." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">43.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Oh that I were as in Months past!.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Job, xxix, 2.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-43-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Sweet was the time when first I felt</span>
      <span class="i1">The Saviour's pard'ning blood</span>
    <span>Applied, to cleanse my soul from guilt,</span>
      <span class="i1">And bring me home to God.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-43-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Soon as the morn the light reveal'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">His praises tuned my tongue;</span>
    <span>And when the evening shades prevail'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">His love was all my song:</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-43-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>In vain the tempter spread his wiles,</span>
      <span class="i1">The world no more could charm;</span>
    <span>I lived upon my Saviour's smiles,</span>
      <span class="i1">And lean'd upon his arm.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-43-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>In pray'r my soul drew near the Lord,</span>
      <span class="i1">And saw his glory shine;</span>
    <span>And when I read his holy word</span>
      <span class="i1">I call'd each promise mine.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-43-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Then to his saints I often spoke</span>
      <span class="i1">Of what his love hath done:</span>
    <span>But now my heart is almost broke,</span>
      <span class="i1">For all my joys are gone.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-43-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Now when the evening shade prevails,</span>
      <span class="i1">My soul in darkness mourns;</span>
    <span>And when the morn the light reveals,</span>
      <span class="i1">No light to me returns.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-43-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>My pray'rs are now a chatt'ring noise,</span>
      <span class="i1">For Jesus hides his face;</span>
    <span>I read, the promise meets my eyes,</span>
      <span class="i1">But will not reach my case.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-43-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Now Satan threatens to prevail,</span>
      <span class="i1">And make my soul his prey;</span>
    <span>Yet, Lord, thy mercies cannot fail:</span>
      <span class="i1">O come without delay!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-44." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">44.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Change.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead"></p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-44-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Saviour, shine, and cheer my soul;</span>
    <span>Bid my dying hopes revive;</span>
    <span>Make my wounded spirit whole;</span>
    <span>Far away the tempter drive;</span>
    <span>Speak the word, and set me free;</span>
    <span>Let me live alone to thee.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-44-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Shall I sigh and pray in vain,</span>
    <span>Wilt thou still refuse to hear;</span>
    <span>Wilt thou not return again;</span>
    <span>Must I yield to black despair?</span>
    <span>Thou hast taught my heart to pray,</span>
    <span>Canst thou turn thy face away?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-44-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Once I thought my mountain strong,</span>
    <span>Firmly fix'd, no more to move;</span>
    <span>Then thy grace was all my song,</span>
    <span>Then my soul was fill'd with love:</span>
    <span>Those were happy golden days,</span>
    <span>Sweetly spent in pray'r and praise.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-44-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When my friends have said, "Beware,</span>
    <span>Soon or late you'll find a change,"</span>
    <span>I could see no cause for fear,</span>
    <span>Vain their caution seem'd and strange:</span>
    <span>Not a cloud obscured my sky,</span>
    <span>Could I think a tempest nigh?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-44-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Little then myself I knew,</span>
    <span>Little thought of Satan's power;</span>
    <span>Now I find their words were true,</span>
    <span>Now I feel the stormy hour!</span>
    <span>Sin has put my joys to flight,</span>
    <span>Sin has changed my day to night.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-44-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Satan asks, and mocks my woe,</span>
    <span>"Boaster, where is now your God?"</span>
    <span>Silence, Lord, this cruel foe;</span>
    <span>Let him know I'm bought with blood;</span>
    <span>Tell him, since I know thy name,</span>
    <span>Though I change, thou art the same.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-45." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">45.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Pleading for Mercy.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Psalm vi.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-45-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>In mercy, not in wrath, rebuke</span>
      <span class="i1">Thy feeble worm, my God!</span>
    <span>My spirit dreads thy angry look,</span>
      <span class="i1">And trembles at thy rod.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-45-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Have mercy, Lord, for I am weak;</span>
      <span class="i1">Regard my heavy groans;</span>
    <span>O let thy voice of comfort speak,</span>
      <span class="i1">And heal my broken bones!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-45-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>By day, my busy beating head</span>
      <span class="i1">Is fill'd with anxious fears;</span>
    <span>By night, upon my restless bed,</span>
      <span class="i1">I weep a flood of tears.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-45-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus I sit desolate and mourn,</span>
      <span class="i1">Mine eyes grow dull with grief;</span>
    <span>How long, my Lord, ere thou return,</span>
      <span class="i1">And bring my soul relief?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-45-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>O come and show thy power to save,</span>
      <span class="i1">And spare my fainting breath;</span>
    <span>For who can praise thee in the grave,</span>
      <span class="i1">Or sing thy name in death?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-45-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Satan, my cruel envious foe,</span>
      <span class="i1">Insults me in my pain;</span>
    <span>He smiles to see me brought so low,</span>
      <span class="i1">And tells me hope is vain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-45-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But hence, thou enemy, depart!</span>
      <span class="i1">Nor tempt me to despair;</span>
    <span>My Saviour comes to cheer my heart,</span>
      <span class="i1">The Lord has heard my prayer.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-46." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">46.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">None upon earth I desire besides Thee.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Psalm lxxiii, 25.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-46-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>How tedious and tasteless the hours</span>
    <span>When Jesus no longer I see;</span>
    <span>Sweet prospects, sweet birds, and sweet flowers,</span>
    <span>Have all lost their sweetness with me:</span>
    <span>The midsummer sun shines but dim.</span>
    <span>The fields strive in vain to look gay,</span>
    <span>But when I am happy in him,</span>
    <span>December's as pleasant as May.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-46-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>His name yields the richest perfume,</span>
    <span>And sweeter than music his voice,</span>
    <span>His presence disperses my gloom,</span>
    <span>And makes all within me rejoice;</span>
    <span>I should, were he always so nigh,</span>
    <span>Have nothing to wish or to fear;</span>
    <span>No mortal so happy as I,</span>
    <span>My summer would last all the year.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-46-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Content with beholding his face,</span>
    <span>My all to his pleasure resign'd,</span>
    <span>No changes of season or place</span>
    <span>Would make any change in my mind:</span>
    <span>While bless'd with a sense of his love,</span>
    <span>A palace a toy would appear;</span>
    <span>And prisons would palaces prove</span>
    <span>If Jesus would dwell with me there.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-46-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Dear Lord, if indeed I am thine,</span>
    <span>If thou art my sun and my song,</span>
    <span>Say, why do I languish and pine,</span>
    <span>And why are my winters so long?</span>
    <span>O drive these dark clouds from my sky,</span>
    <span>Thy soul-cheering presence restore;</span>
    <span>Or take me unto thee on high,</span>
    <span>Where winter and clouds are no more.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-47." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">47.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Believer’s Safety.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Psalm xci.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-47-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Incarnate God! the soul that knows</span>
      <span class="i1">Thy name's mysterious power</span>
    <span>Shall dwell in undisturb'd repose,</span>
      <span class="i1">Nor fear the trying hour.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-47-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thy wisdom, faithfulness, and love,</span>
      <span class="i1">To feeble, helpless worms,</span>
    <span>A buckler and a refuge prove</span>
      <span class="i1">From enemies and storms.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-47-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>In vain the fowler spreads his net,</span>
      <span class="i1">To draw them from thy care;</span>
    <span>Thy timely call instructs their feet</span>
      <span class="i1">To shun the artful snare.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-47-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When, like a baneful pestilence,</span>
      <span class="i1">Sin mows its thousands down,</span>
    <span>On every side, without defence,</span>
      <span class="i1">Thy grace secures thine own.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-47-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>No midnight terrors haunt their bed,</span>
      <span class="i1">No arrow wounds by day;</span>
    <span>Unhurt on serpents they shall tread,</span>
      <span class="i1">If found in duty's way.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-47-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Angels, unseen, attend the saints,</span>
      <span class="i1">And bear them in their arms,</span>
    <span>To cheer the spirit when it faints,</span>
      <span class="i1">And guard their life from harms.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-47-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The angels' Lord himself is nigh</span>
      <span class="i1">To them that love his name,—</span>
    <span>Ready to save them when they cry,</span>
      <span class="i1">And put their foes to shame.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-47-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Crosses and changes are their lot</span>
      <span class="i1">Long as they sojourn here;</span>
    <span>But since their Saviour changes not,</span>
      <span class="i1">What have the saints to fear?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-48." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">48.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Another.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead"></p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-48-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>That man no guard or weapons needs</span>
    <span>Whose heart the blood of Jesus knows;</span>
    <span>But safe may pass, if duty leads,</span>
    <span>Through burning sands or mountain snows.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-48-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Released from guilt, he feels no fear;</span>
    <span>Redemption is his shield and tower;</span>
    <span>lie sees his Saviour always near</span>
    <span>To help in every trying hour.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-48-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Though I am weak, and Satan strong,</span>
    <span>And often to assault me tries,</span>
    <span>When Jesus is my shield and song,</span>
    <span>Abash'd the wolf before me flies.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-48-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>His love possessing, I am blest,</span>
    <span>Secure whatever change may come:</span>
    <span>Whether I go to east or west,</span>
    <span>With him I still shall be at home.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-48-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>If placed beneath the northern pole,</span>
    <span>Though winter reigns with rigour there,</span>
    <span>His gracious beams would cheer my soul,</span>
    <span>And make a spring throughout the year.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-48-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Or if the desert's sun-burnt soil</span>
    <span>My lonely dwelling e'er should prove,</span>
    <span>His presence would support my toil,</span>
    <span>Whose smile is life—whose voice is love.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-49." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">49.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">He led them by a right Way.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Psalm cvii, 7.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-49-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When Israel was from Egypt freed,</span>
      <span class="i1">The Lord, who brought them out,</span>
    <span>Help'd them in every time of need,</span>
      <span class="i1">But led them round about.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-49-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>To enter Canaan soon they hoped;</span>
      <span class="i1">But quickly changed their mind,</span>
    <span>When the Red sea their passage stopp'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">And Pharaoh march'd behind.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-49-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The desert fill'd them with alarms</span>
      <span class="i1">For water and for food;</span>
    <span>And Amalek, by force of arms,</span>
      <span class="i1">To check their progress stood.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-49-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>They often murmur'd by the way,</span>
      <span class="i1">Because they judged by sight;</span>
    <span>But were at length constrain'd to say,</span>
      <span class="i1">The Lord had led them right.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-49-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>In the Red sea, that stopp'd them first,</span>
      <span class="i1">Their enemies were drown'd;</span>
    <span>The rocks gave water for their thirst,</span>
      <span class="i1">And manna spread the ground.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-49-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>By fire and cloud their way was shown</span>
      <span class="i1">Across the pathless sands;</span>
    <span>And Amalek was overthrown</span>
      <span class="i1">By Moses' lifted hands.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-49-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The way was right their hearts to prove,</span>
      <span class="i1">To make God's glory known,</span>
    <span>And show his wisdom, pow'r, and love,</span>
      <span class="i1">Engaged to save his own.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-49-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Just so the true believer's path</span>
      <span class="i1">Through many dangers lies;</span>
    <span>Though dark to sense, 'tis light to faith,</span>
      <span class="i1">And leads us to the skies.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-50." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">50.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">What shall I render?.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Psalm cxvi, 12, 13.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-50-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>For mercies, countless as the sands,</span>
      <span class="i1">Which daily I receive</span>
    <span>From Jesus my Redeemer's hands,</span>
      <span class="i1">My soul, what canst thou give?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-50-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Alas! from such a heart as mine</span>
      <span class="i1">What can I bring him forth?</span>
    <span>My best is stain'd and dyed with sin,</span>
      <span class="i1">My all is nothing worth.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-50-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Yet this acknowledgment I'll make</span>
      <span class="i1">For all he has bestow'd—</span>
    <span>Salvation's sacred cup I'll take,</span>
      <span class="i1">And call upon my God.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-50-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The best returns for one like me,</span>
      <span class="i1">So wretched and so poor,</span>
    <span>Is from his gifts to draw a plea,</span>
      <span class="i1">And ask him still for more.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-50-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>I cannot serve him as I ought,</span>
      <span class="i1">No works have I to boast;</span>
    <span>Yet would I glory in the thought</span>
      <span class="i1">That I should owe him most.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-51." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">51.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Dwelling in Mesech.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Psalm cxx, 5–7.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-51-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>What a mournful life is mine,</span>
    <span>Fill'd with crosses, pains, and cares!</span>
    <span>Every work denied with sin,</span>
    <span>Every step beset with snares.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-51-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>If alone I pensive sit,</span>
    <span>I myself can hardly bear;</span>
    <span>If I pass along the street,</span>
    <span>Sin and riot triumph there.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-51-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Jesus! how my heart is pain'd,</span>
    <span>How it mourns for souls deceived,—</span>
    <span>When I hear thy name profaned,</span>
    <span>When I see thy Spirit grieved!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-51-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When thy children's griefs I view,</span>
    <span>Their distress becomes my own;</span>
    <span>All I hear or see or do</span>
    <span>Makes me tremble, weep, and groan.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-51-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Mourning thus I long had been</span>
    <span>When I heard my Saviour's voice:</span>
    <span>"Thou hast cause to mourn for sin,</span>
    <span>But in me thou may'st rejoice."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-51-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>This kind word dispell'd my grief,</span>
    <span>Put to silence my complaints;</span>
    <span>Though of sinners I am chief,</span>
    <span>He has rank'd me with his saints.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-51-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Though constrain'd to dwell a while</span>
    <span>Where the wicked strive and brawl,</span>
    <span>Let them frown,—so he but smile,</span>
    <span>Heav'n will make amends for all.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-51-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>There, believers, we shall rest,</span>
    <span>Free from sorrow, sin, and fears;</span>
    <span>Nothing there our peace molest</span>
    <span>Through eternal rounds of years.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-51-9>
 	<header>
 		<p>IX</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Let us then the fight endure.—</span>
    <span>See our Captain looking down:</span>
    <span>He will make the conquest sure,</span>
    <span>And bestow the promised crown.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-52." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">52.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Wisdom.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Prov. vii, 22-31.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-52-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Ere God had built the mountains,</span>
      <span class="i1">Or raised the fruitful hills,</span>
    <span>Before he fill'd the fountains</span>
      <span class="i1">That feed the running rills,</span>
    <span>In me, from everlasting,</span>
      <span class="i1">The wonderful I AM</span>
    <span>Found pleasures never wasting,</span>
      <span class="i1">And Wisdom is my name.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-52-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When, like a tent to dwell in,</span>
      <span class="i1">He spread the skies abroad,</span>
    <span>And swathed about the swelling</span>
      <span class="i1">Of ocean's mighty flood,</span>
    <span>He wrought by weight and measure;</span>
      <span class="i1">And I was with him then;—</span>
    <span>Myself the Father's pleasure,</span>
      <span class="i1">And mine the sons of men.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-52-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus Wisdom's words discover</span>
      <span class="i1">Thy glory and thy grace,</span>
    <span>Thou everlasting lover</span>
      <span class="i1">Of our unworthy race!</span>
    <span>Thy gracious eye survey'd us</span>
      <span class="i1">Ere stars were seen above:</span>
    <span>In wisdom thou hast made us,</span>
      <span class="i1">And died for us in love.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-52-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>And couldst thou be delighted</span>
      <span class="i1">With creatures such as we!</span>
    <span>Who, when we saw thee slighted</span>
      <span class="i1">And nail'd thee to a tree!</span>
    <span>Unfathomable wonder,</span>
      <span class="i1">And mystery divine,</span>
    <span>The voice that speaks in thunder,</span>
      <span class="i1">Says, "Sinner, I am thine!"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-53." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">53.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">A Friend that sticketh closer than a Brother.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Prov. xviii, 24.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-53-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>One there is, above all others,</span>
      <span class="i1">Well deserves the name of Friend!</span>
    <span>His is love beyond a brother's,</span>
      <span class="i1">Costly, free, and knows no end:</span>
      <span class="i1">They who once his kindness prove,</span>
      <span class="i1">find it everlasting love!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-53-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Which of all our friends, to save us,</span>
      <span class="i1">Could or would have shed their blood?</span>
    <span>But our Jesus died to have us</span>
      <span class="i1">Reconciled in him to God:</span>
      <span class="i1">This was boundless love indeed!</span>
      <span class="i1">Jesus is a Friend in need.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-53-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Men, when raised to lofty stations,</span>
      <span class="i1">Often know their friends no more;</span>
    <span>Slight and scorn their poor relations,</span>
      <span class="i1">Though they valued them before:</span>
      <span class="i1">But our Saviour always owns</span>
      <span class="i1">Those whom he redeem'd with groans.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-53-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When he lived on earth abased,</span>
      <span class="i1">Friend of sinners was his name;</span>
    <span>Now above all glory raised,</span>
      <span class="i1">He rejoices in the same:</span>
      <span class="i1">Still he calls them brethren, friends,</span>
      <span class="i1">And to all their wants attends.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-53-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Could we bear from one another</span>
      <span class="i1">What he daily bears from us?</span>
    <span>Yet this glorious Friend and Brother</span>
      <span class="i1">Loves us though we treat him thus:</span>
      <span class="i1">Though for good we render ill,</span>
      <span class="i1">He accounts us brethren still.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-53-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>O for grace our hearts to soften!</span>
      <span class="i1">Teach us, Lord, at length to love;</span>
    <span>We, alas! forget too often</span>
      <span class="i1">What a Friend we have above:</span>
      <span class="i1">But when home our souls are brought,</span>
      <span class="i1">We will love thee as we ought.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-54." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">54.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Vanity of Life.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Eccles. i, 2.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-54-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The evils that beset our path,</span>
      <span class="i1">Who can prevent or cure?</span>
    <span>We stand upon the brink of death</span>
      <span class="i1">When most we seem secure.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-54-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>If we to-day sweet peace possess,</span>
      <span class="i1">It soon may be withdrawn;</span>
    <span>Some change may plunge us in distress</span>
      <span class="i1">Before to-morrow's dawn.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-54-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Disease and pain invade our health,</span>
      <span class="i1">And find an easy prey;</span>
    <span>And oft, when least expected, wealth</span>
      <span class="i1">Takes wings and flies away.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-54-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>A fever or a blow can shake</span>
      <span class="i1">Our wisdom's boasted rule,</span>
    <span>And of the brightest genius make</span>
      <span class="i1">A madman or a fool.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-54-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The gourds from which we look for fruit</span>
      <span class="i1">Produce us only pain;</span>
    <span>A worm unseen attacks the root,</span>
      <span class="i1">And all our hopes are vain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-54-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>I pity those who seek no more</span>
      <span class="i1">Than such a world can give;</span>
    <span>Wretched they are and blind and poor,</span>
      <span class="i1">And dying while they live.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-54-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Since sin has fill'd the earth with woe,</span>
      <span class="i1">And creatures fade and die,</span>
    <span>Lord, wean our hearts from things below,</span>
      <span class="i1">And fix our hopes on high.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-55." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">55.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Vanity of the World.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead"></p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-55-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>God gives his mercies to be spent;</span>
    <span>Your hoard will do your soul no good;</span>
    <span>Gold is a blessing only lent,</span>
    <span>Repaid by giving others food.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-55-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The world's esteem is but a bribe;</span>
    <span>To buy their peace you sell your own,</span>
    <span>The slave of a vain-glorious tribe.</span>
    <span>Who hate you while they make you known.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-55-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The joy that vain amusements give,</span>
    <span>Oh, sad conclusion that it brings!</span>
    <span>The honey of a crowded hive,</span>
    <span>Defended by a thousand stings.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-55-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>'Tis thus the world rewards the fools</span>
    <span>That live upon her treach'rous smiles:</span>
    <span>She leads them blindfold by her rules,</span>
    <span>And ruins all whom she beguiles.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-55-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>God knows the thousands who go down</span>
    <span>From pleasure into endless woe,</span>
    <span>And with a long despairing groan</span>
    <span>Blaspheme their Maker as they go.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-55-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>O fearful thought! be timely wise;</span>
    <span>Delight but in a Saviour's charms.</span>
    <span>And God shall take you to the skies.</span>
    <span>Embraced in everlasting arms.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-56." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">56.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Vanity of the Creature Sanctified.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead"></p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-56-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Honey though the bee prepares,</span>
    <span>An envenom'd sting he wears;</span>
    <span>Piercing thorns a guard compose</span>
    <span>Round the fragrant blooming rose.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-56-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Where we think to find a sweet,</span>
    <span>Oft a painful sting we meet;</span>
    <span>When the rose invites our eye,</span>
    <span>We forget the thorn is nigh.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-56-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Why are thus our hopes beguiled?</span>
    <span>Why are all our pleasures spoil'd?</span>
    <span>Why do agony and woe</span>
    <span>From our choicest comforts grow?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-56-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Sin has been the cause of all!</span>
    <span>'Twas not thus before the fall:</span>
    <span>What but pain and thorn and sting</span>
    <span>From the root of sin can spring?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-56-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Now with every good we find</span>
    <span>Vanity and grief entwined;</span>
    <span>What we feel or what we fear</span>
    <span>All our joys embitter here.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-56-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Yet, through the Redeemer's love,</span>
    <span>These afflictions blessings prove;</span>
    <span>He the wounding stings and thorns</span>
    <span>Into healing med'cines turns.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-56-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>From the earth our hearts they wean,</span>
    <span>Teach us on his arm to lean;</span>
    <span>Urge us to a throne of grace;</span>
    <span>Make us seek a resting-place.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-56-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>In the mansions of our King</span>
    <span>Sweets abound without a sting;</span>
    <span>Thornless there the roses blow,</span>
    <span>And the joys unmingled flow,</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-57." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">57.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Name of Jesus.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Cant. i, 3.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-57-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>How sweet the name of Jesus sounds</span>
      <span class="i1">In a believer's ear!</span>
    <span>It soothes his sorrows, heals his wounds,</span>
      <span class="i1">And drives away his fear.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-57-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>It makes the wounded spirit whole,</span>
      <span class="i1">And calms the troubl'd breast;</span>
    <span>'Tis manna to the hungry soul,</span>
      <span class="i1">And to the weary rest.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-57-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Dear name! the rock on which I build,</span>
      <span class="i1">My shield and hiding-place</span>
    <span>My never-failing treas'ry, fill'd</span>
      <span class="i1">With boundless stores of grace.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-57-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>By thee my pray'rs acceptance gain,</span>
      <span class="i1">Although with sin defiled;</span>
    <span>Satan accuses me in vain,</span>
      <span class="i1">And I am own'd a child.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-57-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Jesus! my Shepherd, Husband, Friend,</span>
      <span class="i1">My Prophet, Priest, and King;</span>
    <span>My Lord, my life, my way, my end,</span>
      <span class="i1">Accept the praise I bring.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-57-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Weak is the effort of my heart,</span>
      <span class="i1">And cold my warmest thought;</span>
    <span>But when I see thee as thou art</span>
      <span class="i1">I'll praise thee as I ought.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-57-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Till then I would thy love proclaim</span>
      <span class="i1">With every fleeting breath;</span>
    <span>And may the music of thy name</span>
      <span class="i1">Refresh my soul in death.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-58." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">58.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">O Lord, I will praise thee.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Isa. xii.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-58-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>I will praise thee every day,</span>
    <span>Now thine anger's turn'd away!</span>
    <span>Comfortable thoughts arise</span>
    <span>From the bleeding sacrifice.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-58-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Here, in the fair gospel field,</span>
    <span>Wells of free salvation yield</span>
    <span>Streams of life, a plenteous store,</span>
    <span>And my soul shall thirst no more.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-58-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Jesus is become at length</span>
    <span>My salvation and my strength;</span>
    <span>And his praises shall prolong,</span>
    <span>While I live, my pleasant song.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-58-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Praise ye then his glorious name,</span>
    <span>Publish his exalted fame!</span>
    <span>Still his worth your praise exceeds,</span>
    <span>Excellent are all his deeds.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-58-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Raise again the joyful sound,</span>
    <span>Let the nations roll it round!</span>
    <span>Zion, shout, for this is he,</span>
    <span>God the Saviour dwells in thee.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-59." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">59.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Refuge, River, and Rock of the Church.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Isa. xxxii, 2.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-59-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>He who on earth as man was known,</span>
      <span class="i1">And bore our sins and pains,</span>
    <span>Now, seated on the eternal throne,</span>
      <span class="i1">The God of glory reigns.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-59-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>His hands the wheels of nature guide</span>
      <span class="i1">With an unerring skill;</span>
    <span>And countless worlds extended wide</span>
      <span class="i1">Obey his sovereign will.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-59-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>While harps unnumber'd sound his praise</span>
      <span class="i1">In yonder world above,</span>
    <span>His saints on earth admire his ways,</span>
      <span class="i1">And glory in his love.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-59-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>His righteousness to faith reveal’d,</span>
      <span class="i1">Wrought out for guilty worms,</span>
    <span>Affords a hiding-place and shield</span>
      <span class="i1">From enemies and storms.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-59-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>This land, through which his pilgrims go,</span>
      <span class="i1">Is desolate and dry;</span>
    <span>But streams of grace from him o'erflow,</span>
      <span class="i1">Their thirst to satisfy.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-59-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When troubles, like a burning sun,</span>
      <span class="i1">Beat heavy on their head,</span>
    <span>To this almighty Rock they run,</span>
      <span class="i1">And find a pleasing shade.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-59-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>How glorious he! how happy they</span>
      <span class="i1">In such a glorious Friend!</span>
    <span>Whose love secures them all the way,</span>
      <span class="i1">And crowns them at the end.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-60." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">60.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Zion; or the City of God.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Isa. xxxiii, 20, 21.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-60-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Glorious things of thee are spoken,</span>
    <span>Zion, city of our God!</span>
    <span>He, whose word cannot be broken,</span>
    <span>Form'd thee for his own abode:</span>
    <span>On the Rock of ages founded,</span>
    <span>What can shake thy sure repose?</span>
    <span>With salvation's walls surrounded,</span>
    <span>Thou may'st smile at all thy foes.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-60-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>See! the streams of living waters</span>
    <span>Springing from eternal love,</span>
    <span>Well supply thy sons and daughters,</span>
    <span>And all fear of want remove:</span>
    <span>Who can faint while such a river</span>
    <span>Ever flows their thirst t' assuage?</span>
    <span>Grace, which, like the Lord, the giver,</span>
    <span>Never fails from age to age.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-60-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Round each habitation hov'ring,</span>
    <span>See the cloud and fire appear!</span>
    <span>For a glory and a cov'ring,</span>
    <span>Showing that the Lord is near:</span>
    <span>Thus deriving from their banner</span>
    <span>Light by night, and shade by day;</span>
    <span>Safe they feed upon the manna</span>
    <span>Which he gives them when they pray.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-60-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Bless'd inhabitants of Zion,</span>
    <span>Wash'd in the Redeemer's blood!</span>
    <span>Jesus, whom their souls rely on,</span>
    <span>Makes them kings and priests to God;</span>
    <span>'Tis his love his people raises</span>
    <span>Over self to reign as kings,</span>
    <span>And as priests his solemn praises</span>
    <span>Each for a thank-off'ring brings.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-60-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Saviour, if of Zion's city</span>
    <span>I through grace a member am,</span>
    <span>Let the world deride or pity—</span>
    <span>I will glory in thy name:</span>
    <span>Fading is the worldling's pleasure,—</span>
    <span>All his boasted pomp and show;</span>
    <span>Solid joys and lasting treasure</span>
    <span>None but Zion's children know.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-61." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">61.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Look unto me, and be ye saved.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Isa. xlv, 22.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-61-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>As the serpent raised by Moses</span>
    <span>Heal'd the burning serpent's bite,</span>
    <span>Jesus thus himself discloses</span>
    <span>To the wounded sinner's sight:</span>
    <span>Hear his gracious invitation,</span>
    <span>"I have life and peace to give,—</span>
    <span>I have wrought out full salvation;</span>
    <span>Sinner, look to me and live.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-61-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Pore upon your sins no longer,</span>
    <span>Well I know their mighty guilt;</span>
    <span>But my love than death is stronger,</span>
    <span>I my blood have freely spilt:</span>
    <span>Though your heart has long been harden'd,</span>
    <span>Look on me—it soft shall grow;</span>
    <span>Past transgressions shall be pardon'd,</span>
    <span>And I'll wash you white as snow.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-61-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"I have seen what you were doing,</span>
    <span>Though you little thought of me;</span>
    <span>You were madly bent on ruin,</span>
    <span>But I said—It shall not be:</span>
    <span>You had been for ever wretched,</span>
    <span>Had I not espoused your part;</span>
    <span>Now behold my arms outstretched</span>
    <span>To receive you to my heart.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-61-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Well may shame and joy and wonder</span>
    <span>All your inward passions move;</span>
    <span>I could crush thee with my thunder,</span>
    <span>But I speak to thee in love:</span>
    <span>See! your sins are all forgiven,—</span>
    <span>I have paid the countless sum!</span>
    <span>Now my death has open'd heaven,</span>
    <span>Thither you shall shortly come."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-61-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Dearest Saviour, we adore thee</span>
    <span>For thy precious life and death;</span>
    <span>Melt each stubborn heart before thee,</span>
    <span>Give us all the eye of faith:</span>
    <span>From the law's condemning sentence,</span>
    <span>To thy mercy we appeal;</span>
    <span>Thou alone canst give repentance,</span>
    <span>Thou alone our souls canst heal.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-62." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">62.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The good Physician.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead"></p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-62-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>How lost was my condition</span>
      <span class="i1">Till Jesus made me whole!</span>
    <span>There is but one Physician</span>
      <span class="i1">Can cure a sin-sick soul!</span>
    <span>Next door to death he found me,</span>
      <span class="i1">And snatch'd me from the grave</span>
    <span>To tell to all around me</span>
      <span class="i1">His wondrous power to save.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-62-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The worst of all diseases</span>
      <span class="i1">Is light compared with sin;</span>
    <span>On every part it seizes,</span>
      <span class="i1">But rages most within:</span>
    <span>'Tis palsy, dropsy, fever,</span>
      <span class="i1">And madness—all combined;</span>
    <span>And none but a believer</span>
      <span class="i1">The least relief can find.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-62-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>From men great skill professing</span>
      <span class="i1">I thought a cure to gain;</span>
    <span>But this proved more distressing,</span>
      <span class="i1">And added to my pain:</span>
    <span>Some said that nothing ail'd me,</span>
      <span class="i1">Some gave me up for lost;</span>
    <span>Thus every refuge fail'd me,</span>
      <span class="i1">And all my hopes were cross'd.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-62-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>At length this great Physician,</span>
      <span class="i1">How matchless is his grace!</span>
    <span>Accepted my petition,</span>
      <span class="i1">And undertook my case;</span>
    <span>First gave me sight to view him,</span>
      <span class="i1">For sin my sight had seal'd,</span>
    <span>Then bid me look unto him,—</span>
      <span class="i1">I look'd, and I was heal'd.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-62-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>A dying, risen Jesus,</span>
      <span class="i1">Seen by the eye of faith,</span>
    <span>At once from anguish frees us,</span>
      <span class="i1">And saves the soul from death:</span>
    <span>Come then to this Physician,</span>
      <span class="i1">His help he'll freely give,</span>
    <span>He makes no hard condition,</span>
      <span class="i1">'Tis only—look and live.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-63." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">63.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">To the Afflicted, tossed with Tempests, and not Comforted.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Isa. liv, 5-11.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-63-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Pensive, doubting, fearful heart,</span>
    <span>Hear what Christ the Saviour says;</span>
    <span>Every word should joy impart,</span>
    <span>Change thy mourning into praise:</span>
    <span>Yes, he speaks, and speaks to thee,</span>
    <span>May he help thee to believe!</span>
    <span>Then thou presently wilt see,</span>
    <span>Thou hast little cause to grieve.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-63-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Fear thou not, nor be ashamed,</span>
    <span>All thy sorrows soon shall end:</span>
    <span>I who heaven and earth have framed</span>
    <span>Am thy Husband and thy Friend:</span>
    <span>I the High and Holy One,</span>
    <span>Isr'el's God by all adored,</span>
    <span>As thy Saviour will be known,</span>
    <span>Thy Redeemer and thy Lord.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-63-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>For a moment I withdrew,</span>
    <span>And thy heart was fill'd with pain;</span>
    <span>But my mercies I'll renew,—</span>
    <span>Thou shalt soon rejoice again:</span>
    <span>Though I seem to hide my face,</span>
    <span>Yery soon my wrath shall cease;</span>
    <span>'Tis but for a moment's space,</span>
    <span>Ending in eternal peace.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-63-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When my peaceful bow appears,</span>
    <span>Painted on the wat'ry cloud;</span>
    <span>'Tis to dissipate thy fears,</span>
    <span>Lest the earth should be o'erflow'd:</span>
    <span>'Tis an emblem too of grace,</span>
    <span>Of my cov'nant love a sign;</span>
    <span>Though the mountains leave their place,</span>
    <span>Thou shalt be for ever mine.</span>
