 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-63-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Though afflicted, tempest-toss'd.</span>
    <span>Comfortless awhile thou art,</span>
    <span>Do not think thou canst be lost,</span>
    <span>Thou art graven on my heart:</span>
    <span>All thy wastes I will repair,</span>
    <span>Thou shalt be rebuilt anew;</span>
    <span>And in thee it shall appear</span>
    <span>What a God of love can do.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-64." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">64.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The contrite Heart.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Isa. lvii, 15.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-64-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The Lord will happiness divine</span>
      <span class="i1">On contrite hearts bestow:</span>
    <span>Then tell me, gracious God, is mine</span>
      <span class="i1">A contrite heart or no?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-64-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>I hear, but seem to hear in vain,</span>
      <span class="i1">Insensible as steel;</span>
    <span>If aught is felt, 'tis only pain</span>
      <span class="i1">To find I cannot feel.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-64-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>I sometimes think myself inclined</span>
      <span class="i1">To love thee, if I could;</span>
    <span>But often feel another mind,</span>
      <span class="i1">Averse to all that's good.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-64-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>My best desires are faint and few,</span>
      <span class="i1">I fain would strive for more;</span>
    <span>But when I cry, "My strength renew,"</span>
      <span class="i1">Seem weaker than before.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-64-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thy saints are comforted, I know,</span>
      <span class="i1">And love thy house of prayer;</span>
    <span>I therefore go where others go,</span>
      <span class="i1">But find no comfort there.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-64-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>O make this heart rejoice or ache,</span>
      <span class="i1">Decide this doubt for me;</span>
    <span>And if it be not broken break,</span>
      <span class="i1">And heal it if it be.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-65." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">65.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The future Peace and Glory of the Church.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Isa. lx, 15-20.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-65-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Hear what God the Lord hath spoken:</span>
    <span>"O my people, faint and few,</span>
    <span>Comfortless, afflicted, broken,</span>
    <span>Fair abodes I build for you;</span>
    <span>Thorns of heart-felt tribulation</span>
    <span>Shall no more perplex your ways;</span>
    <span>You shall name your walls Salvation,</span>
    <span>And your gates shall all be Praise.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-65-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>There, like streams that feed the garden,</span>
    <span>Pleasures without end shall flow;</span>
    <span>For the Lord, your faith rewarding,</span>
    <span>All his bounty shall bestow:</span>
    <span>Still in undisturb'd possession</span>
    <span>Peace and righteousness shall reign;</span>
    <span>Never shall you feel oppression,—</span>
    <span>Hear the voice of war again.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-65-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Ye no more your suns descending,</span>
    <span>Waning moons no more shall see;</span>
    <span>But, your griefs for ever ending,</span>
    <span>Find eternal noon in me:</span>
    <span>God shall rise, and shining o'er you,</span>
    <span>Change to day the gloom of night;</span>
    <span>He the Lord, shall be your glory,</span>
    <span>God your everlasting light."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-66." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">66.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Trust of the Wicked and the Righteous compared.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Jer. xvii, 5-8.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-66-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>As parched in the barren sands,</span>
      <span class="i1">Beneath a burning sky,</span>
    <span>The worthless bramble with'ring stands,</span>
      <span class="i1">And only grows to die;</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-66-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Such is the sinner's awful case,</span>
      <span class="i1">Who makes the world his trust,</span>
    <span>And dares his confidence to place</span>
      <span class="i1">In vanity and dust.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-66-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>A secret curse destroys his root,</span>
      <span class="i1">And dries his moisture up;</span>
    <span>He lives awhile, but bears no fruit,</span>
      <span class="i1">Then dies without a hope.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-66-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But happy he whose hopes depend</span>
      <span class="i1">Upon the Lord alone;</span>
    <span>The soul that trusts in such a Friend</span>
      <span class="i1">Can ne'er be overthrown.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-66-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Though gourds should wither, cisterns break.</span>
      <span class="i1">And creature-comforts die,</span>
    <span>No change his solid hope can shake,</span>
      <span class="i1">Or stop his sure supply.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-66-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>So thrives and blooms the tree whose roots</span>
      <span class="i1">By constant streams are fed;</span>
    <span>Array'd in green, and rich in fruits,</span>
      <span class="i1">It rears its branching head.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-66-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>It thrives though rain should be denied,</span>
      <span class="i1">And drought around prevail;</span>
    <span>'Tis planted by a river side</span>
      <span class="i1">Whose waters cannot fail.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-67." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">67.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Jehovah our Righteousness.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Jer. xxiii, 6.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-67-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>My God, how perfect are thy ways!</span>
      <span class="i1">But mine polluted are;</span>
    <span>Sin twines itself about my praise,</span>
      <span class="i1">And slides into my prayer.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-67-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When I would speak what thou hast done</span>
      <span class="i1">To save me from my sin,</span>
    <span>I cannot make thy mercies known</span>
      <span class="i1">But self-applause creeps in.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-67-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Divine desire, that holy flame,</span>
      <span class="i1">Thy grace creates in me;</span>
    <span>Alas! impatience is its name</span>
      <span class="i1">When it returns to thee.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-67-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>This heart, a fountain of vile thoughts,</span>
      <span class="i1">How does it overflow!</span>
    <span>While self upon the surface floats,</span>
      <span class="i1">Still bubbling from below.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-67-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Let others in the gaudy dress</span>
      <span class="i1">Of fancied merits shine,</span>
    <span>The Lord shall be my righteousness,</span>
      <span class="i1">The Lord for ever mine.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-68." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">68.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Ephrain Repenting.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Jer. xxxi, 18-20.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-68-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>My God, till I received thy stroke,</span>
      <span class="i1">How like a beast was I!</span>
    <span>So unaccustom'd to the yoke,</span>
      <span class="i1">So backward to comply.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-68-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>With grief my just reproach I bear,</span>
      <span class="i1">Shame fills me at the thought;</span>
    <span>How frequent my rebellions were!</span>
      <span class="i1">What wickedness I wrought!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-68-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>3 Thy merciful restraint I scorn'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">And left the pleasant road;</span>
    <span>Yet turn me, and I shall be turn'd:</span>
      <span class="i1">Thou art the Lord my God.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-68-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Is Ephraim banish'd from my thoughts,</span>
      <span class="i1">Or vile in my esteem?</span>
    <span>No, saith the Lord, with all his faults</span>
      <span class="i1">I still remember him.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-68-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Is he a dear and pleasant child?</span>
      <span class="i1">Yes, dear and pleasant still;</span>
    <span>Though sin his foolish heart beguiled.</span>
      <span class="i1">And he withstood my will.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-68-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>My sharp rebuke has laid him low,</span>
      <span class="i1">He seeks my face again;</span>
    <span>My pity kindles at his woe,</span>
      <span class="i1">He shall not seek in vain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-69." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">69.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Lord is my Portion.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Lam. iii, 24.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-69-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>1 From pole to pole let others roam,</span>
      <span class="i1">And search in vain for bliss;</span>
    <span>My soul is satisfied at home,</span>
      <span class="i1">The Lord my portion is.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-69-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Jesus, who on his glorious throne,</span>
      <span class="i1">Rules heaven and earth and sea,</span>
    <span>Is pleased to claim me for his own,</span>
      <span class="i1">And give himself to me.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-69-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>His person fixes all my love,</span>
      <span class="i1">His blood removes my fear;</span>
    <span>And while he pleads for me above,</span>
      <span class="i1">His arm preserves me here.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-69-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>His word of promise is my food,</span>
      <span class="i1">His Spirit is my guide;</span>
    <span>Thus daily is my strength renewed,</span>
      <span class="i1">And all my wants supplied.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-69-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>5 For him I count as gain each loss,</span>
      <span class="i1">Disgrace for him renown;</span>
    <span>Well may I glory in his cross,</span>
      <span class="i1">While he prepares my crown!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-69-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Let worldlings then indulge their boast,</span>
      <span class="i1">How much they gain or spend;</span>
    <span>Their joys must soon give up the ghost,</span>
      <span class="i1">But mine shall know no end.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-70." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">70.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Humbled and silenced by Mercy.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Ezek. xvi, 63.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-70-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Once perishing in blood I lay;</span>
      <span class="i1">Creatures no help could give;</span>
    <span>But Jesus pass'd me in the way,</span>
      <span class="i1">He saw, and bade me live.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-70-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Though Satan still his rule maintain'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">And all his arts employ'd;</span>
    <span>That mighty word his rage restrain'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">I could not be destroy'd.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-70-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>At length the time of love arrived,</span>
      <span class="i1">When I my Lord should know;</span>
    <span>Then Satan, of his power deprived,</span>
      <span class="i1">Was forced to let me go.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-70-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>O can I e'er that day forget,</span>
      <span class="i1">When Jesus kindly spoke!</span>
    <span>"Poor soul, my blood has paid thy debt,</span>
      <span class="i1">And now I break thy yoke.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-70-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Henceforth I take thee for my own,</span>
      <span class="i1">And give myself to thee;</span>
    <span>Forsake the idols thou hast known,</span>
      <span class="i1">And yield thy heart to me."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-70-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Ah, worthless heart! it promised fair,</span>
      <span class="i1">And said it would be thine;</span>
    <span>I little thought it e'er would dare</span>
      <span class="i1">Again with idols join.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-70-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Lord, dost thou such backslidings heal,</span>
      <span class="i1">And pardon all that's past?</span>
    <span>Sure, if I am not made of steel,</span>
      <span class="i1">Thou hast prevail'd at last.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-70-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>My tongue, which rashly spoke before,</span>
      <span class="i1">This mercy will restrain;</span>
    <span>Surely I now shall boast no more,</span>
      <span class="i1">Nor censure, nor complain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-71." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">71.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Covenant.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Ezek. xxxvi, 25-28.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-71-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The Lord proclaims his grace abroad!</span>
    <span>"Behold, I change your hearts of stone;</span>
    <span>Each shall renounce his idol-god,</span>
    <span>And serve, henceforth, the Lord alone.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-71-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"My grace, a flowing stream, proceeds</span>
    <span>To wash your filthiness away;</span>
    <span>Ye shall abhor your former deeds,</span>
    <span>And learn my statutes to obey.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-71-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"My truth the great design ensures,</span>
    <span>I give myself away to you;</span>
    <span>You shall be mine, I will be yours,</span>
    <span>Your God unalterably true.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-71-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Yet not unsought or unimplored</span>
    <span>The plenteous grace shall I confer;</span>
    <span>No—your whole hearts shall seek the Lord,</span>
    <span>I'll put a praying spirit there.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-71-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"From the first breath of life divine,</span>
    <span>Down to the last expiring hour,</span>
    <span>The gracious work shall all be mine,</span>
    <span>Begun and ended in my power."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-72" epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">72</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Jehovah-Shammah.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Ezek. xlviii, 35.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-72-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>As birds their infant brood protect,</span>
    <span>And spread their wings to shelter them;</span>
    <span>Thus saith the Lord to his elect,</span>
    <span>"So will I guard Jerusalem."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-72-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>And what then is Jerusalem—</span>
    <span>This darling object of his care?</span>
    <span>Where is its worth in God's esteem?</span>
    <span>Who built it? who inhabits there?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-72-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Jehovah founded it in blood.</span>
    <span>The blood of his incarnate Son;</span>
    <span>There dwell the saints, once foes to God—</span>
    <span>The sinners whom he calls his own.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-72-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>There, though besieged on every side,</span>
    <span>Yet much beloved and guarded well,</span>
    <span>From age to age they have defied</span>
    <span>The utmost force of earth and hell.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-72-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Let earth repent and hell despair,</span>
    <span>This city has a sure defence;</span>
    <span>Her name is call'd "The Lord is there,"</span>
    <span>And who has power to drive him thence?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-73." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">73.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Power and Triumph of Faith.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Dan. iii, 6.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-73-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Supported by the word,</span>
      <span class="i1">Though in himself a worm,</span>
      <span class="i1">The servant of the Lord</span>
      <span class="i1">Can wondrous acts perform:</span>
    <span>Without dismay he boldly treads</span>
    <span>Where'er the path of duty leads.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-73-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">The haughty king in vain,</span>
      <span class="i1">With fury on his brow,</span>
      <span class="i1">Believers would constrain</span>
      <span class="i1">To golden gods to bow:</span>
    <span>The furnace could not make them fear,</span>
    <span>Because they knew the Lord was near.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-73-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">As vain was the decree</span>
      <span class="i1">Which charged them not to pray:</span>
      <span class="i1">Daniel still bow'd his knee,</span>
      <span class="i1">And worshipp'd thrice a day.</span>
    <span>Trusting in God, he fear'd not men,</span>
    <span>Though threaten'd with the lions' den.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-73-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Secure they might refuse</span>
      <span class="i1">Compliance with such laws;</span>
      <span class="i1">For what had they to lose</span>
      <span class="i1">When God espoused their cause?</span>
    <span>He made the hungry lions crouch;</span>
    <span>Nor durst the fire his children touch.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-73-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">The Lord is still the same,</span>
      <span class="i1">A mighty shield and tower,</span>
      <span class="i1">And they who trust his name</span>
      <span class="i1">Are guarded by his power;</span>
    <span>He can the rage of lions tame,</span>
    <span>And bear them harmless through the flame.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-73-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Yet we too often shrink</span>
      <span class="i1">When trials are in view,</span>
      <span class="i1">Expecting we must sink,</span>
      <span class="i1">And never can get through:</span>
    <span>But could we once believe indeed,</span>
    <span>From all these fears we should be freed.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-74." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">74.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Belshazzar.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Dan. v, 5, 6.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-74-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Poor sinners! little do they think</span>
      <span class="i1">With whom they have to do!</span>
    <span>But stand securely on the brink</span>
      <span class="i1">Of everlasting woe.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-74-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Belshazzar thus, profanely bold,</span>
      <span class="i1">The Lord of hosts defied;</span>
    <span>But vengeance soon his boasts control'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">And humbled all his pride.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-74-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>He saw a hand upon the wall</span>
      <span class="i1">(And trembled on his throne),</span>
    <span>Which wrote his sudden dreadful fall</span>
      <span class="i1">In characters unknown.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-74-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Why should he tremble at the view</span>
      <span class="i1">Of what he could not read?</span>
    <span>Foreboding conscience quickly knew</span>
      <span class="i1">His ruin was decreed.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-74-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>See him o'erwhelm'd with deep distress;</span>
      <span class="i1">His eyes with anguish roll;</span>
    <span>His looks and loosen'd joints express</span>
      <span class="i1">The terrors of his soul.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-74-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>His pomp and music, guests and wine,</span>
      <span class="i1">No more delight afford:</span>
    <span>O sinner, ere this case be thine,</span>
      <span class="i1">Begin to seek the Lord.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-74-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The law like this hand-writing stands,</span>
      <span class="i1">And speaks the wrath of God;</span>
    <span>But Jesus answers its demands,</span>
      <span class="i1">And cancels it with blood.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-75." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">75.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Gourd.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Jonah, iv, 6-8.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-75-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>As once for Jonah, so the Lord,</span>
    <span>To sooth and cheer my mournful hours,</span>
    <span>Prepared for me a pleasing gourd,</span>
    <span>Cool was its shade, and sweet its flowers.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-75-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>To prize this gift was surely right;</span>
    <span>But through the folly of my heart,</span>
    <span>It hid the Giver from my sight,</span>
    <span>And soon my joy was changed to smart.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-75-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>While I admired its beauteous form,</span>
    <span>Its pleasant shade and grateful fruit,</span>
    <span>The Lord, displeased, sent forth a worm,</span>
    <span>Unseen to prey upon the root.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-75-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>I trembled when I saw it fade,</span>
    <span>But guilt restrain'd the murm'ring word;</span>
    <span>My folly I confess'd, and pray'd—</span>
    <span>Forgive my sin, and spare my gourd.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-75-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>His wondrous love can ne'er be told,—</span>
    <span>He heard me and relieved my pain;</span>
    <span>His word the threat'ning worm control'd,</span>
    <span>And bid my gourd revive again.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-75-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Now, Lord, my gourd is mine no more,</span>
    <span>'Tis thine, who only couldst it raise;</span>
    <span>The idol of my heart before</span>
    <span>Henceforth shall flourish to thy praise.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-76." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">76.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Prayer for the Lord’s promised Presence.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Zech. ii, 10.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-76-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Son of God, thy people shield!</span>
    <span>Must we still thine absence mourn?</span>
    <span>Let thy promise be fulfill'd,</span>
    <span>Thou hast said, "I will return!"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-76-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Gracious leader, now appear,</span>
    <span>Shine upon us with thy light!</span>
    <span>Like the spring, when thou art near,</span>
    <span>Days and suns are doubly bright.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-76-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>As a mother counts the days</span>
    <span>Till her absent son she see,</span>
    <span>Longs and watches, weeps and prays,</span>
    <span>So our spirits long for thee.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-76-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Come and let us feel thee nigh,</span>
    <span>Then thy sheep shall feed in peace;</span>
    <span>Plenty bless us from on high,</span>
    <span>Evil from amongst us cease.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-76-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>With thy love and voice and aid,</span>
    <span>Thou canst every care assuage;</span>
    <span>Then we shall not be afraid,</span>
    <span>Though the world and Satan rage.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-76-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus each day for thee we'll spend,</span>
    <span>While our callings we pursue;</span>
    <span>And the thoughts of such a friend</span>
    <span>Shall each night our joy renew.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-76-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Let thy light be ne'er withdrawn,</span>
    <span>Golden days afford us long!</span>
    <span>Thus we pray at early dawn,</span>
    <span>This shall be our evening song.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-77." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">77.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">A Brand plucked out of the Fire.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Zech. iii, 1-5.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-77-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>With Satan, my accuser, near,</span>
    <span>My spirit trembled when I saw</span>
    <span>The Lord in majesty appear,</span>
    <span>And heard the language of his law.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-77-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>In vain I wish'd and strove to hide</span>
    <span>The tatter'd filthy rags I wore:</span>
    <span>While my fierce foe insulting cried,</span>
    <span>"See what you trusted in before!"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-77-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Struck dumb, and left without a plea,</span>
    <span>I heard my gracious Saviour say,</span>
    <span>"Know, Satan, I this sinner free,—</span>
    <span>I died to take his sins away.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-77-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"This is a brand which I in love</span>
    <span>To save from wrath and sin design;</span>
    <span>In vain thy accusations prove;</span>
    <span>I answer all, and claim him mine."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-77-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>At this rebuke the tempter fled;</span>
    <span>Then He removed my filthy dress;</span>
    <span>"Poor sinner, take this robe," He said,</span>
    <span>"It is thy Saviour's righteousness.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-77-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"And see a crown of life prepared!</span>
    <span>That I might thus thy head adorn;</span>
    <span>I thought no shame of suff'ring hard,</span>
    <span>But wore for thee a crown of thorn."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-77-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>O, how I heard these gracious words!</span>
    <span>They broke and heal'd my heart at once;</span>
    <span>Constrained me to become the Lord's,</span>
    <span>And all my idol-gods renounce.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-77-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Now, Satan, thou hast lost thy aim;</span>
    <span>Against this brand thy threats are vain;</span>
    <span>Jesus has pluck'd it from the flame,</span>
    <span>And who shall put it in again?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-78." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">78.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">On one Stone shall be seven Eyes.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Zech. iii, 9.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-78-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Jesus Christ, the Lord's Anointed,</span>
      <span class="i2">Who his blood for sinners spilt,</span>
      <span class="i1">Is the Stone by God appointed,</span>
      <span class="i2">And the church is on him built:</span>
    <span>He delivers all who trust him from their guilt.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-78-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Many eyes at once are fix'd</span>
      <span class="i2">On a person so divine;</span>
      <span class="i1">Love, with awful justice mix'd,</span>
      <span class="i2">In his great redemption shine:</span>
    <span>Mighty Jesus! give me leave to call thee mine.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-78-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">By the Father's eye approved,</span>
      <span class="i2">Lo, a voice is heard from heaven,</span>
      <span class="i1">"Sinners, this is my Beloved,</span>
      <span class="i2">For your ransom freely given:</span>
    <span>All offences for his sake shall be forgiven,"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-78-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Angels with their eyes pursued him</span>
      <span class="i2">When he left his glorious throne;</span>
      <span class="i1">With astonishment they view'd him</span>
      <span class="i2">Put the form of servant on;</span>
    <span>Angels worshipp'd Him who was on earth unknown.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-78-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Satan and his host, amazed,</span>
      <span class="i2">Saw this Stone in Zion laid;</span>
      <span class="i1">Jesus, though to death abased,</span>
      <span class="i2">Bruised the subtle Serpent's head</span>
    <span>When, to save us, on the cross his blood he shed.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-78-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">When a guilty sinner sees him,</span>
      <span class="i2">While he looks his soul is heal'd;</span>
      <span class="i1">Soon this sight from anguish frees him,</span>
      <span class="i2">And imparts a pardon seal'd:</span>
    <span>May this Saviour be to all our hearts reveal'd!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-78-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">With desire and admiration,</span>
      <span class="i2">All his blood-bought flock behold</span>
      <span class="i1">Him who wrought out their salvation,</span>
      <span class="i2">And enclosed them in his fold:</span>
    <span>Yet their warmest love and praises are too cold.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-78-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">By the eye of carnal reason</span>
      <span class="i2">Many view him with disdain;</span>
      <span class="i1">How will they abide the season</span>
      <span class="i2">When he comes with all his train?</span>
    <span>To escape him then they'll wish, but wish in vain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-78-9>
 	<header>
 		<p>IX</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">How their hearts will melt and tremble</span>
      <span class="i2">When they hear his awful voice</span>
      <span class="i1">But his saints he'll then assemble,</span>
      <span class="i2">As his portion and his choice,</span>
    <span>And receive them to his everlasting joys.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-79." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">79.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Praise for the Fountain opened.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Zech. xiii, 1.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-79-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>There is a fountain fill'd with blood</span>
      <span class="i1">Drawn from Emmanuel's veins;</span>
    <span>And sinners plunged beneath that flood</span>
      <span class="i1">Lose all their guilty stains.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-79-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The dying thief rejoiced to see</span>
      <span class="i1">That fountain in his day;</span>
    <span>And there have I, as vile as he,</span>
      <span class="i1">Wash'd all my sins away.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-79-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Dear dying Lamb, thy precious blood</span>
      <span class="i1">Shall never lose its power</span>
    <span>Till all the ransom'd church of God</span>
      <span class="i1">Be saved, to sin no more.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-79-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>E'er since, by faith, I saw the stream</span>
      <span class="i1">Thy flowing wounds supply,</span>
    <span>Redeeming love has been my theme,</span>
      <span class="i1">And shall be till I die.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-79-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Then in a nobler, sweeter song,</span>
      <span class="i1">I'll sing thy power to save,—</span>
    <span>When this poor lisping stamm'ring tongue</span>
      <span class="i1">Lies silent in the grave.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-79-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Lord, I believe thou hast prepared</span>
      <span class="i1">(Unworthy though I be,)</span>
    <span>For me a blood-bought free reward,</span>
      <span class="i1">A golden harp for me!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-79-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>'Tis strung, and tuned for endless years,</span>
      <span class="i1">And form'd by power divine;</span>
    <span>To sound in God the Father's ears</span>
      <span class="i1">No other name but thine.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-80." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">80.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">They shall be mine, saith the Lord.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Mal. iii, 16-18.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-80-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When sinners utter boasting words,</span>
      <span class="i1">And glory in their shame,</span>
    <span>The Lord, well pleased, an ear affords,</span>
      <span class="i1">To those who fear his name.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-80-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>They often met to seek his face;</span>
      <span class="i1">And what they do or say</span>
    <span>Is rioted in his book of grace</span>
      <span class="i1">Against another day.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-80-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>For they, by faith, a day descry,</span>
      <span class="i1">And joyfully expect,</span>
    <span>When he, descending from the sky,</span>
      <span class="i1">His jewels will collect.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-80-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Unnoticed now, because unknown,</span>
      <span class="i1">A poor and suff'ring few;</span>
    <span>He comes to claim them for his own,</span>
      <span class="i1">And bring them forth to view.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-80-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>With transport then their Saviour's care</span>
      <span class="i1">And favour they shall prove;</span>
    <span>As tender parents guard and spare</span>
      <span class="i1">The children of their love.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-80-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Assembled worlds will then discern</span>
      <span class="i1">The saints alone are blest,</span>
    <span>When wrath shall like an oven burn,</span>
      <span class="i1">And vengeance strike the rest.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-81." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">81.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Beggar.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Matt, vii, 7, 8.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-81-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Encouraged by thy word</span>
      <span class="i1">Of promise to the poor,</span>
      <span class="i1">Behold a beggar, Lord,</span>
      <span class="i1">Waits at thy mercy's door!</span>
    <span>No hand, no heart, O Lord, but thine,</span>
    <span>Can help or pity wants like mine.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-81-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">The beggar's usual plea,</span>
      <span class="i1">Relief from men to gain,</span>
      <span class="i1">If offer'd unto thee,</span>
      <span class="i1">I know thou wouldst disdain;</span>
    <span>And pleas which move thy gracious ear</span>
    <span>Are such as men would scorn to hear.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-81-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">I have no right to say,</span>
      <span class="i1">That though I now am poor,</span>
      <span class="i1">Yet once there was a day</span>
      <span class="i1">When I possessed more:</span>
    <span>Thou know'st that from my very birth</span>
    <span>I've been the poorest wretch on earth.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-81-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Nor can I dare profess,</span>
      <span class="i1">As beggars often do,</span>
      <span class="i1">Though great is my distress,</span>
      <span class="i1">My faults have been but few:</span>
    <span>If thou shouldst leave my soul to starve,</span>
    <span>It would be what I well deserve.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-81-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">'Twere folly to pretend</span>
      <span class="i1">I never begg'd before;</span>
      <span class="i1">Or if thou now befriend,</span>
      <span class="i1">I'll trouble thee no more;</span>
    <span>Thou often hast relieved my pain,</span>
    <span>And often I must come again.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-81-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Though crumbs are much too good</span>
      <span class="i1">For such a dog as I,</span>
      <span class="i1">No less than children's food</span>
      <span class="i1">My soul can satisfy.</span>
    <span>O do not frown and bid me go,—</span>
    <span>I must have all thou canst bestow!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-81-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Nor can I willing be</span>
      <span class="i1">Thy bounty to conceal</span>
      <span class="i1">From others who, like me,</span>
      <span class="i1">Their wants and hunger feel:</span>
    <span>I'll tell them of thy mercy's store,</span>
    <span>And try to send a thousand more.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-81-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Thy thoughts, thou Only Wise,</span>
      <span class="i1">Our thoughts and ways transcend,</span>
      <span class="i1">Far as the arched skies</span>
      <span class="i1">Above the earth extend:</span>
    <span>Such pleas as mine men would not bear,</span>
    <span>But God receives a beggar's pray'r.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-82." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">82.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Leper.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Matt, viii, 2, 3.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-82-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Oft as the leper's case I read,</span>
      <span class="i1">My own described I feel:</span>
    <span>Sin is a leprosy indeed</span>
      <span class="i1">Which none but Christ can heal.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-82-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Awhile I would have pass'd for well,</span>
      <span class="i1">And strove my spots to hide,</span>
    <span>Till it broke out incurable,</span>
      <span class="i1">Too plain to be denied.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-82-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Then from the saints I sought to flee,</span>
      <span class="i1">And dreaded to be seen;</span>
    <span>I thought they all would point at me.</span>
      <span class="i1">And cry, "Unclean, unclean!"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-82-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>What anguish did my soul endure</span>
      <span class="i1">Till hope and patience ceased!</span>
    <span>The more I strove myself to cure,</span>
      <span class="i1">The more the plague increased.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-82-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>While thus I lay distress'd, I saw</span>
      <span class="i1">The Saviour passing by;</span>
    <span>To him, though fill'd with shame and awe,</span>
      <span class="i1">I raised my mournful cry.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-82-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Lord, thou canst heal me if thou wilt,</span>
      <span class="i1">For thou canst all things do;</span>
    <span>O cleanse my leprous soul from guilt,</span>
      <span class="i1">My filthy heart renew.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-82-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>He heard, and with a gracious look</span>
      <span class="i1">Pronounced the healing word;</span>
    <span>"I will—be clean," and while he spoke</span>
      <span class="i1">I felt my health restored.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-82-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Come, lepers, seize the present hour,</span>
      <span class="i1">The Saviour's grace to prove;</span>
    <span>He can relieve, for he is power—</span>
      <span class="i1">He will, for he is love.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-83." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">83.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">A sick Soul.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Matt, ix, 12.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-83-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Physician of my sin-sick soul,</span>
      <span class="i1">To thee I bring my case;</span>
    <span>My raging malady control,</span>
      <span class="i1">And heal me by thy grace.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-83-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Pity the anguish I endure,</span>
      <span class="i1">See how I mourn and pine;</span>
    <span>For never can I hope a cure</span>
      <span class="i1">From any hand but thine.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-83-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>I would disclose my whole complaint,</span>
      <span class="i1">But where shall I begin?</span>
    <span>No words of mine can fully paint</span>
      <span class="i1">That worst distemper, sin.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-83-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>It lies not in a single part,</span>
      <span class="i1">But through my frame is spread;</span>
    <span>A burning fever in my heart,</span>
      <span class="i1">A palsy in my head.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-83-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>It makes me deaf and dumb and blind,</span>
      <span class="i1">And impotent and lame;</span>
    <span>It overclouds and fills my mind</span>
      <span class="i1">With folly, fear, and shame.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-83-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>A thousand evil thoughts intrude</span>
      <span class="i1">Tumultuous in my breast;</span>
    <span>Which indispose me for my food,</span>
      <span class="i1">And rob me of my rest.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-83-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Lord, I am sick, regard my cry,</span>
      <span class="i1">And set my spirit free:</span>
    <span>Say, canst thou let a sinner die,</span>
      <span class="i1">Who longs to live to thee?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-84." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">84.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Satan returning.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Matt, xii, 43-45.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-84-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When Jesus claims the sinner's heart,</span>
      <span class="i1">Where Satan ruled before,</span>
    <span>The evil spirit must depart,</span>
      <span class="i1">And dares return no more.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-84-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But when he goes without constraint,</span>
      <span class="i1">And wanders from his home,</span>
    <span>Although withdrawn, 'tis but a feint,—</span>
      <span class="i1">He means again to come.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-84-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Some outward change perhaps is seen</span>
      <span class="i1">If Satan quit the place;</span>
    <span>But though the house seem swept and clean.</span>
      <span class="i1">'Tis destitute of grace.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-84-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Except the Saviour dwell and reign</span>
      <span class="i1">Within the sinner's mind,</span>
    <span>Satan, when he returns again,</span>
      <span class="i1">Will easy entrance find.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-84-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>With rage and malice sevenfold</span>
      <span class="i1">He then resumes his sway;</span>
    <span>No more by checks to be control'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">No more to go away.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-84-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The sinner's former state was bad,</span>
      <span class="i1">But worse the latter far;</span>
    <span>He lives possessed, blind, and mad,</span>
      <span class="i1">And dies in dark despair.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-84-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Lord, save me from this dreadful end!</span>
      <span class="i1">And from this heart of mine</span>
    <span>O drive and keep away the fiend</span>
      <span class="i1">Who fears no voice but thine.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-85." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">85.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Sower.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Matt, xiii, 3.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-85-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Ye sons of earth, prepare the plough,</span>
      <span class="i1">Break up your fallow ground!</span>
    <span>The sower is gone forth to sow,</span>
      <span class="i1">And scatter blessings round.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-85-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The seed that finds a stony soil</span>
      <span class="i1">Shoots forth a hasty blade;</span>
    <span>But ill repays the sower's toil,—</span>
      <span class="i1">Soon wither'd, scorch'd, and dead.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-85-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The thorny ground is sure to baulk</span>
      <span class="i1">All hopes of harvest there;</span>
    <span>We find a tall and sickly stalk,</span>
      <span class="i1">But not the fruitful ear.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-85-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The beaten path and highway-side</span>
      <span class="i1">Receive the trust in vain;</span>
    <span>The watchful birds the spoil divide,</span>
      <span class="i1">And pick up all the grain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-85-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But where the Lord of grace and power</span>
      <span class="i1">Has bless'd the happy field,</span>
    <span>How plenteous is the golden store</span>
      <span class="i1">The deep-wrought furrows yield!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-85-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Father of mercies, we have need</span>
      <span class="i1">Of thy preparing grace;</span>
    <span>Let the same hand that gives the seed</span>
      <span class="i1">Provide a fruitful place.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-86." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">86.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Wheat and Tares.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Matt, xiii, 37-42.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-86-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Though in the outward church below</span>
    <span>The wheat and tares together grow,</span>
    <span>Jesus ere long will weed the crop,</span>
    <span>And pluck the tares in anger up.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-86-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Will it relieve their horrors there</span>
    <span>To recollect their stations here—</span>
    <span>How much they heard, how much they knew,</span>
    <span>How long amongst the wheat they grew?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-86-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Oh! this will aggravate their case;</span>
    <span>They perish'd under means of grace;</span>
    <span>To them the word of life and faith</span>
    <span>Became an instrument of death.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-86-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>We seem alike when thus we meet,</span>
    <span>Strangers might think we all are wheat;</span>
    <span>But to the Lord's all-searching eyes</span>
    <span>Each heart appears without disguise.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-86-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The tares are spared for various ends;</span>
    <span>Some for the sake of praying friends,</span>
    <span>Others the Lord, against their will,</span>
    <span>Employs his counsels to fulfill.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-86-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But though they grow so tall and strong,</span>
    <span>His plan will not require them long;</span>
    <span>In harvest, when he saves his own,</span>
    <span>The tares shall into hell be thrown.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-87." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">87.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Peter Walking upon the Water.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Matt, xiv, 28-31.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-87-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>A word from Jesus calms the sea,</span>
      <span class="i1">The stormy wind controls,</span>
    <span>And gives repose and liberty</span>
      <span class="i1">To tempest-tossed souls.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-87-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>To Peter on the waves he came,</span>
      <span class="i1">And gave him instant peace;</span>
    <span>Thus he to me reveal'd his name,</span>
      <span class="i1">And bade my sorrows cease.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-87-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Then fill'd with wonder, joy, and love.</span>
      <span class="i1">Peter's request was mine;</span>
    <span>Lord, call me down, I long to prove</span>
      <span class="i1">That I am wholly thine.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-87-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Unmoved at all I have to meet</span>
      <span class="i1">On life's tempestuous sea,</span>
    <span>Hard shall be easy, bitter sweet,</span>
      <span class="i1">So I may follow thee.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-87-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>He heard and smiled, and bade me try;</span>
      <span class="i1">I eagerly obey'd;</span>
    <span>But when from him I turn'd my eye,</span>
      <span class="i1">How was my soul dismay'd!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-87-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The storm increased on every side,</span>
      <span class="i1">I felt my spirit shrink!</span>
    <span>And soon, with Peter, loud I cried,</span>
      <span class="i1">"Lord, save me, or I sink."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-87-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Kindly he caught me by the hand,</span>
      <span class="i1">And said, "Why dost thou fear</span>
    <span>Since thou art come at my command.</span>
      <span class="i1">And I am always near?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-87-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Upon my promise rest thy hope,</span>
      <span class="i1">And keep my love in view;</span>
    <span>I stand engaged to hold thee up,</span>
      <span class="i1">And guide thee safely through."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-88." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">88.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Woman of Canaan.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Matt, xv, 22-28.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-88-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Prayer an answer will obtain,</span>
    <span>Though the Lord awhile delay;</span>
    <span>None shall seek his face in vain,</span>
    <span>None be empty sent away.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-88-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When the woman came from Tyre,</span>
    <span>And for help to Jesus sought,</span>
    <span>Though he granted her desire,</span>
    <span>Yet at first he answer'd not.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-88-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Could she guess at his intent</span>
    <span>When he to his foll'wers said,</span>
    <span>"I to Israel's sheep am sent;</span>
    <span>Dogs must not have children's bread"?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-88-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>She was not of Israel's seed,</span>
    <span>But of Canaan's wretched race;</span>
    <span>Thought herself a dog indeed;</span>
    <span>Was not this a hopeless case?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-88-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Yet although from Canaan sprung,</span>
    <span>Though a dog herself she styled,</span>
    <span>She had Israel's faith and tongue,</span>
    <span>And was own'd for Abram's child.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-88-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>From His word she draws a plea:</span>
    <span>"Though unworthy children's bread,</span>
    <span>'Tis enough for one like me</span>
    <span>If with crumbs I may be fed."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-88-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Jesus then his heart reveal'd:</span>
    <span>"Woman, canst thou thus believe?</span>
    <span>I to thy petition yield,</span>
    <span>All that thou canst wish receive."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-88-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>'Tis a pattern set for us,</span>
    <span>How we ought to wait and pray;</span>
    <span>None who plead and wrestle thus</span>
    <span>Shall be empty sent away.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-89." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">89.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">What think ye of Christ?.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Matt, xxii, 42.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-89-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>What think you of Christ is the test</span>
    <span>To try both your state and your scheme;</span>
    <span>You cannot be right in the rest</span>
    <span>Unless you think rightly of him.</span>
    <span>As Jesus appears in your view,</span>
    <span>As he is beloved or not,</span>
    <span>So God is disposed to you,</span>
    <span>And mercy or wrath are your lot.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-89-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Some take him a creature to be,</span>
    <span>A man, or an angel at most:</span>
    <span>Sure these have not feelings like me,</span>
    <span>Nor know themselves wretched and lost.</span>
    <span>So guilty, so helpless am I,</span>
    <span>I durst not confide in his blood,</span>
    <span>Nor on his protection rely,</span>
    <span>Unless I were sure he is God.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-89-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Some call him a Saviour in word,</span>
    <span>But mix their own works with his plan;</span>
    <span>And hope he his help will afford,</span>
    <span>When they have done all that they can:</span>
    <span>If doings prove rather too light,</span>
    <span>(A little, they own, they may fail,)</span>
    <span>They purpose to make up full weight,</span>
    <span>By casting his name in the scale.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-89-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Some style him the pearl of great price,</span>
    <span>And say he's the fountain of joys;</span>
    <span>Yet feed upon folly and vice,</span>
    <span>And cleave to the world and its toys;</span>
    <span>Like Judas, the Saviour they kiss,</span>
    <span>And while they salute him, betray;</span>
    <span>Ah! what will profession like this</span>
    <span>Avail in his terrible day?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-89-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>If ask'd what of Jesus I think,—</span>
    <span>Though still my best thoughts are but poor,</span>
    <span>I say he's my meat and my drink,</span>
    <span>My life and my strength and my store;</span>
    <span>My Shepherd, my Husband, my Friend,</span>
    <span>My Saviour from sin and from thrall,</span>
    <span>My hope from beginning to end,</span>
    <span>My portion, my Lord, and my all.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-90." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">90.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The foolish Virgins.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Matt, xxv, 1.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-90-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When descending from the sky</span>
      <span class="i1">The Bridegroom shall appear,</span>
    <span>And the solemn midnight cry</span>
      <span class="i1">Shall call professors near,</span>
    <span>How the sound our hearts will damp—</span>
    <span>How will shame o'erspread each face</span>
    <span>If we only have a lamp</span>
      <span class="i1">Without the oil of grace!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-90-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Foolish virgins then will wake</span>
      <span class="i1">And seek for a supply;</span>
    <span>But in vain the pains they take</span>
      <span class="i1">To borrow or to buy:</span>
    <span>Then with those they now despise</span>
    <span>Earnestly they'll wish to share;</span>
    <span>But the best among the wise</span>
      <span class="i1">Will have no oil to spare.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-90-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Wise are they, and truly blest,</span>
      <span class="i1">Who then shall ready be!</span>
    <span>But despair will seize the rest,</span>
      <span class="i1">And dreadful misery:</span>
    <span>Once, they'll cry, we scorn'd to doubt,</span>
    <span>Though in lies our trust we put;</span>
    <span>Now our lamp of hope is out—</span>
      <span class="i1">The door of mercy shut.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-90-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>If they then presume to plead,</span>
      <span class="i1">"Lord, open to us now;</span>
    <span>We on earth have heard and pray'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">And with thy saints did bow:"</span>
    <span>He will answer from his throne</span>
    <span>"Though you with my people mix'd,</span>
    <span>Yet to me you ne'er were known;</span>
      <span class="i1">Depart, your doom is fix'd."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-90-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Oh that none who worship here</span>
      <span class="i1">May hear that word, depart!</span>
    <span>Lord, impress a godly fear</span>
      <span class="i1">On each professor's heart:</span>
    <span>Help us, Lord, to search the camp,</span>
    <span>Let us not ourselves beguile,</span>
    <span>Trusting to a dying lamp,</span>
      <span class="i1">Without a stock of oil.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-91." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">91.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Peter sinning and repenting.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Matt, xxvi, 73.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-91-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When Peter boasted, soon he fell,</span>
      <span class="i1">Yet was by grace restored;</span>
    <span>His case should be regarded well</span>
      <span class="i1">By all who fear the Lord.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-91-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>A voice it has, and helping hand,</span>
      <span class="i1">Backsliders to recall;</span>
    <span>And cautions those who think they stand,</span>
      <span class="i1">Lest suddenly they fall.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-91-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>He said, "Whatever others do,</span>
      <span class="i1">With Jesus I'll abide;"</span>
    <span>Yet soon amidst a murd'rous crew</span>
      <span class="i1">His suff'ring Lord denied.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-91-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>He who had been so bold before</span>
      <span class="i1">Now trembled like a leaf,—</span>
    <span>Not only lied, but cursed and swore,</span>
      <span class="i1">To gain the more belief.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-91-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>While he blasphemed he heard the cock,</span>
      <span class="i1">And Jesus look'd in love;</span>
    <span>At once, as if by lightning struck,</span>
      <span class="i1">His tongue forebore to move.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-91-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Deliver'd thus from Satan's snare,</span>
      <span class="i1">He starts, as from a sleep;</span>
    <span>His Saviour's look he could not bear,</span>
      <span class="i1">But hasted forth to weep.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-91-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But sure the faithful cock had crow'd</span>
      <span class="i1">A hundred times in vain</span>
    <span>Had not the Lord that look bestow'd</span>
      <span class="i1">The meaning to explain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-91-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>As I, like Peter, vows have made,</span>
      <span class="i1">Yet acted Peter's part;</span>
    <span>So conscience, like the cock, upbraids</span>
      <span class="i1">My base ungrateful heart.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-91-9>
 	<header>
 		<p>IX</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Lord Jesus, hear a sinner's cry,</span>
      <span class="i1">My broken peace renew;</span>
    <span>And grant one pitying look, that I</span>
      <span class="i1">May weep with Peter too.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-92." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">92.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Legion dispossessed.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Mark, v, 18, 19.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-92-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Legion was my name by nature,</span>
    <span>Satan raged within my breast,</span>
    <span>Never misery was greater,</span>
    <span>Never sinner more possess'd:</span>
    <span>Mischievous to all around me,</span>
    <span>To myself the greatest foe;</span>
    <span>Thus I was when Jesus found me,</span>
    <span>Fill'd with madness, sin, and woe.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-92-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Yet in this forlorn condition,</span>
    <span>When he came to see me free,</span>
    <span>I replied to my Physician,</span>
    <span>"What have I to do with thee?"</span>
    <span>But he would not be prevented,</span>
    <span>Rescued me against my will:</span>
    <span>Had he staid till I consented</span>
    <span>I had been a captive still.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-92-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Satan, though thou fain wouldst have it,</span>
    <span>Know this soul is none of thine;</span>
    <span>I have shed my blood to save it,</span>
    <span>Now I challenge it for mine;</span>
    <span>Though it long has thee resembled,</span>
    <span>Henceforth it shall me obey:</span>
    <span>Thus He spoke, while Satan trembled,</span>
    <span>Gnash'd his teeth, and fled away.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-92-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus my frantic soul He heal'd,</span>
    <span>Bid my sins and sorrows cease;</span>
    <span>"Take," said he, "my pardon sealed,</span>
    <span>I have saved thee,—go in peace."</span>
    <span>Rather take me, Lord, to heaven,</span>
    <span>Now thy love and grace I know;</span>
    <span>Since thou hast my sins forgiven,</span>
    <span>Why should I remain below?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-92-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Love," he said, "will sweeten labours;</span>
    <span>Thou hast something yet to do;</span>
    <span>Go and tell your friends and neighbours</span>
    <span>What my love has done for you;</span>
    <span>Live to manifest my glory,</span>
    <span>Wait for heaven a little space:</span>
    <span>Sinners, when they hear thy story,</span>
    <span>Will repent and seek my face."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-93." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">93.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Ruler’s Daughter raised.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Mark, v, 39-42.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-93-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Could the creatures help or ease us</span>
    <span>Seldom should we think of prayer;</span>
    <span>Few, if any, come to Jesus</span>
    <span>Till reduced to self-despair:</span>
    <span>Long we either slight or doubt him;</span>
    <span>But when all the means we try</span>
    <span>Prove we cannot do without him,</span>
    <span>Then at last to him we cry.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-93-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus the ruler, when his daughter</span>
    <span>Suffer'd much, though Christ was nigh,</span>
    <span>Still deferr'd it till he thought her</span>
    <span>At the very point to die:</span>
    <span>Though he mourn'd for her condition,</span>
    <span>He did not entreat the Lord</span>
    <span>Till he found that no physician</span>
    <span>But himself could help afford.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-93-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Jesus did not once upbraid him,</span>
    <span>That he had no sooner come;</span>
    <span>But a gracious answer made him,</span>
    <span>And went straightway with him home:</span>
    <span>Yet his faith was put to trial</span>
    <span>When his servants came, and said,</span>
    <span>Though he gave thee no denial,</span>
    <span>'Tis too late,—the child is dead."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-93-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Jesus, to prevent his grieving,</span>
    <span>Kindly spoke, and eased his pain;</span>
    <span>"Be not fearful, but believing,—</span>
    <span>Thou shalt see her live again."</span>
    <span>When he found the people weeping,</span>
    <span>"Cease," he said, "no longer mourn;</span>
    <span>For she is not dead, but sleeping:"</span>
    <span>Then they laughed him to scorn.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-93-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>O thou meek and lowly Saviour,</span>
    <span>How determined is thy love!</span>
    <span>Not this rude unkind behaviour</span>
    <span>Could thy gracious purpose move.</span>
    <span>Soon as he the room had enter'd,</span>
    <span>Spoke, and took her by the hand,</span>
    <span>Death at once his prey surrender'd,</span>
    <span>And she lived at his command.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-93-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Fear not then, distress'd believer,</span>
    <span>Venture on his mighty name;</span>
    <span>He is able to deliver,</span>
    <span>And his love is still the same:</span>
    <span>Can his pity or his power</span>
    <span>Suffer thee to pray in vain?</span>
    <span>Wait but his appointed hour,</span>
    <span>And thy suit thou shalt obtain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-94." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">94.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">But one Loaf.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Mark, viii, 14.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-94-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When the disciples cross'd the lake</span>
      <span class="i1">With but one loaf on board,</span>
    <span>How strangely did their hearts mistake</span>
      <span class="i1">The caution of their Lord!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-94-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"The leaven of the Pharisees</span>
      <span class="i1">Beware," the Saviour said;</span>
    <span>They thought, It is because he sees</span>
      <span class="i1">We have forgotten bread.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-94-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>It seems they had forgotten too</span>
      <span class="i1">What their own eyes had view'd—</span>
    <span>How, with what scarce sufficed for few,</span>
      <span class="i1">He fed a multitude.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-94-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>If five small loaves, by his command,</span>
      <span class="i1">Could many thousands serve,</span>
    <span>Might they not trust his gracious hand.</span>
      <span class="i1">That they should never starve?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-94-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>They oft his power and love had known,</span>
      <span class="i1">And doubtless were to blame;</span>
    <span>But we have reason good to own</span>
      <span class="i1">That we are just the same.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-94-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>How often has he brought relief,</span>
      <span class="i1">And every want supplied!</span>
    <span>Yet soon, again, our unbelief</span>
      <span class="i1">Says, "Can the Lord provide?"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-94-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Be thankful for one loaf to-day,</span>
      <span class="i1">Though that be all your store:</span>
    <span>To-morrow, if you trust and pray,</span>
      <span class="i1">Shall timely bring you more.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-95." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">95.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Bartimeus.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Mark, x, 47, 48.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-95-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Mercy, thou son of David!"</span>
    <span>Thus blind Bartimeus pray'd;</span>
    <span>"Others by thy word are saved,</span>
    <span>Now to me afford thine aid."</span>
    <span>Many for his crying chid him,</span>
    <span>But he call'd the louder still,</span>
    <span>Till the gracious Saviour bid him</span>
    <span>"Come, and ask me what you will."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-95-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Money was not what he wanted,</span>
    <span>Though by begging used to live;</span>
    <span>But he ask'd, and Jesus granted</span>
    <span>Alms which none but he could give:</span>
    <span>"Lord, remove this grievous blindness,</span>
    <span>Let my eyes behold the day;"</span>
    <span>Straight he saw and, won by kindness,</span>
    <span>Follow'd Jesus in the way.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-95-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Oh! methinks I hear him praising,</span>
    <span>Publishing to all around,</span>
    <span>"Friends, is not my case amazing?</span>
    <span>What a Saviour I have found!</span>
    <span>Oh! that all the blind but knew him,</span>
    <span>And would be advised by me;</span>
    <span>Surely they would hasten to him,</span>
    <span>He would cause them all to see."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-96." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">96.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The House of Prayer.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Mark, xi, 17.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-96-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thy mansion is the Christian's heart,</span>
    <span>O Lord, thy dwelling-place secure!</span>
    <span>Bid the unruly throng depart,</span>
    <span>And leave the consecrated door.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-96-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Devoted as it is to thee,</span>
    <span>A thievish swarm frequents the place;</span>
    <span>They steal away my joys from me,</span>
    <span>And rob my Saviour of his praise.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
