<section id="stanza-1-96-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>There too a sharp designing trade,</span>
    <span>Sin, Satan, and the world maintain;</span>
    <span>Nor cease to press me, and persuade,</span>
    <span>To part with ease and purchase pain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-96-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>I know them, and I hate their din,</span>
    <span>Am weary of the bustling crowd;</span>
    <span>But while their voice is heard within</span>
    <span>I cannot serve thee as I would.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-96-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Oh! for the joy thy presence gives,—</span>
    <span>What peace shall reign when thou art here!</span>
    <span>Thy presence makes this den of thieves</span>
    <span>A calm delightful house of prayer.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-96-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>And if thou make thy temple shine,</span>
    <span>Yet, self-abased, will I adore;</span>
    <span>The gold and silver are not mine,—</span>
    <span>I give thee what was thine before.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-97." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">97.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Blasted Fig-tree.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Mark, xi, 20.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-97-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>One awful word which Jesus spoke</span>
    <span>Against the tree which bore no fruit,</span>
    <span>More piercing than the lightning's stroke,</span>
    <span>Blasted and dried it to the root.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-97-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But could a tree the Lord offend,</span>
    <span>To make him show his anger thus!</span>
    <span>He surely had, a further end—</span>
    <span>To be a warning word to us.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-97-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The fig-tree by its leaves was known;</span>
    <span>But having not a fig to show,</span>
    <span>It brought a heavy sentence down—</span>
    <span>"Let none hereafter on thee grow."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-97-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Too many, who the gospel hear,</span>
    <span>Whom Satan blinds and sin deceives</span>
    <span>We to this fig-tree may compare,</span>
    <span>They yield no fruit, but only leaves</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-97-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Knowledge and zeal and gifts and talk.</span>
    <span>Unless combined with faith and love,</span>
    <span>And witnessed by a gospel-walk,</span>
    <span>Will not a true profession prove.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-97-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Without the fruit the Lord expects,</span>
    <span>Knowledge will make our state the worse;</span>
    <span>The barren trees he still rejects,</span>
    <span>And soon will blast them with his curse.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-97-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>O Lord, unite our hearts in prayer!</span>
    <span>On each of us thy Spirit send,</span>
    <span>That we the fruits of grace may bear,</span>
    <span>And find acceptance in the end.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-98." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">98.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Two Debtors.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Luke, vii, 47.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-98-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Once a woman silent stood</span>
      <span class="i1">While Jesus sat at meat;</span>
    <span>From her eyes she pour'd a flood,</span>
      <span class="i1">To wash his sacred feet:</span>
    <span>Shame and wonder, joy and love,</span>
    <span>All at once possess'd her mind,</span>
    <span>That she e'er so vile could prove,</span>
      <span class="i1">Yet now forgiveness find.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-98-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"How came this vile woman here?</span>
      <span class="i1">Will Jesus notice such?</span>
    <span>Sure, if he a prophet were,</span>
      <span class="i1">He would disdain her touch!"</span>
    <span>Simon thus, with scornful heart,</span>
    <span>Slighted one whom Jesus loved;</span>
    <span>But her Saviour took her part,</span>
      <span class="i1">And thus his pride reproved:</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-98-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"If two men in debt were bound,</span>
      <span class="i1">One less, the other more,</span>
    <span>Fifty, or five hundred pound,</span>
      <span class="i1">And both alike were poor;</span>
    <span>Should the lender both forgive</span>
    <span>When he saw them both distress'd,</span>
    <span>Which of them would you believe</span>
      <span class="i1">Engaged to love him best?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-98-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Surely he who most did owe,"</span>
      <span class="i1">The Pharisee replied:</span>
    <span>Then our Lord, "By judging so,</span>
      <span class="i1">Thou dost for her decide:</span>
    <span>Simon, if like her you knew</span>
    <span>How much you forgiveness need,</span>
    <span>You like her had acted too,</span>
      <span class="i1">And welcomed me indeed.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-98-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"When the load of sin is felt,</span>
      <span class="i1">And much forgiveness known</span>
    <span>Then the heart of course will melt,</span>
      <span class="i1">Though hard before as stone:</span>
    <span>Blame not then her love and tears,</span>
    <span>Greatly she in debt has been;</span>
    <span>But I have removed her fears,</span>
      <span class="i1">And pardon'd all her sin."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-98-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When I read this woman's case,</span>
      <span class="i1">Her love and humble zeal,</span>
    <span>I confess, with shame of face,</span>
      <span class="i1">My heart is made of steel.</span>
    <span>Much has been forgiven to me,</span>
    <span>Jesus paid my heavy score;</span>
    <span>What a creature must I be,</span>
      <span class="i1">That I can love no more!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-99." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">99.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Good Samaritan.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Luke, x, 33-35.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-99-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>How kind the good Samaritan</span>
    <span>To him who fell among the thieves!</span>
    <span>Thus Jesus pities fallen man,</span>
    <span>And heals the wounds the soul receives.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-99-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Oh! I remember well the day</span>
    <span>When, sorely wounded, nearly slain,</span>
    <span>Like that poor man, I bleeding lay,</span>
    <span>And groan'd for help, but groan'd in vain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-99-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Men saw me in this helpless case,</span>
    <span>And pass'd without compassion by;</span>
    <span>Each neighbour turn'd away his face,</span>
    <span>Unmoved by my mournful cry.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-99-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But He whose name had been my scorn</span>
    <span>(As Jews Samaritans despise)</span>
    <span>Came, when he saw me thus forlorn,</span>
    <span>With love and pity in his eyes.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-99-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Gently he raised me from the ground,</span>
    <span>Press'd me to lean upon his arm,</span>
    <span>And into every gaping wound</span>
    <span>He pour'd his own all-healing balm.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-99-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Unto his church my steps he led,</span>
    <span>The house prepared for sinners lost,</span>
    <span>Gave charge I should be clothed and fed,</span>
    <span>And took upon him all the cost.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-99-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus saved from death, from want secured,</span>
    <span>I wait till he again shall come</span>
    <span>(When I shall be completely cured,)</span>
    <span>And take me to his heavenly home.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-99-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>There, through eternal, boundless days,</span>
    <span>When Nature's wheel no longer rolls,</span>
    <span>How shall I love, adore, and praise</span>
    <span>This good Samaritan to souls!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-100." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">100.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Martha and Mary.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Luke, x, 38-42.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-100-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Martha her love and joy express'd</span>
    <span>By care to entertain her guest;</span>
    <span>While Mary sat to hear her Lord,</span>
    <span>And could not bear to lose a word.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-100-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The principle, in both the same,</span>
    <span>Produced in each a different aim;</span>
    <span>The one to feast the Lord was led,</span>
    <span>The other waited to be fed.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-100-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But Mary chose the better part,</span>
    <span>Her Saviour's words refresh'd her heart,</span>
    <span>While busy Martha angry grew,</span>
    <span>And lost her time and temper too.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-100-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>With warmth she to her sister spoke,</span>
    <span>But brought upon herself rebuke:</span>
    <span>"One thing is needful, and but one,</span>
    <span>Why do thy thoughts on many run?"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-100-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>How oft are we like Martha vex'd,</span>
    <span>Encumber'd, hurried, and perplex'd,</span>
    <span>While trifles so engross our thought</span>
    <span>The one thing needful is forgot!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-100-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Lord, teach us this one thing to choose,</span>
    <span>Which they who gain can never lose,—</span>
    <span>Sufficient in itself alone,</span>
    <span>And needful, were the world our own.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-100-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Let grov'ling hearts the world admire,—</span>
    <span>Thy love is all that I require!</span>
    <span>Gladly I may the rest resign,</span>
    <span>If the one needful thing be mine!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-101." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">101.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Heart taken.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Luke, xi, 21, 22.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-101-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The castle of the human heart,</span>
      <span class="i1">Strong in its native sin,</span>
    <span>Is guarded well in every part</span>
      <span class="i1">By him who dwells within.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-101-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>For Satan there in arms resides,</span>
      <span class="i1">And calls the place his own,—</span>
    <span>With care against assaults provides,</span>
      <span class="i1">And rules as on a throne.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-101-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Each traitor thought on him, as chief,</span>
      <span class="i1">In blind obedience waits;</span>
    <span>And pride, self-will, and unbelief,</span>
      <span class="i1">Are posted at the gates.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-101-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus Satan for a season reigns,</span>
      <span class="i1">And keeps his goods in peace;</span>
    <span>The soul is pleased to wear his chains,</span>
      <span class="i1">Nor wishes a release.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-101-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But Jesus, stronger far than he,</span>
      <span class="i1">In his appointed hour</span>
    <span>Appears, to set his people free</span>
      <span class="i1">From the usurper's power.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-101-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"This heart I bought with blood," he says,</span>
      <span class="i1">"And now it shall be mine;"</span>
    <span>His voice the strong one arm'd dismays,—</span>
      <span class="i1">He knows he must resign.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-101-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>In spite of unbelief and pride,</span>
      <span class="i1">And self, and Satan's art,</span>
    <span>The gates of brass fly open wide,</span>
      <span class="i1">And Jesus wins the heart.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-101-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The rebel soul that once withstood</span>
      <span class="i1">The Saviour's kindest call,</span>
    <span>Rejoices now, by grace subdued,</span>
      <span class="i1">To serve him with her all.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-102." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">102.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Worldling.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Luke, xii, 16-21.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-102-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"My barns are full, my stores increase,</span>
      <span class="i1">And now, for many years,</span>
    <span>Soul, eat and drink, and take thine ease,</span>
      <span class="i1">Secure from wants and fears."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-102-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus while a worldling boasted once,</span>
      <span class="i1">As many now presume,</span>
    <span>He heard the Lord himself pronounce</span>
      <span class="i1">His sudden awful doom.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-102-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"This night, vain fool, thy soul must pass</span>
      <span class="i1">Into a world unknown;</span>
    <span>And who shall then the stores possess</span>
      <span class="i1">Which thou hast call'd thine own?"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-102-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus blinded mortals fondly scheme</span>
      <span class="i1">For happiness below,</span>
    <span>Till death disturbs the pleasing dream,</span>
      <span class="i1">And they awake to woe.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-102-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Ah! who can speak the vast dismay</span>
      <span class="i1">That fills the sinner's mind,</span>
    <span>When, torn by Death's strong hand away,</span>
      <span class="i1">He leaves his all behind.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-102-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Wretches, who cleave to earthly things,</span>
      <span class="i1">But are not rich to God,</span>
    <span>Their dying hour is full of stings,</span>
      <span class="i1">And hell their dark abode.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-102-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Dear Saviour, make us timely wise</span>
      <span class="i1">Thy gospel to attend,</span>
    <span>That we may live above the skies</span>
      <span class="i1">When this poor life shall end.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-103." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">103.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Barren Fig-Tree.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Luke, xiii, 6-9.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-103-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">The church a garden is,</span>
      <span class="i1">In which believers stand</span>
      <span class="i1">Like ornamental trees</span>
      <span class="i1">Planted by God's own hand!</span>
    <span>His Spirit waters all their roots,</span>
    <span>And every branch abounds with fruits.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-103-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">But other trees there are</span>
      <span class="i1">In this enclosure grow,</span>
      <span class="i1">Which, though they promise fair,</span>
      <span class="i1">Have only leaves to show:</span>
    <span>No fruits of grace are on them found,</span>
    <span>They stand but cumberers of the ground.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-103-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">The under gardener grieves,</span>
      <span class="i1">In vain his strength he spends,</span>
      <span class="i1">For heaps of useless leaves</span>
      <span class="i1">Afford him small amends:</span>
    <span>He hears the Lord his will make known,</span>
    <span>To cut the barren fig-trees down.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-103-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">How difficult his post,</span>
      <span class="i1">What pangs his bowels move,</span>
      <span class="i1">To find his wishes cross'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">His labours useless prove!</span>
    <span>His last relief is earnest prayer,</span>
    <span>"Lord, spare them yet another year.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-103-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">"Spare them, and let me try</span>
      <span class="i1">What further means may do;</span>
      <span class="i1">I'll fresh manure apply,</span>
      <span class="i1">My digging I'll renew:</span>
    <span>Who knows but yet they fruit may yield?</span>
    <span>If not—'tis just, they must be fell'd."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-103-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">If under means of grace</span>
      <span class="i1">No gracious fruits appear,</span>
      <span class="i1">It is a dreadful case,</span>
      <span class="i1">Though God may long forbear:</span>
    <span>At length he'll strike the threaten'd blow,</span>
    <span>And lay the barren fig-tree low.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-104." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">104.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Prodigal Son.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Luke, xv, 11-24.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-104-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Afflictions, though they seem severe,</span>
      <span class="i1">In mercy oft are sent;</span>
    <span>They stopp'd the prodigal's career,</span>
      <span class="i1">And forced him to repent.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-104-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Although he no relentings felt</span>
      <span class="i1">Till he had spent his store,</span>
    <span>His stubborn heart began to melt</span>
      <span class="i1">When famine pinch'd him sore.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-104-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"What have I gain'd by sin," he said,</span>
      <span class="i1">"But hunger, shame, and fear?</span>
    <span>My father's house abounds with bread</span>
      <span class="i1">While I am starving here.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-104-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>I'll go and tell him all I've done,</span>
      <span class="i1">And fall before his face;</span>
    <span>Unworthy to be call'd his son,</span>
      <span class="i1">I'll seek a servant's place."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-104-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>His father saw him coming back,</span>
      <span class="i1">He saw and ran and smiled,</span>
    <span>And threw his arms around the neck</span>
      <span class="i1">Of his rebellious child.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-104-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Father, I've sinn'd—but O forgive!"</span>
      <span class="i1">"I've heard enough," he said;</span>
    <span>"Rejoice, my house,—my son's alive</span>
      <span class="i1">For whom I mourn'd as dead.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-104-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Now let the fatted calf be slain,</span>
      <span class="i1">And spread the news around:</span>
    <span>My son was dead, but lives again,—</span>
      <span class="i1">Was lost, but now is found.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-104-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>'Tis thus the Lord his love reveals</span>
      <span class="i1">To call poor sinners home;</span>
    <span>More than a father's love he feels.</span>
      <span class="i1">And welcomes all that come.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-105." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">105.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The rich Man and Lazarus.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Luke, xvi, 19-25.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-105-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">1 A worlding spent each day</span>
      <span class="i1">In luxury and state,</span>
      <span class="i1">While a believer lay</span>
      <span class="i1">A beggar at his gate.</span>
    <span>Think not the Lord's appointment strange,</span>
    <span>Death made a great and lasting change.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-105-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Death brought the saint release</span>
      <span class="i1">From want, disease, and scorn;</span>
      <span class="i1">And to the land of peace</span>
      <span class="i1">His soul, by angels borne,</span>
    <span>In Abraham's bosom safely placed,</span>
    <span>Enjoys an everlasting feast.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-105-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">The rich man also died,</span>
      <span class="i1">And in a moment fell</span>
      <span class="i1">From all his pomp and pride</span>
      <span class="i1">Into the flames of hell:</span>
    <span>The beggar's bliss, from far beheld,</span>
    <span>His soul with double anguish fill'd.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-105-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">"O, Abra'm, send," he cries,</span>
      <span class="i1">(But his request was vain,)</span>
      <span class="i1">"The beggar from the skies</span>
      <span class="i1">To mitigate my pain!</span>
    <span>One drop of water I entreat,</span>
    <span>To sooth my tongue's tormenting heat."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-105-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Let all who worldly pelf</span>
      <span class="i1">And worldly spirits have</span>
      <span class="i1">Observe, each for himself,</span>
      <span class="i1">The answer Abra'm gave:</span>
    <span>"Remember thou wast fill'd with good,</span>
    <span>While the poor beggar pined for good.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-105-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">"Neglected at thy door,</span>
      <span class="i1">With tears he begg'd his bread;</span>
      <span class="i1">But now he weeps no more—</span>
      <span class="i1">His griefs and pains are fled:</span>
    <span>His joys eternally will flow,</span>
    <span>While thine expire in endless woe."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-105-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Lord, make us truly wise,</span>
      <span class="i1">To choose thy people's lot,</span>
      <span class="i1">And earthly joys despise,</span>
      <span class="i1">Which soon will be forgot:</span>
    <span>The greatest evil we can fear,</span>
    <span>Is to possess our portion here!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-106." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">106.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The importunate Widow.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Luke, xviii, 1-7.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-106-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Our Lord, who knows full well</span>
      <span class="i1">The heart of every saint,</span>
    <span>Invites us, by a parable.</span>
      <span class="i1">To pray and never faint.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-106-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">He bows his gracious ear,</span>
      <span class="i1">We never plead in vain;</span>
    <span>Yet we must wait till he appear,</span>
      <span class="i1">And pray, and pray again.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-106-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Though unbelief suggest,</span>
      <span class="i1">Why should we longer wait?</span>
    <span>He bids us never give him rest,</span>
      <span class="i1">But be importunate.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-106-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">'Twas thus a widow poor,</span>
      <span class="i1">Without support or friend,</span>
    <span>Beset the unjust judge's door,</span>
      <span class="i1">And gain'd, at last, her end.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-106-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">For her he little cared,</span>
      <span class="i1">As little for the laws;</span>
    <span>Nor god nor man did he regard,</span>
      <span class="i1">Yet he espoused her cause.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-106-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">She urged him day and night,</span>
      <span class="i1">Would no denial take;</span>
    <span>At length he said, "I'll do her right,</span>
      <span class="i1">For my own quiet's sake."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-106-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">And shall not Jesus hear</span>
      <span class="i1">His chosen when they cry?</span>
    <span>Yes, though he may a while forbear,</span>
      <span class="i1">He'll help them from on high.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-106-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">His nature, truth, and love,</span>
      <span class="i1">Engage him on their side;</span>
    <span>When they are grieved, his bowels move,</span>
      <span class="i1">And can they be denied?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-106-9>
 	<header>
 		<p>IX</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Then let us earnest be,</span>
      <span class="i1">And never faint in prayer;</span>
    <span>He loves our importunity,</span>
      <span class="i1">And makes our cause his care.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-107." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">107.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Zaccheus.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Luke, xix, 1-6.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-107-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Zaccheus climb'd the tree,</span>
      <span class="i1">And thought himself unknown;</span>
      <span class="i1">But how surprised was he</span>
      <span class="i1">When Jesus call'd him down!</span>
    <span>The Lord beheld him, though conceal'd,</span>
    <span>And by a word his power reveal'd.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-107-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Wonder and joy at once</span>
      <span class="i1">Were painted in his face;</span>
      <span class="i1">"Does he my name pronounce,</span>
      <span class="i1">And does he know my case?</span>
    <span>Will Jesus deign with me to dine?</span>
    <span>Lord, I, with all I have, are thine."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-107-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Thus, where the gospel's preach'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">And sinners come to hear,</span>
      <span class="i1">The hearts of some are reach'd</span>
      <span class="i1">Before they are aware:</span>
    <span>The word directly speaks to them,</span>
    <span>And seems to point them out by name.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-107-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">'Tis curiosity</span>
      <span class="i1">Oft brings them in the way,</span>
      <span class="i1">Only the man to see</span>
      <span class="i1">And hear what he can say;</span>
    <span>But how the sinner starts to find</span>
    <span>The preacher knows his inmost mind!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-107-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">His long-forgotten faults</span>
      <span class="i1">Are brought again in view,</span>
      <span class="i1">And all his secrets thoughts</span>
      <span class="i1">Reveal'd in public too.</span>
    <span>Though compass'd with a crowd about,</span>
    <span>The searching word has found him out.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-107-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">While thus distressing pain</span>
      <span class="i1">And sorrow fill his heart,</span>
      <span class="i1">He hears a voice again,</span>
      <span class="i1">That bids his fears depart,</span>
    <span>Then like Zaccheus he is blest,</span>
    <span>And Jesus deigns to be his guest.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-108." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">108.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Believer’s Danger, Safety, and Duty.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Luke, xxii, 31, 32.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-108-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Simon beware," the Saviour said,—</span>
      <span class="i1">Satan, your subtle foe,</span>
    <span>Already has his measures laid</span>
      <span class="i1">Your soul to overthrow.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-108-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"He wants to sift you all as wheat,</span>
      <span class="i1">And thinks his vict'ry sure;</span>
    <span>But I his malice will defeat,—</span>
      <span class="i1">My pray'r shall faith secure."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-108-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Believers, tremble and rejoice,</span>
      <span class="i1">Your help and danger view;</span>
    <span>This warning has to you a voice,</span>
      <span class="i1">This promise speaks to you.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-108-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Satan beholds with jealous eye</span>
      <span class="i1">Your privilege and joy;</span>
    <span>He's always watchful, always nigh,</span>
      <span class="i1">To tear and to destroy.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-108-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But Jesus lives to intercede,</span>
      <span class="i1">That faith may still prevail;</span>
    <span>He will support in time of need,</span>
      <span class="i1">And Satan's art shall fail.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-108-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Yet let us not the warning slight,</span>
      <span class="i1">But watchful still be found;</span>
    <span>Though faith cannot be slain in fight,</span>
      <span class="i1">It may receive a wound.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-108-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>While Satan watches dare we sleep?</span>
      <span class="i1">We must our guard maintain;</span>
    <span>But, Lord, do thou the city keep,</span>
      <span class="i1">Or else we watch in vain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-109." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">109.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Father, forgive them.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Luke, xxiii, 34.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-109-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Father, forgive," the Saviour said,</span>
      <span class="i1">"They know not what they do:"</span>
    <span>His heart was moved when thus he pray'd</span>
      <span class="i1">For me, my friends, and you.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-109-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>He saw that as the Jews abused</span>
      <span class="i1">And crucified his flesh,</span>
    <span>So he by us would be refused,</span>
      <span class="i1">And crucified afresh.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-109-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Through love of sin we long were prone</span>
      <span class="i1">To act as Satan bid;</span>
    <span>But now with grief and shame we own</span>
      <span class="i1">We knew not what we did.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-109-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>We knew not the desert of sin,</span>
      <span class="i1">Nor whom we thus defied;</span>
    <span>Nor where our guilty souls had been</span>
      <span class="i1">If Jesus had not died.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-109-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>We knew not what a law we broke,</span>
      <span class="i1">How holy, just, and pure!</span>
    <span>Nor what a God we durst provoke,</span>
      <span class="i1">But thought ourselves secure.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-109-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But Jesus all our guilt foresaw,</span>
      <span class="i1">And shed his precious blood,</span>
    <span>To satisfy the holy law,</span>
      <span class="i1">And make our peace with God.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-109-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>My sin, dear Saviour, made thee bleed,</span>
      <span class="i1">Yet didst thou pray for me!</span>
    <span>I knew not what I did, indeed,</span>
      <span class="i1">When ignorant of thee.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-110." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">110.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The two Malefactors.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Luke, xxiii, 39-43.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-110-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Sovereign grace has power alone</span>
    <span>To subdue a heart of stone;</span>
    <span>And the moment grace is felt,</span>
    <span>Then the hardest heart will melt.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-110-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When our Lord was crucified</span>
    <span>Two transgressors with him died!</span>
    <span>One, with vile blaspheming tongue,</span>
    <span>Scoff'd at Jesus as he hung.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-110-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus he spent his wicked breath</span>
    <span>In the very jaws of death;</span>
    <span>Perish'd, as too many do,</span>
    <span>With the Saviour in his view.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-110-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But the other, touch'd with grace,</span>
    <span>Saw the danger of his case,—</span>
    <span>Faith received to own the Lord,</span>
    <span>Whom the scribes and priests abhorr'd.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-110-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Lord," he pray'd, "remember me</span>
    <span>When in glory thou shalt be!"</span>
    <span>"Soon with me," the Lord replies,</span>
    <span>"Thou shalt rest in paradise."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-110-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>This was wondrous grace indeed,</span>
    <span>Grace vouchsafed in time of need!</span>
    <span>Sinners, trust in Jesus' name,</span>
    <span>You shall find him still the same.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-110-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But beware of unbelief,</span>
    <span>Think upon the harden'd thief;</span>
    <span>If the gospel you disdain,</span>
    <span>Christ to you will die in vain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-111." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">111.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Woman of Samaria.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">John, iv, 28.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-111-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Jesus, to what didst thou submit,</span>
    <span>To save thy dear-bought flock from hell!</span>
    <span>Like a poor trav'ler see him sit</span>
    <span>Athirst and weary by the well.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-111-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The woman who for water came</span>
    <span>(What great events on small depend!)</span>
    <span>Then learn'd the glory of his name,</span>
    <span>The well of life, the sinner's Friend!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-111-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Taught from her birth to hate the Jews,</span>
    <span>And fill'd with party pride, at first</span>
    <span>Her zeal induced her to refuse</span>
    <span>Water, to quench the Saviour's thirst.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-111-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But soon she knew the gift of God,</span>
    <span>And Jesus, whom she scorn'd before,</span>
    <span>Unask'd, that drink on her bestow'd</span>
    <span>Which whoso tastes shall thirst no more.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-111-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>His words her prejudice removed,</span>
    <span>Her sin she felt, relief she found;</span>
    <span>She saw and heard, believed and loved,</span>
    <span>And ran to tell her neighbours round.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-111-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>O come, this wondrous man behold,</span>
    <span>The promised Saviour! this is he</span>
    <span>Whom ancient prophecies foretold,</span>
    <span>Born from our guilt to set us free,</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-111-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Like her, in ignorance content,</span>
    <span>I worshipp'd long I knew not what;</span>
    <span>Like her, on other things intent,</span>
    <span>I found him when I sought him not.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-111-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>He told me all that e'er I did,</span>
    <span>And told me all was pardon'd too;</span>
    <span>And now, like her, as he has bid,</span>
    <span>I live to point him out to you.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-112." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">112.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Pool of Bethesda.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">John, v, 2-4.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-112-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Beside the gospel pool,</span>
      <span class="i1">Appointed for the poor,</span>
    <span>From year to year my helpless soul</span>
      <span class="i1">Has waited for a cure.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-112-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">How often have I seen</span>
      <span class="i1">The healing waters move,</span>
    <span>And others, round me, stepping in,</span>
      <span class="i1">Their efficacy prove!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-112-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">But my complaints remain:</span>
      <span class="i1">I feel the very same;</span>
    <span>As full of guilt and fear and pain</span>
      <span class="i1">As when at first I came.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-112-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">O would the Lord appear</span>
      <span class="i1">My malady to heal;</span>
    <span>He knows how long I've languish'd here,</span>
      <span class="i1">And what distress I feel.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-112-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">How often have I thought,</span>
      <span class="i1">Why should I longer lie?</span>
    <span>Surely the mercy I have sought</span>
      <span class="i1">Is not for such as I?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-112-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">But whether can I go?</span>
      <span class="i1">There is no other pool</span>
    <span>Where streams of sovereign virtue flow</span>
      <span class="i1">To make a sinner whole.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-112-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Here, then, from day to day,</span>
      <span class="i1">I'll wait and hope and try;</span>
    <span>Can Jesus hear a sinner pray,</span>
      <span class="i1">Yet suffer him to die!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-112-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">No: he is full of grace;</span>
      <span class="i1">He never will permit</span>
    <span>A soul that fain would see his face</span>
      <span class="i1">To perish at his feet.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-113." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">113.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Another.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead"></p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-113-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Here at Bethesda's pool, the poor,</span>
      <span class="i1">The wither'd, halt, and blind,</span>
    <span>With waiting hearts expect a cure,</span>
      <span class="i1">And free admittance find.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-113-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Here streams of wondrous virtue flow,</span>
      <span class="i1">To heal the sin-sick soul,—</span>
    <span>To wash the filthy white as snow,</span>
      <span class="i1">And make the wounded whole.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-113-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The dumb break forth in songs of praise,</span>
      <span class="i1">The blind their sight receive,</span>
    <span>The cripple runs in wisdom's ways,</span>
      <span class="i1">The dead revive and live.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-113-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Restrain'd to no one case or time,</span>
      <span class="i1">These waters always move;</span>
    <span>Sinners in every age and clime</span>
      <span class="i1">Their vital influence prove.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-113-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Yet numbers daily near them lie,</span>
      <span class="i1">Who meet with no relief;</span>
    <span>With life in view they pine and die</span>
      <span class="i1">In hopeless unbelief.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-113-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>'Tis strange they should refuse to bathe.</span>
      <span class="i1">And yet frequent the pool;</span>
    <span>But none can even wish for faith,</span>
      <span class="i1">While love of sin bears rule.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-113-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Satan their consciences has seal'd</span>
      <span class="i1">And stupifies their thought;</span>
    <span>For were they willing to be heal'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">The cure would soon be wrought.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-113-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Do thou, dear Saviour, interpose,</span>
      <span class="i1">Their stubborn wills constrain;</span>
    <span>Or else to them the water flows</span>
      <span class="i1">And grace is preached in vain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-114." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">114.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Disciples at Sea.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">John, vi, 16-21.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-114-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Constrain'd by their Lord to embark,</span>
    <span>And venture without him to sea,</span>
    <span>The season tempestuous and dark,</span>
    <span>How grieved the disciples must be!</span>
    <span>But though he remain'd on the shore,</span>
    <span>He spent the night for them in pray'r;</span>
    <span>They still were as safe as before,</span>
    <span>And equally under his care.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-114-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>They strove, though in vain, for awhile</span>
    <span>The force of the waves to withstand,</span>
    <span>But when they were wearied with toil</span>
    <span>They saw their dear Saviour at hand:</span>
    <span>They gladly received him on board,</span>
    <span>His presence their spirits revived,</span>
    <span>The sea became calm at his word,</span>
    <span>And soon at their port they arrived.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-114-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>We, like the disciples, are toss'd,</span>
    <span>By storms on a perilous deep;</span>
    <span>But cannot be possibly lost,</span>
    <span>For Jesus has charge of the ship:</span>
    <span>Though billows and winds are enraged,</span>
    <span>And threaten to make us their sport;</span>
    <span>This pilot his word has engaged</span>
    <span>To bring us in safety to port.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-114-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>If sometimes we struggle alone,</span>
    <span>And he is withdrawn from our view,</span>
    <span>It makes us more willing to own</span>
    <span>We nothing without him can do:</span>
    <span>Then Satan our hopes would assail,</span>
    <span>But Jesus is still within call,</span>
    <span>And when our poor efforts quite fail</span>
    <span>He comes in good time and does all.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-114-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Yet, Lord, we are ready to shrink</span>
    <span>Unless we thy presence perceive;</span>
    <span>save us, (we cry,) or we sink;</span>
    <span>We would, but we cannot believe!</span>
    <span>The night has been long and severe,</span>
    <span>The winds and the seas are still high,</span>
    <span>Dear Saviour, this moment appear,</span>
    <span>And say to our souls, "It is I!"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-115." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">115.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Will ye also go away?.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">John, vi, 67-69.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-115-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When any turn from Zion's way—</span>
      <span class="i1">Alas! what numbers do!—</span>
    <span>Methinks I hear my Saviour say,</span>
      <span class="i1">"Wilt thou forsake me too?"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-115-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Ah, Lord! with such a heart as mine,</span>
      <span class="i1">Unless thou hold me fast,</span>
    <span>I feel I must, I shall decline,</span>
      <span class="i1">And prove like them at last.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-115-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Yet thou alone hast power, I know,</span>
      <span class="i1">To save a wretch like me;</span>
    <span>To whom, or whither, could I go,</span>
      <span class="i1">If I should turn from thee?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-115-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Beyond a doubt I rest assured</span>
      <span class="i1">Thou art the Christ of God,</span>
    <span>Who hast eternal life secured</span>
      <span class="i1">By promise and by blood.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-115-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The help of men and angels join'd</span>
      <span class="i1">Could never reach my case;</span>
    <span>Nor can I hope relief to find</span>
      <span class="i1">But in thy boundless grace.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-115-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>No voice but thine can give me rest,</span>
      <span class="i1">And bid my fears depart;</span>
    <span>No love but thine can make me bless’d.</span>
      <span class="i1">And satisfy my heart.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-115-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>What anguish has that question stirr'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">If I will also go?</span>
    <span>Yet, Lord, relying on thy word,</span>
      <span class="i1">I humbly answer—No.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-116." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">116.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Resurrection and the Life.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">John, xi, 25.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-116-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"I am," saith Christ, "your glorious head,"</span>
      <span class="i1">(May we attention give,)</span>
    <span>"The resurrection of the dead,</span>
      <span class="i1">The life of all that live.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-116-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"By faith in me the soul receives</span>
      <span class="i1">New life, though dead before;</span>
    <span>And he that in my name believes,</span>
      <span class="i1">Shall live to die no more.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-116-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"The sinner, sleeping in his grave,</span>
      <span class="i1">Shall at my voice awake;</span>
    <span>And when I once begin to save,</span>
      <span class="i1">My work I ne'er forsake."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-116-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Fulfill thy promise, gracious Lord,</span>
      <span class="i1">On us assembled here;</span>
    <span>Put forth thy Spirit with the word,</span>
      <span class="i1">And cause the dead to hear.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-116-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Preserve the power of faith alive</span>
      <span class="i1">In those who love thy name;</span>
    <span>For sin and Satan daily strive</span>
      <span class="i1">To quench the sacred flame.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-116-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thy power and mercy first prevail'd</span>
      <span class="i1">From death to set us free;</span>
    <span>And often since our life had fail'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">If not renew'd by thee.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-116-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>To thee we look, to thee we bow,</span>
      <span class="i1">To thee for help we call;</span>
    <span>Our life and resurrection thou,</span>
      <span class="i1">Our hope, our joy, our all.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-117." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">117.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Weeping Mary.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">John xx, 11-16.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-117-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Mary to her Saviour's tomb</span>
    <span>Hasted at the early dawn;</span>
    <span>Spice she brought, and sweet perfume;</span>
    <span>But the Lord she loved was gone.</span>
    <span>For awhile she weeping stood,</span>
    <span>Struck with sorrow and surprise,</span>
    <span>Shedding tears, a plenteous flood,</span>
    <span>For her heart supplied her eyes.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-117-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Jesus, who is always near,</span>
    <span>Though too often unperceived,</span>
    <span>Came, his drooping child to cheer,</span>
    <span>Kindly asking, "Why she grieved?"</span>
    <span>Though at first she knew him not,</span>
    <span>When he call'd her by her name</span>
    <span>Then her griefs were all forgot,</span>
    <span>For she found he was the same.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-117-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Grief and sighing quickly fled</span>
    <span>When she heard his welcome voice:</span>
    <span>Just before she thought him dead,</span>
    <span>Now he bids her heart rejoice.</span>
    <span>What a change his word can make,</span>
    <span>Turning darkness into day!</span>
    <span>You who weep for Jesu's sake,</span>
    <span>He will wipe your tears away.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-117-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>He who came to comfort her,</span>
    <span>When she thought her all was lost,</span>
    <span>Will for your relief appear,</span>
    <span>Though you now are tempest-toss'd:</span>
    <span>On his word your burden cast,</span>
    <span>On his love your thoughts employ;</span>
    <span>Weeping for awhile may last,</span>
    <span>But the morning brings the joy.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-118." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">118.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Lovest thou me?.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">John, xxi, 16.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-118-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Hark, my soul! it is the Lord;</span>
    <span>'Tis thy (Saviour, hear his word;</span>
    <span>Jesus speaks, and speaks to thee:</span>
    <span>"Say, poor sinner, lov'st thou me?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-118-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"I deliver'd thee when bound,</span>
    <span>And, when bleeding, heal'd thy wound,—</span>
    <span>Sought thee wand ring, set thee right,</span>
    <span>Turn'd thy darkness into light.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-118-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Can a woman's tender care</span>
    <span>Cease towards the child she bare?</span>
    <span>Yes, she may forgetful be,</span>
    <span>Yet will I remember thee.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-118-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Mine is an unchanging love,</span>
    <span>Higher than the heights above,</span>
    <span>Deeper than the depths beneath,</span>
    <span>Free and faithful, strong as death.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-118-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Thou shalt see my glory soon,</span>
    <span>When the work of grace is done,—</span>
    <span>Partner of my throne shalt be,</span>
    <span>Say, poor sinner, lov'st thou me?"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-118-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Lord, it is my chief complaint,</span>
    <span>That my love is weak and faint;</span>
    <span>Yet I love thee and adore,</span>
    <span>Oh for grace to love thee more?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-119." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">119.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Another.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead"></p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-119-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>'Tis a point I long to know,</span>
    <span>Oft it causes anxious thought—</span>
    <span>Do I love the Lord, or no?</span>
    <span>Am I his, or am I not?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-119-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>If I love, why am I thus?</span>
    <span>Why this dull, this lifeless frame?</span>
    <span>Hardly sure can they be worse</span>
    <span>Who have never heard his name!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-119-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Could my heart so hard remain,</span>
    <span>Pray'r a task and burden prove,</span>
    <span>Every trifle give me pain,</span>
    <span>If I knew a Saviour's love?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-119-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When I turn my eyes within,</span>
    <span>All is dark and vain and wild:</span>
    <span>Fill'd with unbelief and sin,</span>
    <span>Can I deem myself a child?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-119-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>If I pray or hear or read,</span>
    <span>Sin is mix'd with all I do;</span>
    <span>You that love the Lord indeed,</span>
    <span>Tell me, is it thus with you?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-119-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Yet I mourn my stubborn will,</span>
    <span>Find my sin a grief and thrall:</span>
    <span>Should I grieve for what I feel,</span>
    <span>If I did not love at all?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-119-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Could I joy his saints to meet,</span>
    <span>Choose the ways I once abhorr'd,</span>
    <span>Find, at times, the promise sweet,</span>
    <span>If I did not love the Lord?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-119-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Lord, decide the doubtful case!</span>
    <span>Thou who art thy people's sun,</span>
    <span>Shine upon thy work of grace,</span>
    <span>If it be indeed begun.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-119-9>
 	<header>
 		<p>IX</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Let me love thee more and more,</span>
    <span>If I love at all, I pray;</span>
    <span>If I have not loved before,</span>
    <span>Help me to begin to-day.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-120." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">120.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Death of Stephen.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Acts, vii, 54-60.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-120-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>As some tall rock amidst the waves</span>
    <span>The fury of the tempest braves,</span>
    <span>While the fierce billows, tossing high,</span>
    <span>Break at its foot, and murm'ring, die:</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-120-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus they who in the Lord confide,</span>
    <span>Though foes assault on every side,</span>
    <span>Cannot be moved or overthrown,</span>
    <span>For Jesus makes their cause his own.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-120-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>So faithful Stephen, undismay'd,</span>
    <span>The malice of the Jews survey'd;</span>
    <span>The holy joy which fill'd his breast,</span>
    <span>A lustre on his face impress'd.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-120-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Behold," he said, "the world of light</span>
    <span>Is open'd to my strengthened sight;</span>
    <span>My glorious Lord appears in view,</span>
    <span>That Jesus whom ye lately slew."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-120-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>With such a friend and witness near,</span>
    <span>No form of death could make him fear;</span>
    <span>Calm, amidst showers of stones, he kneels,</span>
    <span>And only for his murderers feels.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-120-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>May we by faith perceive thee thus,</span>
    <span>Dear Saviour, ever near to us!</span>
    <span>This sight our peace through life shall keep,</span>
    <span>And death be fear'd no more than sleep.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-121." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">121.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Rebel’s surrender to Grace.–Lord, what wilt thou have me to do?.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Acts, ix, 6.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-121-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Lord, thou hast won,—at length I yield,—</span>
    <span>My heart, by mighty grace compell'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">Surrenders all to thee;</span>
    <span>Against thy terrors long I strove,</span>
    <span>But who can stand against thy love?</span>
      <span class="i1">Love conquers even me.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-121-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>All that a wretch could do I tried,—</span>
    <span>Thy patience scorn'd, thy power defied,</span>
      <span class="i1">And trampled on thy laws:</span>
    <span>Scarcely thy martyrs at the stake</span>
    <span>Could stand more steadfast for thy sake</span>
      <span class="i1">Than I in Satan's cause.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-121-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But since thou hast thy love reveal'd,</span>
    <span>And shown my soul a pardon seal'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">I can resist no more:</span>
    <span>Couldst thou for such a sinner bleed?</span>
    <span>Canst thou for such a rebel plead?</span>
      <span class="i1">I wonder and adore!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-121-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>If thou hadst bid thy thunders roll,</span>
    <span>And lightnings flash, to blast my soul,</span>
      <span class="i1">I still had stubborn been;</span>
    <span>But mercy has my heart subdued,—</span>
    <span>A bleeding Saviour I have view'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">And now I hate my sin.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-121-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Now, Lord, I would be thine alone;</span>
    <span>Come, take possession of thine own,</span>
      <span class="i1">For thou hast set me free:</span>
    <span>Released from Satan's hard command,</span>
    <span>See all my powers waiting stand</span>
      <span class="i1">To be employed by thee.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-121-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>My will conform'd to thine would move;</span>
    <span>On thee, my hope, desire, and love,</span>
      <span class="i1">In fix'd attention join;</span>
    <span>My hands, my eyes, my ears, my tongue,</span>
    <span>Have Satan's servants been too long,</span>
      <span class="i1">But now they shall be thine.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-121-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>And can I be the very same</span>
    <span>Who lately durst blaspheme thy name,</span>
      <span class="i1">And on thy gospel tread?</span>
    <span>Surely each one who hears my case</span>
    <span>Will praise thee and confess thy grace</span>
      <span class="i1">Invincible indeed!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-122." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">122.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Peter released from Prison.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Acts, xii, 5-8.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-122-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Fervent persevering prayers</span>
      <span class="i1">Are faith's assured resource;</span>
    <span>Brazen gates and iron bars</span>
      <span class="i1">In vain withstand their force:</span>
    <span>Peter, when in prison cast,</span>
    <span>Though by soldiers kept with care,</span>
    <span>Though the doors were bolted fast,</span>
      <span class="i1">Was soon released by prayer.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-122-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>While he slept, an angel came,</span>
      <span class="i1">And spread a light around,</span>
    <span>Touch'd and call'd him by his name,</span>
      <span class="i1">And raised him from the ground:</span>
    <span>All his chains and fetters burst,</span>
    <span>Every door wide open flew;</span>
    <span>Peter thought he dream'd at first,</span>
      <span class="i1">But found the vision true.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-122-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus the Lord can make a way</span>
      <span class="i1">To bring his saints relief;</span>
    <span>'Tis their part to wait and pray</span>
      <span class="i1">In spite of unbelief:</span>
    <span>He can break through walls of stone,</span>
    <span>Sink the mountain to a plain;</span>
    <span>They to whom his name is known</span>
      <span class="i1">Can never pray in vain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-122-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus in chains of guilt and sin,</span>
      <span class="i1">Poor sinners sleeping lie;</span>
    <span>No alarm is felt within,</span>
      <span class="i1">Although condemn'd to die,</span>
    <span>Till, descending from above,</span>
    <span>(Mercy smiling in his eyes,)</span>
    <span>Jesus, with a voice of love,</span>
      <span class="i1">Awakes, and bids them rise.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-122-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Glad the summons they obey,</span>
      <span class="i1">And liberty desire:</span>
    <span>Straight their fetters melt away</span>
      <span class="i1">Like wax before the fire:</span>
    <span>By the word of Him who died,</span>
    <span>Guilty pris'ners to release,</span>
    <span>Every door flies open wide,</span>
      <span class="i1">And they depart in peace.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-123." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">123.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The trembling Gaoler.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Acts, xvi, 29-31.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-123-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>A believer, free from care,</span>
    <span>May in chains or dungeons sing,</span>
    <span>If the Lord be with him there,</span>
    <span>And be happier than a king:</span>
    <span>Paul and Silas thus confined,</span>
    <span>Though their backs were torn by whips,</span>
    <span>Yet, possessing peace of mind,</span>
    <span>Sung his praise with joyful lips.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-123-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Suddenly the prison shook,</span>
    <span>Open flew the iron doors;</span>
    <span>And the gaoler, terror-struck,</span>
    <span>Now his captives' help implores:</span>
    <span>Trembling at their feet he fell,</span>
    <span>"Tell me, sirs, what must I do</span>
    <span>To be saved from guilt and hell?</span>
    <span>None can tell me this but you."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-123-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Look to Jesus," they replied,</span>
    <span>"If on him thou canst believe,</span>
    <span>By the death which he has died,</span>
    <span>Thou salvation shalt receive."</span>
    <span>While the living word he heard,</span>
    <span>Faith sprung up within his heart,</span>
    <span>And released from all he fear'd,</span>
    <span>In their joy his soul had part.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-123-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Sinners, Christ is still the same;</span>
    <span>O that you could likewise fear!</span>
    <span>Then the mention of his name</span>
    <span>Would be music to your ear:</span>
    <span>Jesus rescues Satan's slaves,</span>
    <span>His dear wounds still plead, "Forgive!"</span>
    <span>Jesus to the utmost saves;</span>
    <span>Sinners, look to him and live.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-124." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">124.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Exorcists.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Acts, xix, 13-16.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-124-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When the apostle wonders wrought,</span>
    <span>And heal'd the sick in Jesu's name,</span>
    <span>The sons of Sceva vainly thought</span>
    <span>That they had power to do the same.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-124-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>On one possess'd they tried their art,</span>
    <span>And naming Jesus preach'd by Paul,</span>
    <span>They charged the spirit to depart,</span>
    <span>Expecting he'd obey their call.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-124-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The spirit answer'd with a mock,</span>
    <span>"Jesus I know, and Paul I know;</span>
    <span>I must have gone if Paul had spoke;</span>
    <span>But who are ye that bid me go?"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-124-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>With fury then the man he fill'd,</span>
    <span>Who on the poor pretenders flew;</span>
    <span>Naked and wounded, almost kill'd,</span>
    <span>They fled in all the people's view.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-124-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Jesus! that name pronounced by faith,</span>
    <span>Is full of wonder-working power:</span>
    <span>It conquers Satan, sin, and death,</span>
    <span>And cheers in trouble's darkest hour.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-124-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But they who are not born again</span>
    <span>Know nothing of it but the sound;</span>
    <span>They do but take his name in vain</span>
    <span>When most their zeal and pains abound.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-124-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Satan their vain attempts derides,</span>
    <span>Whether they talk or pray or preach;</span>
    <span>Long as the love of sin abides,</span>
    <span>His power is safe beyond their reach.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-124-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But you, believers, may rejoice,</span>
    <span>Satan well knows your mighty Friend;</span>
    <span>He trembles at your Saviour's voice,</span>
    <span>And owns he cannot gain his end.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-125." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">125.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Paul’s Voyage.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Acts, xxvii.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-125-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>If Paul in Cesar's court must stand,</span>
      <span class="i1">He need not fear the sea,</span>
    <span>Secured from harm on every hand</span>
      <span class="i1">By the divine decree.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-125-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Although the ship in which he sail'd</span>
      <span class="i1">By dreadful storms was toss'd,</span>
    <span>The promise over all prevailed,</span>
      <span class="i1">And not a life was lost.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-125-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Jesus! the God whom Paul adored,</span>
      <span class="i1">Who saves in time of need;</span>
    <span>Was then confess'd by all on board,</span>
      <span class="i1">A present help indeed!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-125-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Though neither sun nor stars were seen,</span>
      <span class="i1">Paul knew the Lord was near;</span>
    <span>And faith preserved his soul serene,</span>
      <span class="i1">When others shook for fear.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-125-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Believers thus are toss'd about,</span>
      <span class="i1">On life's tempestuous main;</span>
    <span>But grace assures beyond a doubt,</span>
      <span class="i1">They shall their port attain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-125-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>They must, they shall appear one day</span>
      <span class="i1">Before their Saviour's throne;</span>
    <span>The storms they meet with by the way</span>
      <span class="i1">But make his power known.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-125-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Their passage lies across the brink</span>
      <span class="i1">Of many a threat'ning wave;</span>
    <span>The world expects to see them sink,</span>
      <span class="i1">But Jesus lives to save.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-125-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Lord, though we are but feeble worms,</span>
      <span class="i1">Yet since thy word is past,</span>
    <span>We'll venture through a thousand storms,</span>
      <span class="i1">To see thy face at last.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-126." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">126.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Good that I would do, I do not.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Rom. vii, 19.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-126-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">I would, but cannot sing,—</span>
      <span class="i1">Guilt has untuned my voice,</span>
    <span>The serpent sin's envenom'd sting</span>
      <span class="i1">Has poison'd all my joys.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-126-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">I know the Lord is nigh,</span>
      <span class="i1">And would, but cannot pray;</span>
    <span>For Satan meets me when I try,</span>
      <span class="i1">And frights my soul away.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-126-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">I would, but can't repent,</span>
      <span class="i1">Though I endeavour oft;</span>
    <span>This stony heart can ne'er relent</span>
      <span class="i1">Till Jesus make it soft.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-126-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">I would, but cannot love,</span>
      <span class="i1">Though woo'd by love divine:</span>
    <span>No arguments have power to move</span>
      <span class="i1">A soul so base as mine.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-126-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">I would, but cannot rest</span>
      <span class="i1">In God's most holy will;</span>
    <span>I know what he appoints is best,</span>
      <span class="i1">Yet murmur at it still.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-126-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">O could I but believe!</span>
      <span class="i1">Then all would easy be;</span>
    <span>I would, but cannot—Lord, relieve;</span>
      <span class="i1">My help must come from thee!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-126-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">But if indeed I would,</span>
      <span class="i1">Though I can nothing do;</span>
    <span>Yet the desire is something good,</span>
      <span class="i1">For which my praise is due.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-126-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">By nature prone to ill,</span>
      <span class="i1">Till thine appointed hour,</span>
