    <span>I was as destitute of will,</span>
      <span class="i1">As now I am of power.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-126-9>
 	<header>
 		<p>IX</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Wilt thou not crown at length</span>
      <span class="i1">The work thou hast begun,</span>
    <span>And with a will afford me strength</span>
      <span class="i1">In all thy ways to run?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-127." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">127.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Salvation drawing nearer.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Rom. xiii, 11, 12.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-127-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Darkness overspreads us here,</span>
    <span>But the night wears fast away;</span>
    <span>Jacob's Star will soon appear,</span>
    <span>Leading on eternal day!</span>
    <span>Now 'tis time to rouse from sleep,</span>
    <span>Trim our lamps, and stand prepared,</span>
    <span>For our Lord strict watch to keep,</span>
    <span>Lest he find us off our guard.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-127-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Let his people courage take,</span>
    <span>Bear with a submissive mind</span>
    <span>All they suffer for his sake,—</span>
    <span>Rich amends they soon will find:</span>
    <span>He will wipe away their tears,</span>
    <span>Near himself appoint their lot;</span>
    <span>All their sorrows, pains, and fears,</span>
    <span>Quickly then will be forgot.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-127-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Though already saved by grace,</span>
    <span>From the hour we first believed;</span>
    <span>Yet while sin and war have place,</span>
    <span>We have but a part received:</span>
    <span>Still we for salvation wait,</span>
    <span>Every hour it nearer comes!</span>
    <span>Death will break the prison gate</span>
    <span>And admit us to our homes.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-127-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Sinners, what can you expect,</span>
    <span>You who now the Saviour dare,</span>
    <span>Break his laws, his grace reject?</span>
    <span>You must stand before his bar!</span>
    <span>Tremble, lest he say, depart!</span>
    <span>Oh! the horrors of that sound!</span>
    <span>Lord, make every careless heart</span>
    <span>Seek thee while thou may'st be found.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-128." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">128.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">That Rock was Christ.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">1 Cor. x, 4.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-128-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When Isr'el's tribes were parch'd with thirst,</span>
    <span>Forth from the rock the waters burst,</span>
    <span>And all their future journey through</span>
    <span>Yielded them drink and gospel too?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-128-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>In Moses' rod a type they saw</span>
    <span>Of His severe and fiery law;</span>
    <span>The smitten rock prefigured Him</span>
    <span>From whose pierced side all blessings stream.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-128-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But ah! the types were all too faint</span>
    <span>His sorrows or His worth to paint;</span>
    <span>Slight was the stroke of Moses' rod,</span>
    <span>But He endured the wrath of God.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-128-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Their outward rock could feel no pain,</span>
    <span>But ours was wounded, torn, and slain;</span>
    <span>The rock gave but a wat'ry flood,</span>
    <span>But Jesus pour'd forth streams of blood.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-128-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The earth is like their wilderness,</span>
    <span>A land of drought and sore distress,</span>
    <span>Without one stream from pole to pole</span>
    <span>To satify a thirsty soul.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-128-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But let the Saviour's praise resound;</span>
    <span>In him refreshing streams are found,</span>
    <span>Which pardon, strength, and comfort give,</span>
    <span>And thirsty sinners drink and live.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-129." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">129.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">My Grace is sufficient for thee.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">2 Cor. xii, 9.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-129-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Oppress'd with unbelief and sin,</span>
    <span>Fightings without, and fears within,</span>
    <span>While earth and hell, with force combined.</span>
    <span>Assault and terrify my mind;</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-129-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>What strength have I against such foes,</span>
    <span>Such hosts and legions to oppose?</span>
    <span>Alas! I tremble, faint, and fall;</span>
    <span>Lord, save me, or I give up all.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-129-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus sorely press'd, I sought the Lord,</span>
    <span>To give me some sweet cheering word;</span>
    <span>Again I sought, and yet again;</span>
    <span>I waited long, but not in vain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-129-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Oh! 'twas a cheering word indeed!</span>
    <span>Exactly suited to my need;</span>
    <span>"Sufficient for thee is my grace,</span>
    <span>Thy weakness my great power displays."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-129-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Now I despond and mourn no more,</span>
    <span>I welcome all I fear'd before:</span>
    <span>Though weak, I'm strong, though troubled, blest,</span>
    <span>For Christ's own power shall on me rest.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-129-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>My grace would soon exhausted be,</span>
    <span>But his is boundless as the sea;</span>
    <span>Then let me boast with holy Paul,</span>
    <span>That I am nothing, Christ is all.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-130." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">130.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Inward Warfare.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Gal. v, 17.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-130-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Strange and mysterious is my life,</span>
    <span>What opposites I feel within!</span>
    <span>A stable peace, a constant strife;</span>
    <span>The rule of grace, the power of sin:</span>
    <span>Too often I am captive led,</span>
    <span>Yet daily triumph in my Head.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-130-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>I prize the privilege of prayer,</span>
    <span>But oh! what backwardness to pray!</span>
    <span>Though on the Lord I cast my care,</span>
    <span>I feel its burden every day;</span>
    <span>I seek his will in all I do,</span>
    <span>Yet find my own is working too.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-130-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>I call the promises my own,</span>
    <span>And prize them more than mines of gold;</span>
    <span>Yet though their sweetness I have known,</span>
    <span>They leave me unimpress'd and cold:</span>
    <span>One hour upon the truth I feed,</span>
    <span>The next I know not what to read.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-130-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>I love the holy day of rest,</span>
    <span>When Jesus meets his gather'd saints;</span>
    <span>Sweet day, of all the week the best!</span>
    <span>For its return my spirit pants:</span>
    <span>Yet often through my unbelief,</span>
    <span>It proves a day of guilt and grief.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-130-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>While on the Saviour I rely,</span>
    <span>I know my foes shall lose their aim;</span>
    <span>And therefore dare their power defy,</span>
    <span>Assured of conquest through his name:</span>
    <span>But soon my confidence is slain,</span>
    <span>And all my fears return again.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-130-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus diff'rent powers within me strive,</span>
    <span>And grace and sin by turns prevail;</span>
    <span>I grieve, rejoice, decline, revive,</span>
    <span>And vict'ry hangs in doubtful scale:</span>
    <span>But Jesus has his promise past,</span>
    <span>That grace shall overcome at last.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-131." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">131.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Contentment.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Phil, iv, 11.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-131-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Fierce passions discompose the mind,</span>
      <span class="i1">As tempests vex the sea;</span>
    <span>But calm content and peace we find</span>
      <span class="i1">When, Lord, we turn to thee.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-131-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>In vain by reason and by rule</span>
      <span class="i1">We try to bend the will;</span>
    <span>For none but in the Saviour's school</span>
      <span class="i1">Can learn the heavenly skill.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-131-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Since at his feet my soul has sat,</span>
      <span class="i1">His gracious words to hear;</span>
    <span>Contented with my present state,</span>
      <span class="i1">I cast on him my care.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-131-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Art thou a sinner, soul?" he said,</span>
      <span class="i1">"Then how canst thou complain?</span>
    <span>How light thy troubles here, if weigh'd</span>
      <span class="i1">With everlasting pain?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-131-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>If thou of murm'ring wouldst be cured,</span>
      <span class="i1">Compare thy griefs with mine;</span>
    <span>Think what my love for thee endured,</span>
      <span class="i1">And thou wilt not repine.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-131-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>'Tis I appoint thy daily lot,</span>
      <span class="i1">And I do all things well:</span>
    <span>Thou soon shalt leave this wretched spot,</span>
      <span class="i1">And rise with me to dwell.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-131-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>In life, my grace shall strength supply</span>
      <span class="i1">Proportion'd to thy day;</span>
    <span>At death, thou still shalt find me nigh,</span>
      <span class="i1">To wipe thy tears away."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-131-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus I, who once my wretched days</span>
      <span class="i1">In vain repinings spent,</span>
    <span>Taught in my Saviour's school of grace,</span>
      <span class="i1">Have learn'd to be content.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-132." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">132.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Old Testament Gospel.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Heb. iv, 2.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-132-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Isr'el, in ancient days,</span>
      <span class="i1">Not only had a view</span>
      <span class="i1">Of Sinai in a blaze,</span>
      <span class="i1">But learn'd the gospel too:</span>
    <span>The types and figures were a glass</span>
    <span>In which they saw a Saviour's face.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-132-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">The paschal sacrifice,</span>
      <span class="i1">And blood be-sprinkled door,</span>
      <span class="i1">Seen with enlighten'd eyes,</span>
      <span class="i1">And once applied with power,</span>
    <span>Would teach the need of other blood</span>
    <span>To reconcile an angry God.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-132-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">The Lamb, the Dove, set forth</span>
      <span class="i1">His perfect innocence,</span>
      <span class="i1">Whose blood of matchless worth</span>
      <span class="i1">Should be the soul's defence:</span>
    <span>For He who can for sin atone</span>
    <span>Must have no failings of his own.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-132-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">The scape-goat on his head</span>
      <span class="i1">The people's trespass bore,</span>
      <span class="i1">And to the desert led,</span>
      <span class="i1">Was to be seen no more:</span>
    <span>In him our Surety seem'd to say,</span>
    <span>"Behold! I bear your sins away."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-132-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Dipt in his fellow's blood,</span>
      <span class="i1">The living bird went free;</span>
      <span class="i1">The type, well understood,</span>
      <span class="i1">Express'd the sinner's plea;</span>
    <span>Described a guilty soul enlarged,</span>
    <span>And by a Saviour's death discharged.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-132-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Jesus, I love to trace</span>
      <span class="i1">Throughout the sacred page</span>
      <span class="i1">The footsteps of thy grace,</span>
      <span class="i1">The same in every age!</span>
    <span>O grant that I may faithful be</span>
    <span>To clearer light vouchsafed to me!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-133." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">133.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The word quick and powerful.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Heb. iv, 12, 13.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-133-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">The word of Christ our Lord,</span>
      <span class="i1">With whom we have to do,</span>
    <span>Is sharper than a two-edged sword</span>
      <span class="i1">To pierce the sinner through!</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-133-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Swift as the lightning's blaze</span>
      <span class="i1">When awful thunders roll,</span>
    <span>It fills the conscience with amaze,</span>
      <span class="i1">And penetrates the soul.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-133-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">No heart can be conceal'd</span>
      <span class="i1">From his all-piercing eyes:</span>
    <span>Each thought and purpose stands reveal'd,</span>
      <span class="i1">Naked without disguise.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-133-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">He sees his people's fears,</span>
      <span class="i1">He notes their mournful cry;</span>
    <span>He counts their sighs and falling tears,</span>
      <span class="i1">And helps them from on high.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-133-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Though feeble is their good,</span>
      <span class="i1">It has its kind regard;</span>
    <span>Yea, all they would do, if they could,</span>
      <span class="i1">Shall find a sure reward.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-133-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">He sees the wicked too,</span>
      <span class="i1">And will repay them soon,</span>
    <span>For all the evil deeds they do,</span>
      <span class="i1">And all they would have done.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-133-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
      <span class="i1">Since all our secret ways</span>
      <span class="i1">Are mark'd and known by thee,</span>
    <span>Afford us, Lord, thy light of grace,</span>
      <span class="i1">That we ourselves may see.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-134." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">134.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Looking unto Jesus.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Heb. xii, 2.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-134-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>By various maxims, forms, and rules,</span>
    <span>That pass for wisdom in the schools,</span>
    <span>I strove my passion to restrain;</span>
    <span>But all my efforts proved in vain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-134-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>But since the Saviour I have known,</span>
    <span>My rules are all reduced to one,</span>
    <span>To keep my Lord by faith in view;</span>
    <span>This strength supplies and motives too.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-134-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>I see him lead a suff'ring life,</span>
    <span>Patient amidst reproach and strife;</span>
    <span>And from his pattern courage take</span>
    <span>To bear and suffer for his sake.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-134-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Upon the cross I see him bleed,</span>
    <span>And by the sight from guilt am freed;</span>
    <span>This sight destroys the life of sin,</span>
    <span>And quickens heav'nly life within.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-134-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>To look to Jesus as he rose,</span>
    <span>Confirms my faith, disarms my foes;</span>
    <span>Satan I shame and overcome,</span>
    <span>By pointing to my Saviour's tomb.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-134-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Exalted on his glorious throne,</span>
    <span>I see him make my cause his own;</span>
    <span>Then all my anxious cares subside,</span>
    <span>For Jesus lives, and will provide.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-134-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>I see him look with pity down,</span>
    <span>And hold in view the conq'ror's crown.</span>
    <span>If press'd with griefs and cares before,</span>
    <span>My soul revives, nor asks for more.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-134-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>By faith I see the hour at hand,</span>
    <span>When in his presence I shall stand;</span>
    <span>Then it will be my endless bliss</span>
    <span>To see him where and as he is.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-135." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">135.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Love Tokens.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Heb. xii, 5-11.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-135-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Afflictions do not come alone,</span>
      <span class="i1">A voice attends the rod;</span>
    <span>By both he to his saints is known,</span>
      <span class="i1">A Father and a God.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-135-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Let not my children slight the stroke</span>
      <span class="i1">I for chastisement send,</span>
    <span>Nor faint beneath my kind rebuke,</span>
      <span class="i1">For still I am their Friend.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-135-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"The wicked I perhaps may leave</span>
      <span class="i1">Awhile, and not reprove;</span>
    <span>But all the children I receive,</span>
      <span class="i1">I scourge, because I love.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-135-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"If therefore you were left without</span>
      <span class="i1">This needful discipline,</span>
    <span>You might with cause admit a doubt</span>
      <span class="i1">If you indeed were mine.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-135-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Shall earthly parents then expect</span>
      <span class="i1">Their children to submit?</span>
    <span>And will not you, when I correct,</span>
      <span class="i1">Be humbled at my feet?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-135-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"To please themselves they oft chastise,</span>
      <span class="i1">And put their sons to pain;</span>
    <span>But you are precious in my eyes,</span>
      <span class="i1">And shall not smart in vain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-135-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"I see your hearts at present fill'd</span>
      <span class="i1">With grief and deep distress;</span>
    <span>But soon these bitter seeds shall yield</span>
      <span class="i1">The fruits of righteousness."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-135-8>
 	<header>
 		<p>VIII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Break through the clouds, dear Lord, and shine!</span>
      <span class="i1">Let us perceive thee nigh!</span>
    <span>And to each mourning child of thine</span>
      <span class="i1">These gracious words apply.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-136." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">136.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Ephesus.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Rev. ii, 1-7.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-136-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus saith the Lord to Ephesus,</span>
    <span>And thus he speaks to some of us,—</span>
    <span>"Amidst my churches, lo, I stand,</span>
    <span>And hold the pastors in my hand.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-136-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Thy works to me are fully known,</span>
    <span>Thy patience and thy toil I own;</span>
    <span>Thy views of gospel truth are clear,</span>
    <span>Nor canst thou other doctrine bear.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-136-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Yet I must blame while I approve;</span>
    <span>Where is thy first, thy fervent love?</span>
    <span>Dost thou forget my love to thee,</span>
    <span>That thine is grown so faint to me?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-136-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Recall to mind the happy days</span>
    <span>When thou wast fill'd with joy and praise;</span>
    <span>Repent—thy former works renew—</span>
    <span>Then I'll restore thy comforts too.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-136-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Return at once, when I reprove,</span>
    <span>Lest I thy candlestick remove;</span>
    <span>And thou too late thy loss lament:</span>
    <span>I warn before I strike—Repent."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-136-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Hearken to what the Spirit saith,</span>
    <span>"To him that overcomes by faith,</span>
    <span>The fruit of life's unfading tree</span>
    <span>In paradise his food shall be."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-137." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">137.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Smyrna.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Rev. ii, 11.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-137-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The message first to Smyrna sent,</span>
      <span class="i1">A message full of grace,</span>
    <span>To all the Saviour's flock is meant</span>
      <span class="i1">In every age and place.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-137-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus to his church, his chosen bride,</span>
      <span class="i1">Saith the great First and Last,</span>
    <span>Who ever lives, though once he died,</span>
      <span class="i1">"Hold thy profession fast.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-137-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Thy works and sorrow well I know,</span>
      <span class="i1">Perform'd and borne for me;</span>
    <span>Poor though thou art, despised and low,</span>
      <span class="i1">Yet who is rich like thee?</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-137-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"I know thy foes, and what they say,</span>
      <span class="i1">How long they have blasphemed;</span>
    <span>The synagogue of Satan they,</span>
      <span class="i1">Though they would Jews be deem'd.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-137-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Though Satan for a season rage,</span>
      <span class="i1">And prisons be your lot,</span>
    <span>I am your Friend, and I engage</span>
      <span class="i1">You shall not be forgot.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-137-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Be faithful unto death, nor fear</span>
      <span class="i1">A few short days of strife;</span>
    <span>Behold! the prize you soon shall wear,</span>
      <span class="i1">A crown of endless life!"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-137-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Hear what the Holy Spirit saith,</span>
      <span class="i1">Of all who overcome;</span>
    <span>"They shall escape the second death,</span>
      <span class="i1">The sinner's awful doom!"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-138." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">138.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Sardis.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Cowper</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Rev. in, 1-6.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-138-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Write to Sardis," (saith the Lord,)</span>
      <span class="i1">And write what he declares,</span>
    <span>He whose Spirit and whose word</span>
      <span class="i1">Upholds the seven stars:</span>
    <span>"All thy works and ways I search,</span>
    <span>Find thy zeal and love decay'd;</span>
    <span>Thou art call'd a living church,</span>
      <span class="i1">But thou art cold and dead.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-138-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Watch, remember, seek, and strive,</span>
      <span class="i1">Exert thy former pains:</span>
    <span>Let thy timely care revive,</span>
      <span class="i1">And strengthen what remains:</span>
    <span>Cleanse thine heart, thy works amend,</span>
    <span>Former times to mind recall,</span>
    <span>Lest my sudden stroke descend,</span>
      <span class="i1">And smite thee once for all.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-138-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Yet I number now in thee</span>
      <span class="i1">A few that are upright;</span>
    <span>These my Father's face shall see,</span>
      <span class="i1">And walk with me in white:</span>
    <span>When in judgment I appear,</span>
    <span>They for mine shall be confess'd,</span>
    <span>Let my faithful servants hear,</span>
      <span class="i1">And woe be to the rest!"</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-139." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">139.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Philadelphia.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Rev. iii, 7-13.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-139-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus saith the Holy One and true,</span>
    <span>To his beloved faithful few,</span>
    <span>"Of heaven and hell I hold the keys,</span>
    <span>To shut or open as I please.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-139-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"I know thy works, and I approve,</span>
    <span>Though small thy strength, sincere thy love;</span>
    <span>Go on, my word and name to own,</span>
    <span>For none shall rob thee of thy crown.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-139-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Before thee see my mercy's door</span>
    <span>Stands open wide to shut no more;</span>
    <span>Fear not temptation's fiery day,</span>
    <span>For I will be thy strength and stay.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-139-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Thou hast my promise, hold it fast,</span>
    <span>The trying hour will soon be past;</span>
    <span>Rejoice, for lo! I quickly come</span>
    <span>To take thee to my heav'nly home.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-139-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"A pillar there no more to move,</span>
    <span>Inscribed with all my names of love,</span>
    <span>A monument of mighty grace,</span>
    <span>Thou shalt for ever have a place."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-139-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Such is the conqueror's reward,</span>
    <span>Prepared and promised by the Lord!</span>
    <span>Let him that hath the ear of faith,</span>
    <span>Attend to what the Spirit saith.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-140." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">140.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">Laodicea.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Rev. iii, 14-20.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-140-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Hear what the Lord, the great Amen,</span>
    <span>The true and faithful Witness, says;</span>
    <span>He form'd the vast creation's plan,</span>
    <span>And searches all our hearts and ways.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-140-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>To some he speaks as once of old,</span>
    <span>"I know thee, thy profession's vain;</span>
    <span>Since thou art neither hot nor cold.,</span>
    <span>I'll spit thee from me with disdain.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-140-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Thou boasted, 'I am wise and rich,</span>
    <span>Increased in goods and nothing need;'</span>
    <span>And dost not know thou art a wretch,</span>
    <span>Naked and poor and blind and dead.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-140-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Yet while I thus rebuke I love,</span>
    <span>My message is in mercy sent;</span>
    <span>That thou may'st my compassion prove,</span>
    <span>I can forgive if thou repent.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-140-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Wouldst thou be truly rich and wise!</span>
    <span>Come, buy my gold in fire well tried,</span>
    <span>My ointment to anoint thine eyes,</span>
    <span>My robe thy nakedness to hide.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-140-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"See, at thy door I stand and knock!</span>
    <span>Poor sinner, shall I wait in vain?</span>
    <span>Quickly thy stubborn heart unlock,</span>
    <span>That I may enter with my train.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-140-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>"Thou canst not entertain a king,</span>
    <span>Unworthy thou of such a guest!</span>
    <span>But I my own provisions bring,</span>
    <span>To make thy soul a heavenly feast."</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="hymn-1-141." epub:type="z3998:hymn">
  <header>
  <hgroup>
    <h3 epub:type="ordinal">141.</h3>
    <p epub:type="title">The Little Book.</p>
  </hgroup>
  <p epub:type="z3998:contributors">By Newton</p>
  <p epub:type="bridgehead">Rev. x.</p>
  </header>
<section id="stanza-1-141-1>
 	<header>
 		<p>I</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When the beloved disciple took</span>
    <span>The angel's little open book,</span>
    <span>Which by the Lord's command he eat,</span>
    <span>It tasted bitter after sweet.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-141-2>
 	<header>
 		<p>II</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>Thus when the gospel is embraced,</span>
    <span>At first 'tis sweeter to the taste</span>
    <span>Than honey or the honey-comb,</span>
    <span>But there's a bitterness to come.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-141-3>
 	<header>
 		<p>III</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>What sweetness does the promise yield,</span>
    <span>When by the Spirit's power seal'd!</span>
    <span>The longing soul is fill'd with good,</span>
    <span>Nor feels a wish for other food.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-141-4>
 	<header>
 		<p>IV</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>By these inviting tastes allured,</span>
    <span>We pass to what must be endured;</span>
    <span>For soon we find it is decreed,</span>
    <span>That bitter must to sweet succeed.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-141-5>
 	<header>
 		<p>V</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When sin revives and shows its power,</span>
    <span>When Satan threatens to devour,</span>
    <span>When God afflicts, and men revile,</span>
    <span>We draw our steps with pain and toil.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-141-6>
 	<header>
 		<p>VI</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>When thus deserted, tempest-toss'd,</span>
    <span>The sense of former sweetness lost,</span>
    <span>We tremble lest we were deceived</span>
    <span>In thinking that we once believed.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
<section id="stanza-1-141-7>
 	<header>
 		<p>VII</p>
 	</header>
 	<p>
    <span>The Lord first makes the sweetness known,</span>
    <span>To win and fix us for his own;</span>
    <span>And though we now some bitter meet,</span>
    <span>We hope for everlasting sweet.</span>
 	</p>
 	</section>
</section>
</body>
</html>
